The Five Conditions for the Obligation to Perform Hajj
Listing and explaining the five conditions for the obligation to perform Hajj with their proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for the obligation to perform Hajj (wujub al-ada) and identify the Quranic and Hadith proofs for each condition.

Core Idea
Hajj is obligatory only when five conditions are met; absence of any postpones performance.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah lists the five conditions that must be present for the obligation to perform Hajj immediately. The author distinguishes between the obligation itself (wujub al-asl) and the obligation to perform (wujub al-ada). Understanding these conditions is crucial for knowing when Hajj becomes a binding duty on a Muslim. The passage provides proofs from the Quran and Sunnah for each condition, and addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding the requirement of a mahram for women.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between obligation and performance
Recognize that the five conditions are for wujub al-ada (immediate performance), not for the Hajj being obligatory in principle (wujub al-asl). If a condition is missing, the Hajj remains a debt but may be delayed.
The text says 'ala al-ashahh' (according to the most correct view), indicating this distinction is established.
2
Identify the five conditions
List the five conditions: sound body, removal of physical hindrance, safe road, woman not in iddah, presence of a mahram for women. Note that conditions 1-3 apply to both men and women, while 4-5 are specific to women.
The mahram condition includes relatives through lineage, fosterage (rada'), affinity (musahara), or husband.
3
Analyze the proofs for each condition
For health: Quran 48:17 and 3:97. For hindrance and road safety: Hadith from Abu Umamah. For iddah: derived from the general ruling that a woman in iddah must stay home. For mahram: Hadith from Abu Sa'id and Dar Qutni.
The hadith on mahram uses 'la yahillu' (not lawful), which indicates prohibition, not just recommendation.
4
Examine the mahram dispute
The Hanafi school insists on a mahram for a woman's Hajj obligation. The Maliki school and some Shafi'i views allow travel without mahram if the route is safe and she is with trustworthy women. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf.
The Hanafi response emphasizes the literal prohibition in the hadith and the necessity of protection.
5
Apply the conditions to scenarios
Practice applying the conditions: e.g., a healthy man with safe route is obligated; a woman without mahram is not obligated until she obtains one; a person in prison is not obligated due to physical hindrance.
The condition of 'ghalabat al-salamah' (preponderance of safety) for land and sea travel means safety does not have to be absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢ بفرضية الحج لمن اسلم بدار الحرب او الكون بدار الاسلام .
(١٢٢٩) وشروط وجوب الاداء خمسة على الاصح صحة البدن وزوال المانع الحسّى عن الذهاب للحج وامن الطريق وعدم قيام العدة (١٢٣٠) و خروج محرم ولو من رضاع او مصاهرة (١٢٣١) مسلم مامون عاقل بالغ او زوج (١٢٣٢) و في سفر البر و البحر اعتبار غلبة السلامة
الاسلام میں ہونا۔ تشریح : اگر دارالحرب میں مسلمان ہوا تو وہاں حج فرض ہے اس کے جاننے کے اسباب نہیں ہیں، اس لئے اس کو علم ہو کہ حج فرض ہے تب فرض ہوگا اور نہ نہیں ۔ اور اگر دار الاسلام میں ہے تو یہاں علم دین کا چرچاہے اس لئے دارالاسلام میں ہونا ہی حج فرض ہونے کے لئے کافی ہے، اگر اس کو اس کا علم نہیں ہے تو یہ اس کی غفلت ہے۔
ترجمه : (١٢٢٩) صحیح مذہب میں حج کے وجوب ادا کی پانچ شرطیں ہیں: تشریح : یہ پانچ شرطیں پائی جائیں تو حج ادا کرنا فرض ہوگا، اور ان میں سے ایک بھی نہ ہو تو ادا کرنا فرض نہیں ہوگا، بلکہ فرض ہونے کے باوجود مؤخر کرنے کی گنجائش ہوگی ، اور اگر زندگی بھر اس کی شرط پوری نہیں ہوئی تو ادا کرنا فرض نہیں ہوگا اس لئے حج ادا کرنے کی وصیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
وجوب ادا کی پانچ شرطیں ایک نظر میں ..... بدن کا صحیح ہونا۔
حج میں جانے سے مانع حسی کا زائل ہونا
...... راستہ امن والا ہو۔
عورت کے لئے عدت کے دن کا نہ ہونا۔
محرم کا ساتھ چلنا۔
ہر ایک کی دلیل یہ ہے۔
[1] تندرست ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ليـس عـلـى الاعمى حرج ولا على الاعرج حرج و لا على المريض حرج ۔ ( آیت ۱۷، سورۃ الفتح ۴۸ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ معذور پر کوئی حرج نہیں ہے (۲) یہ آیت بھی اس کی دلیل ہے کہ بیت اللہ تک پہونچنے کی قدرت ہو تب حج فرج ہوگا۔ ولله على الناس حج البيت من استطاع اليه سبيلا . ( آیت ۹۷ سوره آل عمران ۳)
[۲] حسی مانع نہ ہو [۳] اور راستہ مامون ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابی امامة عن النبي الله قال من لم يحبسه مرض او حاجة ظاهرة او سلطان جائر ولم يحج فليمت ان شاء يهوديا او نصرانيا ۔(سنن امکان الحج حج رابع ص ۵۴۶ نمبر ۸۶۶۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ظالم بادشاہ نہ روکے اس سے پتہ چلا بھسی مانع نہ ہو۔
[۴] عورت کو عدت کے زمانے میں گھر میں رہنا ضروری ہے، اس لئے اگر جج کے زمانے میں عورت عدت گزار رہی ہو تو اس پر حج ادا کرنا فرض نہیں ہے۔
[۵] عورت کے ساتھ ذی رحم محرم نکلے چاہے رضاعت سے ہو، چاہے سسرالی رشتے سے ہو۔ تشریح : عورت کے ساتھ ذی رحم محرم جاسکتا ہو تب ہی اس پر حج ادا کرنا فرض ہوگا۔ یہ ذی رحم محرم چار قسم کے ہو سکتے ہیں [1] نسبی رشتے سے ہو جیسے باپ اور بھائی ۔ [۲] دودھ پینے کی وجہ سے ذی رحم محرم بنا ہو، جیسے رضاعی بھائی رضاعی باپ ۔[۳] نکاح کی وجہ سے ذی رحم محرم بنا ہو ، جیسے سر، دماد، نکاح کرنے کی وجہ سے ان لوگوں سے ہمیشہ ہمیش نکاح کرنا حرام ہے [۴] یا نکاح کی وجہ سے شوہر بنا ہو۔
[۵] اس حدیث میں نبی ، رضاعی ، اور مصاہرت کی وجہ سے ذی رحم محرم ہونے کا تذکرہ ہے، اور یہ بھی ہے کہ یہ ذی رحم محرم ہوم ہو تو حج کا سفر کر سکتی ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ عن ابی سعید قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا يحل لامرأة تومن بالله واليوم الآخر ان تسافر سفرا فوق ثلثة ايام فصاعدا الا و معها ابوها او اخوها او زوجها او ابنها او ذو محرم منها . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في المرأة تج بغیر محرم ص ۲۴۹نمبر ۱۷۲۶ر مسلم شریف ، باب سفر المرأة مع محرم الى حج وغیرہ ص ۲۳۲ نمبر ۱۳۴۰) (۲) دار قطنی میں ہے عن ابی امامۃ قال سمعت رسول الله الا الله يقول لا تسافر امرأة سفرا ثلاثة ايام او تحج الا و معها زوجها. (دار قطنی، کتاب الحج ج ثانی ص ۱۹۹ نمبر ۲۴۱۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورت کے ساتھ محرم ہوتب حج فرض ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بغیر محرم کے تین دن سے زیادہ کا سفر کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ لغت محرم : جس سے ہمیشہ کے لئے نکاح کرنا حرام ہو اس کو محرم کہتے ہیں۔ رضاع: دودھ پینے کی وجہ سے ذی رحم محرم بن جائے ، جیسے کسی عورت کا دودھ پیا تو وہ ماں بن گئی اور اس کا شوہر باپ بن گیا، اور اس کا بیٹا بھائی بن گیا، اور ان سے نکاح کرنا ہمیشہ کے لئے حرام ہو گیا۔ مصاہرت : نکاح کرنے کی وجہ سے ذی رحم محرم بن جائے ، جیسے کسی عورت سے نکاح کیا تو اس کی ماں ساس بن گئی ، اور اس سے ہمیشہ کے لئے نکاح کرنا حرام ہو گیا۔
ترجمه : (١٢٣١) مسلمان ، قابل اطمینان ، عاقل، بالغ ہو ، یا عورت کا شوہر ہو، یہ ہر سفر میں شرط ہے۔
تشریح : شوہر کے علاوہ جو بھی ذکی رحم محرم ہو اس میں یہ چار شرطیں ہونا ضروری ہیں تب حج فرض ہو گا ورنہ نہیں [1] ذکی رحم محرم قابل اعتماد ہو، فاسق یا زانی کی عادت ہو تو حج فرض نہیں ہو گا [۲] عاقل ہو [۳] بالغ ہو تب حج فرض ہوگا ، تا کہ یہ عورت کی حفاظت کر سکے، یہ خود بچہ یا مجنون ہے تو عورت پر حج فرض نہیں ہوگا۔
ترجمه : (١٢٣٢) اور جنگل و سمندر کے سفر میں غلبہ سلامت کا اعتبار ہے۔
Book of Hajj. Thamaratun Najah vol. 2: On the obligation of Hajj for one who became Muslim in Dar al-Harb or is in Dar al-Islam. (1229) And the conditions for the obligation of performance are five according to the correct opinion: soundness of body, removal of physical hindrance to going for Hajj, safety of the road, absence of the waiting period (iddah), (1230) and the presence of a mahram (even through fosterage or affinity), (1231) who is Muslim, trustworthy, sane, adult, or the husband. (1232) And in travel by land and sea, reliance on preponderance of safety. Explanation: If one became Muslim in Dar al-Harb, then Hajj is obligatory upon him, but he does not have the means to know it; therefore, it becomes obligatory when he knows that Hajj is obligatory, otherwise not. And if he is in Dar al-Islam, then religious knowledge is widespread; therefore, being in Dar al-Islam is sufficient for Hajj to be obligatory, even if he does not know it, that is his negligence. Translation: (1229) In the correct madhhab, there are five conditions for the obligation to perform Hajj. Explanation: If these five conditions are met, performing Hajj becomes obligatory; if any one of them is not met, it is not obligatory to perform, but rather there is leeway to delay even though it is obligatory, and if the condition is never fulfilled in one's lifetime, performing it is not obligatory, so it is not necessary to make a will to perform Hajj. The five conditions at a glance: Soundness of body; Removal of physical hindrance to going for Hajj; Safe road; Woman not being in iddah days; Mahram accompanying. The proof for each is as follows: [1] The proof for being healthy is this verse: 'There is no blame upon the blind, nor upon the lame, nor upon the sick.' (Surah al-Fath, 48:17) This verse indicates that there is no difficulty on the excused. (2) This verse also is proof that Hajj becomes obligatory when one has the ability to reach the House of Allah: 'And upon Allah is the right of the people to perform Hajj of the House for whoever is able to find a way to it.' (Surah Al Imran, 3:97) [2] That there be no physical hindrance. [3] And that the road be secure. The proof for this is the hadith from Abu Umamah from the Prophet: 'Whoever is not prevented by sickness, an apparent need, or a tyrannical ruler, and does not perform Hajj, let him die – if he wishes – as a Jew or a Christian.' (Sunan, possibility of Hajj, fourth section, p. 546, no. 8660) This hadith indicates that a tyrannical ruler does not prevent, from which it is understood that physical hindrance must not exist. [4] For a woman, it is necessary to stay at home during the period of iddah; therefore, if she is observing iddah during the days of Hajj, performing Hajj is not obligatory upon her. [5] A mahram from among her unmarriageable relatives should accompany her, whether through fosterage or affinity. Explanation: If a mahram from among her unmarriageable relatives can accompany her, only then is performing Hajj obligatory upon her. This mahram can be of four types: [1] through blood relation, like father and brother; [2] through fosterage, like a foster brother, foster father; [3] through marriage, like father-in-law, son-in-law, due to marriage, marrying these people is forever forbidden; [4] or through marriage, the husband. This hadith mentions the mahram due to lineage, fosterage, and affinity, and also that if she has such a mahram, she can travel for Hajj, otherwise not. From Abu Sa'id, the Messenger of Allah said: 'Indeed, it is not lawful for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel a journey of three days or more except with her father, brother, husband, son, or a mahram of hers.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on woman traveling without mahram, p. 249, no. 1726; Muslim, chapter on woman traveling with mahram for Hajj etc., p. 232, no. 1340) (2) In Dar Qutni from Abu Umamah: 'I heard the Messenger of Allah say: A woman should not travel a journey of three days or perform Hajj except with her husband.' (Dar Qutni, Book of Hajj, vol. 2, p. 199, no. 2419) From this hadith it is understood that if a woman has a mahram, Hajj is obligatory upon her, because without a mahram, traveling for more than three days is not permissible. Lexical meaning of mahram: One with whom marriage is forever forbidden. Rada': A mahram through unmarriageable kinship due to breastfeeding, e.g., a woman whose milk is drunk becomes a mother, and her husband becomes a father, and his son becomes a brother, and marriage with them becomes forever forbidden. Musahara: A mahram through unmarriageable kinship due to marriage, e.g., if one marries a woman, her mother becomes mother-in-law, and marriage with her becomes forever forbidden. Translation: (1231) The mahram must be Muslim, trustworthy, sane, adult, or the husband of the woman; this is a condition in every journey. Explanation: Apart from the husband, any mahram from among the unmarriageable relatives must have these four conditions for Hajj to be obligatory, otherwise not: [1] The mahram must be trustworthy; if he is a habitual sinner or adulterer, Hajj is not obligatory. [2] He must be sane. [3] He must be adult; only then Hajj becomes obligatory, so that he can protect the woman; if he is a child or insane, Hajj is not obligatory on the woman. Translation: (1232) And in travel by land and sea, reliance is on preponderance of safety.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the five conditions for the obligation to perform Hajj (shurut wujub al-ada). It distinguishes between the obligation of Hajj itself (wujub al-asl) and the obligation to perform it immediately (wujub al-ada). The author states that according to the correct (al-ashahh) view in the Hanafi madhhab, there are five conditions for the obligation to perform. If these conditions are all present, performing Hajj is obligatory (fard) immediately. If any condition is absent, the obligation to perform is deferred, though the Hajj remains a debt upon the person. If the condition is never fulfilled, the obligation to perform never becomes active, and no will (wasiyyah) is required for Hajj. The five conditions are: (1) soundness of body (sihhat al-badan) – the person must be physically able to undertake the journey and perform the rites; (2) removal of physical hindrance (zawal al-mani' al-hissi) – there must be no physical barrier such as imprisonment or being shackled; (3) safety of the road (amn al-tariq) – the route must be secure from dangers; (4) a woman not being in her waiting period (iddah) – a woman observing iddah after divorce or death of husband must remain at home and cannot travel; (5) the presence of a mahram for a woman – a woman must travel with a mahram, who can be from lineage (nasab), fosterage (rada'), or affinity (musahara), or her husband. The author then provides proofs: for health, the Quranic verse (48:17) exempting the blind, lame, and sick, and the verse (3:97) on ability (istita'ah). For removal of hindrance and safe road, the hadith of Abu Umamah stating that he who is not prevented by sickness, obvious need, or tyrannical ruler and does not perform Hajj may die as a Jew or Christian. For the woman's conditions, hadiths from Abu Dawud and Muslim prohibit a woman from traveling three days or more without a mahram, and another from Dar Qutni specifies Hajj with a husband. The author then defines mahram, rada', and musahara. Additionally, the mahram must be Muslim, trustworthy (ma'mun), sane (aqil), and adult (baligh) – these are conditions for the mahram himself. If the mahram is a child, insane, or unreliable, the woman's obligation to perform is not triggered. Finally, for land and sea travel, the condition is not absolute safety but the preponderance of safety (ghalabat al-salamah); if the route is generally safe, the condition is met.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently forbidden due to lineage, fosterage, or affinity, and who may accompany a woman in travel.
رضاع (rada'): Fosterage kinship established through breastfeeding, creating permanent marriage prohibition.
مصاهرة (musahara): Kinship through marriage, e.g., mother-in-law, son-in-law, creating permanent marriage prohibition.
شروط وجوب الأداء (shurut wujub al-ada): Conditions that must be present for the obligation to perform Hajj immediately, as opposed to conditions for the Hajj itself being obligatory (wujub al-asl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT one of the five conditions for the obligation to perform Hajj (wujub al-ada)?
A) Soundness of body
B) Having a mahram for a woman
C) Being free from debt
D) Safety of the road

Key Takeaway
The obligation to perform Hajj immediately depends on five specific conditions; if any is missing, performance is deferred but the Hajj remains a debt.

Woman's Hajj: The Mahram Requirement
Ruling on obligatory mahram for women's Hajj journey

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a mahram for a woman's Hajj and explain why the Hanafi school requires a mahram for the obligation of Hajj.

Core Idea
A woman's Hajj is not obligatory without a mahram; the mahram must be Muslim, trustworthy, sane, adult, or her husband.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the requirement of a mahram for a woman's Hajj. Drawing from hadith evidence, the text establishes that travel of three days or more without a mahram is prohibited, and thus Hajj – which involves such travel – becomes obligatory only when a suitable mahram accompanies her. We will unpack the conditions that make a mahram valid and explore the proof for this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that Hajj is obligatory (fard) upon a woman only if she has a mahram to accompany her. Without a mahram, Hajj is not obligatory.
This is a conditional obligation (fard 'ala al-shart).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith from Abu Dawud and Muslim: 'It is not lawful for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel a distance of three days or more except with a mahram.'
The hadith is a hadith ahad, so it provides zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith prohibits travel without a mahram. Since Hajj normally involves travel of more than three days, the prohibition implies that Hajj is not permissible without a mahram, and therefore not obligatory.
The 'illa (effective cause) is the travel duration.
4
Note the conditions for the mahram
For a mahram other than the husband, four conditions are required: Muslim, trustworthy (aman), sane (aqil), and adult (baligh). The husband is exempt from these conditions.
The text also lists four categories of mahram: lineage, suckling, in-law relationship, and husband.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'i) allow a woman to travel with a group of trustworthy women without a mahram. The Hanafi school adheres to the requirement of a mahram based on the hadith.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi view is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text

(ابوداؤد شریف، باب في المرأة تج بغیر محرم ص ۲۴۹ نمبر ۱۷۲۶ و مسلم شریف ، باب سفر المرأة مع محرم الى حج وغیرہ ص ۲۳۲ نمبر ۱۳۴۰) (۲) دار قطنی میں ہے عن ابی امامۃ قال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول لا تسافر امرأة سفرا ثلاثة ايام او تحج الا و معها زوجها. Number (1230) And the exit of a mahram, even if from suckling or affinity. (1231) Muslim, trustworthy, sane, adult, or husband. Translation (1230): A woman should go out with a dhul-mahram, whether from suckling or from in-law relations. Explanation: Only if a dhul-mahram can accompany her does Hajj become obligatory upon her. These dhul-mahram can be four types: [1] from lineage like father and brother; [2] from suckling like foster brother, foster father; [3] from marriage like father-in-law, son-in-law, marriage with whom is permanently forbidden; [4] husband. [5] This hadith mentions mahram by lineage, suckling, and affinity, and that if there is a mahram she can travel for Hajj, otherwise not. From Abu Sa'id: The Messenger of Allah said: 'It is not lawful for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel a distance of three days or more except with her father, brother, husband, son, or a mahram of hers.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on woman traveling without mahram, p. 249 no. 1726; Muslim, chapter on woman's travel with mahram for Hajj etc., p. 232 no. 1340) (2) In Dar Qutni: From Abu Umama: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'A woman should not travel a journey of three days or perform Hajj except with her husband.' (Dar Qutni, Book of Hajj, vol. 2 p. 199 no. 2419) This hadith makes it clear that Hajj becomes obligatory only if there is a mahram with the woman, because travel of more than three days without a mahram is not permissible. Lexical meaning of mahram: one with whom marriage is permanently forbidden. Rida': one becomes a mahram through suckling, e.g., if a woman's milk is drunk, she becomes a mother, her husband becomes a father, his son becomes a brother, and marriage with them is permanently forbidden. Musaharat: one becomes a mahram through marriage, e.g., if a man marries a woman, her mother becomes his mother-in-law, and marriage with her is permanently forbidden. Translation (1231): Muslim, trustworthy, sane, adult, or the woman's husband; this is a condition in every journey. Explanation: Apart from the husband, any other dhul-mahram must have these four conditions for Hajj to become obligatory; otherwise it does not: [1] The dhul-mahram must be trustworthy; if he is a habitual sinner or fornicator, Hajj is not obligatory. [2] Sane. [3] Adult, so that he can protect her; if he is a child or insane, Hajj is not obligatory upon the woman.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the requirement of a mahram for a woman's Hajj. The matn (1230) states that a woman must have a mahram—whether by lineage, suckling, or affinity—for her journey. The commentary lists four categories: blood relatives like father and brother; foster relatives like foster brother and father; in-laws through marriage where marriage is permanently forbidden, such as father-in-law and son-in-law; and the husband himself. The passage then provides hadith evidence: the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade women from traveling three or more days without a mahram. This includes Hajj since it involves travel. The hadith from Abu Dawud and Muslim specify acceptable mahrams. Another hadith from Dar Qutni emphasizes the husband. Thus, the ruling is that Hajj becomes obligatory for a woman only if she has a mahram. The matn (1231) adds conditions for the mahram other than the husband: he must be Muslim, trustworthy (not a sinner), sane, and adult. The commentary explains that if the mahram is a child or insane, he cannot provide protection, so Hajj is not obligatory. These conditions ensure that the woman is safe during the journey.

Key Terms
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, suckling, or affinity.
رضاع (rida'): Suckling relationship that creates permanent marriage prohibition; e.g., foster mother, foster father, foster siblings.
مصاهرة (musaharat): Affinity relationship created through marriage, making certain relatives permanently forbidden for marriage (e.g., mother-in-law).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Muslim, trustworthy, adult, and sane

C) Trustworthy, adult, married, and sane
D) Muslim, adult, and a blood relative

Key Takeaway
A woman's Hajj is obligatory only if she has a mahram who is Muslim, trustworthy, sane, and adult (or her husband).

Safety of Route for Hajj: The Criterion of Predominant Safety
Legal criterion for safety on land and sea routes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criterion for route safety in Hajj and apply it to determine whether Hajj is obligatory.

Core Idea
Hajj becomes obligatory if the route is predominantly safe; occasional dangers do not prevent obligation.

Hajj is obligatory only when the route to Makkah is secure. But how secure must it be? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi standard: it is not absolute safety but predominant safety (ghalabat al-salamah). Even if danger occurs occasionally, as long as the general condition of the route is safe, Hajj is fard. We will explore the reasoning behind this rule and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The passage states that for Hajj to be obligatory, the route must be secure. But security is defined as predominant safety, not absolute safety. Recognize that this is a condition (shart) for the obligation.
Condition: route predominantly safe on land and sea.
2
Clarify the meaning of 'predominant safety'
Understand that 'ghalabat al-salamah' means the usual state of the route is safe, even if there are rare incidents of danger. The text emphasizes that occasional danger is not considered.
Contrast: if danger is frequent, then not predominant.
3
Apply the reasoning from the Farewell Pilgrimage
The Prophet performed Hajj despite potential war danger because peace was the norm. This shows that the predominant condition, not exceptional risks, determines obligation.
Wajh: istidlal with the Prophet's action.
4
Distinguish from alternative views
Note that some scholars require absolute safety. The Hanafi school relies on predominant safety, and this is the mufta bihi (position for fatwa). Understand the practical difference.
Ikhtilaf: other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۲۳۲) اور جنگل و سمندر کے سفر میں غلبہ سلامت کا اعتبار ہے۔ تشریح : اوپر آیا کہ راستہ مامون ہو، تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ غالب گمان یہ ہے کہ مامون ہے، یا عام حالات میں مامون ہو تو حج فرض ہو جائے گا، پھر کبھی کبھار خطرہ ہو جائے تو اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ وجه : حجۃ الوداع کے موقع پر عام حالات امن کے تھے تو حج فرض ہو گیا ، حالانکہ جنگ کا بھی خطرہ تھا، اس لئے غالب حالت کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔
Translation (1232): And the consideration is of predominant safety on land and sea, according to the fatwa. Explanation: Earlier it came that the route should be secure; its meaning is that the predominant assumption is that it is secure, or under normal circumstances it is secure, so Hajj will become obligatory. Then if danger occurs occasionally, it is not considered. Reasoning: On the occasion of the Farewell Pilgrimage, normal circumstances were of peace, so Hajj became obligatory, even though there was also danger of war; therefore, the predominant condition will be considered.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage states the ruling regarding safety of the travel route for Hajj. The matn (1232) says that the criterion is predominant safety (ghalabat al-salamah) on both land and sea, and this is the position adopted for fatwa (mufta bihi). The commentary explains that if the route is generally secure and the predominant assumption is safety, then Hajj becomes obligatory. Rare or occasional dangers do not prevent obligation. The reasoning (wajh) is derived from the Farewell Pilgrimage: the Prophet performed Hajj despite potential dangers, because security was the norm. Thus, the normal state is considered, not exceptional risks.

Key Terms
غلبۃ السلامة (ghalabat al-salamah): The predominant or overwhelming state of safety; the usual condition of the route being secure.
المفتى به (al-mufta bihi): The relied-upon position for legal verdicts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On what basis is Hajj considered obligatory regarding route safety?
A) Absolute safety must be guaranteed
B) Predominant safety is sufficient
C) Safety of the first leg of journey
D) Opinion of local scholars

Key Takeaway
Hajj becomes obligatory if the route is predominantly safe; occasional dangers do not matter.

Pillars and Conditions of Hajj Performance
Conditions and pillars for valid Hajj with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions (shurut) and pillars (arkan) of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and identify the proofs for wuquf and tawaf.

Core Idea
Hajj is valid with two conditions (Islam and ihram) and two pillars (wuquf and tawaf).

This passage from Thamaratun Najah clarifies the essential elements for a valid Hajj. The Hanafi school distinguishes between conditions (shurut) that must be present for the act to be valid, and pillars (arkan) that constitute the act itself. Understanding this distinction is crucial for performing Hajj correctly and knowing what obligations are incurred if something is missed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that Hajj is fard ayn, and its valid performance requires four elements: two conditions and two pillars.
The ruling is fard ayn, not fard kifayah.
2
Distinguish conditions from pillars
The text explicitly says Islam and ihram are conditions (shartan), while wuquf and tawaf are the acts that constitute the pillars (ruknan).
Conditions must be present for validity; pillars are the essential acts.
3
Locate the dalil for wuquf
Two hadiths are cited: the first from 'Urwa ibn Mudarris and the second from Abd al-Rahman ibn Ya'mur, both stating that Hajj is completed by standing at Arafah before Fajr of the 10th.
These hadiths are from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
4
Locate the dalil for tawaf
The Quranic verse (22:29) 'And let them circumambulate the Ancient House' is cited as evidence for the obligation of tawaf al-ziyarah.
The imperative form indicates obligation.
5
Note the Hanafi distinction
Ihram is a condition, not a pillar. Only wuquf and tawaf are pillars. This contrasts with some other schools that consider sai or other acts as pillars.
This distinction affects what requires dam if omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۲۳۳) آزاد آدمی کے لئے حج فرض کی ادائیگی چار چیز کے کر لینے سے صحیح ہو جاتی ہے :[1] احرام باندھنا اور مسلمان ہونا، اور یہ دونوں شرطیں ہیں۔ تشریح : آزاد آدمی دو شرطوں کے ساتھ دو کام کر لے تو حج ادا ہو جائے گا۔ دو شرطیں یہ ہیں کہ [1] احرام باندھا ہوا ہو، [۲] اور دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ مسلمان ہو۔ اور دو کام یہ ہیں کہ [1] عرفہ کے دن وقوف عرفہ کر لے (۲) اور دسویں ذی الحجہ سے بارہویں ذی الحجہ کی شام تک طواف زیارت کر لے تو حج ادا ہو جائے گا ، یہ سب ملا کر چار چیزیں ہیں ۔ اصل تو تین ہی فرض ہیں [1] احرام باندھنا (۲) وقوف عرفہ کرنا (۳) طواف زیارت کرنا۔ وجه : (۱) وقوف عرفہ فرض ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ اخبرني عروة بن مضرس الطائي قال اتيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالموقف يعني بجمع قلت جئت يا رسول الله من جبلي طيء اكللت مطيتي و اتعبت نفسي والله ما تركت من حبل الا وقفت عليه فهل لي من حج فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من ادرك معنا هذه الصلوة و اتى عرفات قبل ذلك ليلا او نهارا فقد تم حجه و قضى تفثه . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من لم یدرک عرفته، ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۱۹۵۰؛ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء من ادرک الامام بجمع فقد ادرک الحج، ص ۲۲۰، نمبر ۸۸۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ کی فجر سے پہلے دن یا رات میں وقوف عرفہ کر لیا تو اس کا حج ہو گیا (۲) عن عبد الرحمن بن يعمر الديلي قال اتيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو بعرفة فجاء ناس او نفر من اهل نجد فامروا رجلا فنادى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كيف الحج فامر رجلا فنادى الحج الحج يوم عرفة ومن جاء قبل صلوة الصبح من ليلة جمع فتم حجه (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من لم یدرک عرفته، ص ۲۸۴، نمبر ۱۹۴۹؛ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء من ادرک الامام بجمع فقد ادرک الحج، ص ۲۱۹ نمبر ۸۸۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وقوف عرفہ کرے تو حج ہوگا۔ (۳) اور طواف زیارت کے لئے یہ آیت ہے۔ و ليطوفوا بالبيت العتيق - آیت ۲۹ ، سورۃ الحج ۲۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ طواف زیارت کرو۔ ترجمه : (۱۲۳۴) پھر دونوں رکنوں کو لائے ، اور وہ احرام کی حالت میں عرفات کا وقوف کرنا ہے چاہے ایک لحظہ ہو.
Translation (1233): For a free person, the performance of obligatory Hajj is valid with four things: [1] donning ihram and being Muslim, and these two are conditions. Explanation: A free person, with two conditions and performing two acts, will have his Hajj performed. The two conditions are: [1] he has donned ihram, [2] the second condition is that he is Muslim. And the two acts are: [1] he performs wuquf at Arafat on the day of Arafah, [2] and he performs tawaf al-ziyarah from the tenth of Dhul Hijjah until the evening of the twelfth of Dhul Hijjah; thus Hajj is performed. These together are four things. Actually there are three obligatory acts: [1] donning ihram, [2] performing wuquf at Arafah, [3] performing tawaf al-ziyarah. Evidence: (1) Wuquf at Arafah is obligatory; for this there is hadith: 'Urwa ibn Mudarris al-Tai reported: I came to the Messenger of Allah at the standing place (i.e., Muzdalifah) and said: I have come, O Messenger of Allah, from the mountains of Tayy; I have exhausted my mount and tired myself; by Allah, I left no hill without standing on it; so is there Hajj for me? The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever prays this prayer with us and comes to Arafat before that, night or day, has completed his Hajj and fulfilled his obligations. (Abu Dawud, chapter on one who does not catch Arafah, p. 285, no. 1950; Tirmidhi, chapter on one who catches the imam at Muzdalifah has caught Hajj, p. 220, no. 889) This hadith states that if one performs wuquf at Arafah during the day or night before Fajr of the tenth, his Hajj is valid. (2) From Abd al-Rahman ibn Ya'mur al-Dili: I came to the Prophet at Arafah, and some people from Najd came; they asked a man to call out: How is Hajj? The Prophet ordered a man to call out: Hajj is (standing at) Arafah; whoever comes before the Fajr prayer of the night of Muzdalifah, his Hajj is complete. (Abu Dawud, p. 284 no. 1949; Tirmidhi p. 219 no. 888) This hadith states that performing wuquf at Arafah makes Hajj valid. (3) For tawaf al-ziyarah, there is the verse: 'And let them circumambulate the Ancient House' (Surah al-Hajj 22:29). This verse commands tawaf al-ziyarah. Translation (1234): Then he brings its two pillars, and they are: wuquf at Arafat while in ihram, even if for a moment.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage explains the elements necessary for the validity of Hajj. The matn (1233) states that Hajj is valid with four things: ihram and Islam as conditions, and then the two pillars mentioned in (1234). The commentary clarifies that there are actually three obligations (fara'id) according to the Hanafi school: ihram, wuquf at Arafah, and tawaf al-ziyarah. Islam is a condition (shart), not a pillar. The passage then provides proofs: for wuquf, two hadiths from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi emphasize that the essence of Hajj is standing at Arafah. For tawaf al-ziyarah, the Quranic verse (22:29) 'And let them circumambulate the Ancient House' is cited as evidence. The matn (1234) clarifies that the two pillars are wuquf at Arafat while in ihram, even for a moment, and tawaf al-ziyarah (which is implied). The commentary explains that performing these with the conditions makes Hajj valid.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, initiated by wearing two unstitched cloths and making niyyah.
وقوف عرفة (wuquf 'Arafah): Standing at the plain of Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; the essential pillar of Hajj.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The circumambulation of the Kaaba performed after wuquf, from 10th to 12th of Dhul Hijjah; a pillar of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Tawaf al-ziyarah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes conditions (Islam and ihram) from pillars (wuquf and tawaf) for Hajj; both are essential but with different consequences if missed.

Pillars and Conditions of Hajj with Proofs
States the pillars and conditions of Hajj with scriptural proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions and pillars of Hajj according to the Hanafi school, identify their proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and distinguish between a condition (shart) and a pillar (rukn).

Core Idea
Hajj has two conditions (Islam and ihram) and two pillars (wuquf at 'Arafat and tawaf al-ifadah) — missing a pillar invalidates Hajj.

This passage establishes the essential components of Hajj in the Hanafi school. It carefully distinguishes between conditions (shurut) that must be present for the act to be valid and pillars (arkan) that constitute the act itself. The author also provides scriptural proofs from the Sunnah and Quran to confirm each element, giving you both the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the validity of performing obligatory Hajj. It states that for a free person, Hajj is valid with four things: two conditions and two pillars.
The ruling is fard 'ayn for those who meet the conditions of obligation.
2
Locate the conditions
Identify the two conditions: Islam (being Muslim) and ihram (state of consecration). These must be present for Hajj to be valid.
Ihram is a condition, not a pillar, in the Hanafi school.
3
Identify the pillars
The two pillars are wuquf at 'Arafat (standing at 'Arafat) and tawaf al-ifadah (tawaf al-ziyarah). The author specifies time limits and requirements for each.
Wuquf must occur between zawaal of 9th and dawn of 10th; tawaf requires at least four circuits after dawn of 10th.
4
Examine the proofs
The author cites two hadiths for wuquf: one from 'Urwa ibn Mudarris and one from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ya'mur, both confirming that wuquf at 'Arafat completes Hajj. For tawaf, the Quranic verse (22:29) is cited.
The hadiths are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but their meaning (dalala) is clear.
5
Note the Hanafi nuance
Understand why ihram is a condition (not a pillar) and why the majority (akthar) of tawaf suffices. This affects how rulings are derived.
The Urdu summary also lists the 22 wajibat of Hajj, which are distinct from the pillars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصح اداء فرض الـحــج باربعة اشياء للحرّ الاحرام والاسلام وهما شرطان (۱۲۳۴ ) ثم الاتيان بركنيه و هما الوقوف مـحــرمـا بعرفات لحظة من زوال يوم التاسع الى فجر يوم النحر بشرط عدم الجماع قبله محرما(۱۲۳۵) والركن الثاني هو اكثر طواف الإفاضة في وقته وهو ما بعد طلوع فجر يوم النحر.(دلائل:) اخبرني عروة بن مضرس الطائي قال اتيت رسول الله بالموقف يعني بجمع قلت جئت يا رسول الله من جبلي طي اكللت مطيتي و اتعبت نفسي والله ما تركت من حبل الا وقـفـت عليه فهل لي من حج فقال رسول الله من ادرك معنا هذه الصلوة واتى عرفات قبل ذلك ليلا او نهارا فقد تم حجه و قضى تفته . (ابوداؤد شريف ، باب من لم یدرک عرفته ، ص ۲۸۵، نمبر ۱۹۵۰ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء من ادرك الامام مجمع فقد ادرك الحج، ص ۲۲۰، نمبر ۸۸۹) وعن عبد الرحمن بن يعمر الديلي قال اتيت النبي وهو بعرفات فجاء ناس او نفر من اهل نجد فامروا رجلا فنادى رسول الله كيف الحج فامر رجلا فنادى الحج الحج يوم عرفة ومن جاء قبل صلوة الصبح من ليلة جمع فتم حجه (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من لم یدرک عرفته ، ص ۲۸۴، نمبر ۱۹۴۹ ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء من ادرك الامام مجمع فقد ادرك الحج ،ص ۲۱۹ نمبر ۸۸۹) واما طواف الإفاضة فدليله قوله تعالى: {وَلْيَطَّوَّفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتِيقِ} (الحج: ٢٩) حج کے فرائض (۳) چیزیں ہیں: ایک نظر میں ...... احرام باندھنا ...... وقوف عرفہ کرنا .... طواف زیارت کرنا حج کے واجبات (۲۲) چیزیں ہیں: ایک نظر میں ا میقات سے احرام باندھنا۔ .. وقوف عرفات کو غروب تک دراز کرنا۔ ... یوم نحر کی فجر کے بعد طلوع شمس سے پہلے مزدلفہ کا قیام۔ ....... ...... جمروں پر کنکری پھینکنا۔ قارن اور متمتع کو قربانی کرنا۔ سرمنڈوانا ( یا بال کٹوانا )۔ ... اور اس کو خاص حرم میں اور ایام نحر میں کرنا۔ رمی کو حلق سے مقدم کرنا۔
(1233) For a free person, the performance of the Hajj obligatory duty is valid by four things: ihram and Islam – these are two conditions – (1234) then performing its two pillars, which are: standing at 'Arafat while in ihram for a moment from the decline of the sun on the ninth day until the dawn of the day of sacrifice, with the condition of not having sexual intercourse before it while in ihram, (1235) and the second pillar is the majority of the tawaf al-ifadah in its time, and that is after the dawn of the day of sacrifice. (Proofs:) 'Urwah ibn Mudarris narrated: 'I came to the Messenger of Allah at the standing place, i.e., Jam'. I said: 'I have come from the mountains of Tayyi', exhausting my mount and myself. By Allah, I left no mountain pass without standing on it. Do I have a complete Hajj?' The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever joins us in this prayer and comes to 'Arafat before it, by night or by day, has completed his Hajj and fulfilled his duty.' (Abu Dawud, Bab man lam yudrik 'Arafah, p. 285, no. 1950; Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a man adraka al-imam bi Jam', p. 220, no. 889) And from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Ya'mur al-Dayli: 'I came to the Prophet while he was at 'Arafat, and some people from Najd came and asked a man to call out: 'How is Hajj?' He ordered a man to call out: 'Hajj, Hajj is the day of 'Arafah. Whoever comes before the dawn prayer of the night of Jam' has completed his Hajj.' (Abu Dawud, p. 284, no. 1949; Tirmidhi, p. 219, no. 888) As for tawaf al-ifadah, its proof is the saying of Allah: 'And let them perform tawaf around the Ancient House' (Surah Hajj 22:29). [The remainder is Urdu commentary summarizing the obligations and recommendations of Hajj.]
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof presentation of the essential components of Hajj in the Hanafi school. It begins by stating that performing the obligatory Hajj is valid with four matters: two conditions (ihram and being Muslim) and two pillars (wuquf at 'Arafat and tawaf al-ziyarah). The author emphasizes that ihram and Islam are prerequisites, not pillars themselves. The first pillar, wuquf, must be done in a state of ihram at 'Arafat for at least a moment, between the decline of the sun on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah and dawn of the 10th, with the condition that no sexual intercourse occurred before it in the state of ihram (which would invalidate ihram). The second pillar is performing the majority (at least four circuits) of tawaf al-ziyarah (tawaf al-ifadah) within its time, which begins at dawn of the 10th. The author then provides scriptural evidences: two hadiths from Sahih sources confirming that wuquf is the essence of Hajj, and the Quranic verse 'wal yattawwafu bil bayt al-`atiq' for tawaf. The passage ends with a concise Urdu list of the three fara'id (ihram, wuquf, tawaf) and the twenty-two wajibat (including ihram from miqat, extending wuquf until sunset, staying at Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat, sacrifice for qarin and mutamatti', shaving/trimming, and sequence). This reinforces the standard Hanafi teaching that while the arkan are few, the wajibat are numerous and must be observed.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj, initiated by wearing the unsewn garments and making niyyah, which is a condition for the validity of Hajj.
وقوف عرفة (wuquf 'Arafah): Standing or being present at 'Arafat during the specified time (zawaal of 9th to dawn of 10th) while in ihram, which is the primary pillar of Hajj.
طواف الإفاضة (tawaf al-ifadah): Also called tawaf al-ziyarah, the obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba performed after returning from Mina, of which the majority (four circuits) must be done within its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT part of the four things required to perform Hajj for a free person?
A) Ihram
B) Islam
C) Wuquf at 'Arafat
D) Sacrifice of a sheep

Key Takeaway
The validity of Hajj depends on two conditions (Islam and ihram) and two pillars (wuquf at 'Arafat and tawaf al-ifadah); any missing pillar invalidates the Hajj, while omitted wajibat require a sacrifice.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner

The Pillars of Hajj: Wuquf and Tawaf al-Ifada
Defines the two pillars of Hajj with conditions and timings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two pillars of Hajj, identify their conditions and timings, and explain the consequence of omission according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Wuquf at Arafat and Tawaf al-Ifada are the two pillars of Hajj; each has precise timing and conditions.

The Hajj pilgrimage rests on two foundational acts: standing at Arafat and circumambulating the Kaaba. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on what these pillars are, when they must be performed, and what invalidates them. The source text from the Thamrat al-Najah commentary provides the essential rulings with expansion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two pillars
Recognize that wuquf at Arafat and Tawaf al-Ifada are the two arkan of Hajj. Omission of either invalidates the Hajj.
The text also mentions a third fard (ihram) in the summary, but the focus here is on the two pillars.
2
Define the time window for wuquf
Wuquf must occur between the decline of the sun on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah and the dawn of the 10th. A single moment within this window suffices.
Hanafis do not require standing; mere presence (even riding) counts as wuquf.
3
Identify the condition of ihram and prohibition of intercourse
The pilgrim must be in the state of ihram during wuquf. Sexual intercourse after ihram but before wuquf invalidates the ihram and thus the Hajj.
Intercourse after wuquf does not invalidate the Hajj but requires a dam (penalty).
4
Understand the ruling for Tawaf al-Ifada
The second pillar is performing the majority (akthar) of Tawaf al-Ifada within its prescribed time: from dawn of the 10th to the evening of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
Hanafis: more than half of the seven circuits suffices; other schools require all seven.
5
Note the three faraid of Hajj
The text summarizes that the faraid (pillars) of Hajj are three: binding ihram, wuquf at Arafat, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah (al-Ifada).
In Hanafi terminology, 'fard' is often used interchangeably with 'rukn' for Hajj.

الوقوف مـحــرمـا بعرفات لحظة من زوال يوم التاسع الى فجر يوم النحر بشرط عدم الجماع قبلة محرما(۱۲۳۵) والركن الثاني هو اكثر طواف الإفاضة في وقته وهو ما بعد طلوع فجر کا زوال سے دسویں تاریخ کے فجر تک ، اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ احرام کی حالت میں اس سے پہلے جماع نہ کیا ہو۔ تشریح : احرام کی حالت میں عرفات کا وقوف کرے، اور یہ وقت نویں ذی الحجہ کے زوال سے شروع ہوتا ہے اور دسویں ذی الحجہ کی فجر تک رہتا ہے، لیکن یہ شرط ہے کہ احرام باندھنے کے بعد جماع نہ کیا ہو، کیونکہ جماع کرنے سے احرام فاسد ہو جائے گا اس لئے حج بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ ترجمه : (۱۲۳۵) دوسرا رکن یہ ہے کہ طواف زیارت کا اکثر حصہ اپنے وقت میں کیا ہو، اور وہ دسویں تاریخ کے فجر کے بعد سے شروع ہوتا ہے ( اور تیرہویں تاریخ کی شام تک رہتا ہے )
تشریح : حج کا دوسرا رکن یہ ہے کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ کے فجر سے لیکر تیرہویں تاریخ کی شام تک طواف زیارت کا اکثر حصہ ادا کر لے تو جج ہو جائے گا۔
حج کے فرائض (۳) چیزیں ہیں: ایک نظر میں
...... احرام باندھنا
...... وقوف عرفہ کرنا
.... طواف زیارت کرنا
Standing as a muhrim at Arafat for a moment from the decline of the sun on the ninth day until the dawn of the day of Nahr, with the condition of no intercourse before it while in ihram (1235). The second pillar is the majority of Tawaf al-Ifada in its time, which is after the dawn of the tenth day. Tashreeh: Perform wuquf at Arafat in the state of ihram; this time begins from the decline of the sun on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah and lasts until dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, but with the condition that one did not have intercourse after donning ihram, because intercourse invalidates ihram and thus the Hajj. Translation: (1235) The second pillar is that the majority of Tawaf al-Ziyarah is performed in its time, which begins after the dawn of the tenth day (and lasts until the evening of the thirteenth day). Tashreeh: The second pillar of Hajj is that one performs the majority of Tawaf al-Ziyarah from the dawn of the tenth of Dhul Hijjah until the evening of the thirteenth day, then the Hajj becomes valid. The obligatory acts (faraid) of Hajj are three things: at a glance... binding ihram, performing wuquf at Arafat, performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage defines the two pillars (arkan) of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. The first pillar is wuquf at Arafat, which must be done in the state of ihram for any moment between the decline of the sun on the ninth of Dhul Hijjah and the dawn of the tenth. A critical condition is that one must not have engaged in sexual intercourse after entering ihram, as that would invalidate the ihram and consequently the entire Hajj. The second pillar is performing the majority (akthar) of Tawaf al-Ifada (also called Tawaf al-Ziyarah) within its allowed time: from the dawn of the tenth until the evening of the thirteenth. The passage also summarizes the three faraid (obligatory acts at the level of pillars) of Hajj: ihram, wuquf, and tawaf. The Urdu commentary expands on these rulings, emphasizing that the standing at Arafat must be while in ihram and that the tawaf's majority suffices.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): A pillar or integral element of Hajj; its omission invalidates the act entirely.
وقوف (wuquf): Standing or staying at Arafat; it is the first pillar of Hajj.
طواف الإفاضة (tawaf al-ifada): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba after returning from Mina, also called Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The pilgrim must be standing and facing the Kaaba

Key Takeaway
Wuquf at Arafat for a moment in ihram and performing the majority of Tawaf al-Ifada within their specified times are essential for a valid Hajj.

The Twenty-Two Wajibat of Hajj
Lists the twenty-two wajibat of Hajj and provides proof for their compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 22 wajibat of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and explain the consequence of omitting a wajib (dam) with proof from the Companions.

Core Idea
Omitting a wajib of Hajj requires dam but does not invalidate the Hajj.

This passage enumerates the twenty-two wajibat of Hajj — acts that are obligatory but not pillars. Unlike fard, omitting a wajib does not break the Hajj; it only necessitates a compensatory blood sacrifice (dam). The author also provides the evidential basis from the statements of two Companions, Ibn Abbas and Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib, who command that forgetting or delaying a rite must be compensated by spilling blood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept of wajib in Hajj
Understand that these 22 acts are wajib, not fard, meaning omission does not invalidate Hajj but requires dam.
2
Review the list of wajibat
The text lists 22 specific actions. Note the variety: some are about timing, sequence, or location.
3
Analyze the proof from the Companions
The author quotes two qawl sahabi: Ibn Abbas and Abbas. The imperative 'falyuhriq daman' indicates the obligation of dam for any omission or delay.
The dalil is zanni al-thubut, hence the ruling is wajib not fard.
4
Distinguish between wajib and fard
The text draws an analogy to sajda sahw in prayer. This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.

The wajibat of Hajj are 22 things: at a glance: (1) Binding ihram from the miqat. (2) Prolonging wuquf at Arafat until sunset. (3) Staying at Muzdalifah after dawn of the day of Nahr before sunrise. (4) Throwing pebbles at the Jamarat. (5) Qarin and Mutamatti' sacrificing. (6) Shaving the head (or trimming hair). (7) Doing so specifically in the Haram and in the days of Nahr; preferring rami over halq. An-Nahr. (1236) And the wajibat of Hajj: (1237) Binding ihram from the miqat; Qarin and Mutamatti' sacrificing between rami and halq. (8) Performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah in the days of Nahr. (9) Performing Sa'y between Safa and Marwah in the months of Hajj. (10) This Sa'y being after a valid tawaf. (11) Performing Sa'y walking for one not excused. (12) Starting Sa'y from Safa. (15) Tawaf al-Wada'. (13) Starting every tawaf of the House from the Black Stone. (14) Starting with the right hand (tayammun). (16) Performing Tawaf walking for one not excused. (17) Being free from both hadaths (minor and major). (20) Covering the nakedness. (18) Performing all of Tawaf al-Ziyarah in the days of Nahr. (19) Abandoning the prohibitions (muharramat). Translation: (1236) The wajibat of Hajj are 22 things: Explanation: The 22 things are the wajibat of Hajj. If one omits them, the Hajj is not invalid, but for some of them a blood sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory, just as in prayer omitting a wajib requires sajda sahw. Proof: (1) In this saying of a Companion: Ibn Abbas said, 'Whoever forgets something of his rites or leaves it, let him spill blood.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab man taraka shay'an min al-rami hatta yadhhab ayyam mina, vol. 5, p. 248, no. 9688) This effect shows that if one forgets or leaves something, dam is necessary. (2) Also in this saying of a Companion: 'From Abbas, he said: Whoever brings forward something of his Hajj or delays it, let him spill blood for that.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, fi al-rajul yuhalliq qabla an yadhbah, vol. 3, p. 1345, no. 14954) This effect shows that if one delays from the time, dam becomes necessary. Translation: (1337) [1] Binding ihram from the miqat.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage outlines the twenty-two wajibat (obligatory acts) of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. These actions are not pillars; omitting them does not invalidate the Hajj, but for each omission, a blood sacrifice (dam) is required as compensation. The list includes actions such as binding ihram from the miqat, prolonging wuquf until sunset, staying at Muzdalifah, throwing pebbles, shaving the head, performing tawaf and sa'y in specified ways, and abandoning prohibitions. The text then provides the evidence from the statements of the Companions: Ibn Abbas and Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib (may Allah be pleased with them) who said that whoever forgets or leaves a rite must offer a dam, and whoever delays or advances a rite must also offer a dam. This establishes the Hanafi ruling that wajibat omissions require dam but do not break the Hajj, analogous to how sajda sahw compensates for wajib omissions in prayer. The passage ends by beginning the enumeration with the first wajib: binding ihram from the miqat.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act whose omission does not invalidate Hajj but requires a dam (blood sacrifice).
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep or goat) required as compensation for missing a wajib of Hajj or Umrah.
قول صحابی (qawl sahabi): The statement of a Companion of the Prophet; used as a source of evidence in Hanafi fiqh under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) One must perform sajda sahw

Key Takeaway
The twenty-two wajibat of Hajj are obligatory acts that, if omitted, do not invalidate the Hajj but require a blood sacrifice (dam), established by the statements of the Companions.

Initiating Ihram from the Miqat: Wajib and Its Proof
Proof that initiating ihram at the miqat is wajib and its omission requires dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on initiating ihram from the miqat, identify the hadith proofs, and apply the ruling to a scenario where a pilgrim crosses the miqat without ihram.

Core Idea
Crossing the miqat without ihram incurs a dam—the obligation is fixed by the Prophet's practice.

In this lesson, we study the first wajib of Hajj: entering ihram at the proper boundary (miqat). The author clearly states that this act is wajib, and failure to do so requires a dam (sacrifice). The proof comes from two authentic hadiths that specify the exact boundaries set by the Prophet ﷺ. Understanding this ruling is essential for every pilgrim, as it applies regardless of the means of travel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that 'tying ihram from the miqat' is wajib. Note the consequence: if omitted, a dam becomes obligatory. This is the central legal point.
The act is the initiation of ihram before crossing the miqat.
2
Examine the first hadith (Ibn 'Abbas)
The Prophet ﷺ appointed specific miqat for different regions: Dhu'l-Hulayfah for Madinah, al-Juhfah for Syria, Qarn al-Manazil for Najd, Yalamlam for Yemen. These boundaries are for those regions and for anyone passing through them.
This hadith establishes the general miqat.
3
Examine the second hadith ('A'ishah)
The Prophet ﷺ appointed Dhat 'Irq for the people of Iraq. This supplements the first hadith, completing the five miqat recognized by the Hanafi school.
Iraq did not exist as a Muslim region at the time of the first hadith, hence the additional specification.
4
Understand the Hanafi ruling
Based on these hadiths, the Hanafi school holds that it is wajib to enter ihram at the miqat. If one passes the miqat without ihram, a dam must be offered. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is relied upon for fatwa.
No intra-madhhab dispute is recorded on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۳۷) [۱] میقات سے احرام باندھنا۔
تشریح : میقات سے احرام باندھنا واجب ہے اگر نہیں باندھا تو دم لازم ہوگا۔
وجه : (۱) دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابن عباس قال وقت رسول الله صلی الله علیہ وسلم لاهل المدينة ذا الحليفة، ولاهل الشام الجحفة ، ولاهل نجد قرن المنازل ، ولاهل اليمن يلملم هن لهن ولمن اتى عليهن من غير هن ممن اراد الحج والعمرة ومن كان دون ذلك فمن حيث انشاء حتى اهل مكة من مكة . (بخارى شريف، باب محصل اہل مکتہ حج و العمر ة ص ۲۰۶ نمبر ۱۵۲۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب مواقیت الحج ص ۳۷۴ نمبر ۲۸۰۳/۱۱۸) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ یہ مقامات ان لوگوں کے لئے میقات ہیں۔ بغیر احرام کے ان سے آگے گزرنا جائز نہیں (۲) عن عائشة ان رسول الله الله وقت لاهل العراق ذات عرق (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی امواقیت ص ۲۵۰ نمبر ۷۳۹ار بخاری شریف ، باب ذات عرق لاحل العراق ص ۲۰۷ نمبر ۱۵۳۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل عراق کے لئے میقات مقام ذات عرق ہے۔
Translation: (1237) [1] Tying Ihram from the Miqat. Explanation: Tying Ihram from the Miqat is wajib; if one does not tie it, a Dam becomes obligatory. Proof: (1) The evidence is this hadith: From Ibn 'Abbas, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed for the people of Medina Dhu'l-Hulayfah, for the people of Syria al-Juhfah, for the people of Najd Qarn al-Manazil, and for the people of Yemen Yalamlam; these are for them and for anyone who comes from other than them intending Hajj and 'Umrah. And whoever is within these (boundaries) then from wherever he initiates (ihram) until the people of Mecca from Mecca. (Bukhari, Bab ... ; Muslim, Bab Mawaqit al-Hajj). From this hadith, it is established that these places are the Miqat for those people; proceeding beyond them without Ihram is not permissible. (2) From 'A'ishah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed for the people of Iraq Dhat 'Irq. (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Mawaqit; Bukhari, Bab Dhat 'Irq li-Ahl al-'Iraq). From this hadith, it is learned that for the people of Iraq, the Miqat is Dhat 'Irq.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage discusses the first wajib of Hajj: initiating ihram from the miqat. The author states that this is wajib, and failure to do so (i.e., passing the miqat without ihram) requires a dam. The proof is from two authentic hadith: the first is the well-known hadith of Ibn 'Abbas that establishes the five miqat (Dhu'l-Hulayfah for Madinah, al-Juhfah for Syria, Qarn al-Manazil for Najd, Yalamlam for Yemen, and for Iraq later specified as Dhat 'Irq). The second hadith from 'A'ishah confirms Dhat 'Irq as miqat for Iraqis. The Hanafi madhhab emphasizes that crossing these boundaries without ihram is not permissible and necessitates a dam. This ruling is consistent across the school, with the miqat boundaries considered fixed by Sunnah.

Key Terms
ميقات (miqat): Fixed boundary for entering the state of ihram for Hajj or 'Umrah.
إحرام (ihram): The sacred state entered by a pilgrim with the intention and wearing of special garments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) al-Juhfah
C) Dhat 'Irq
D) Qarn al-Manazil

Key Takeaway
Initiating ihram from the miqat is a wajib act of Hajj/Umrah; omission requires a dam, and the proof is from the Prophet's own appointment of boundaries.

Wuquf at Muzdalifah: Wajib Timing and Ruling
Ruling that standing at Muzdalifah after Fajr on the 10th is wajib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time for waqf at Muzdalifah and explain why it is wajib in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Standing at Muzdalifah after Fajr on the 10th is a wajib; omitting it requires a dam.

In the previous lesson, we learned that after leaving Arafat, the pilgrim proceeds to Muzdalifah. This lesson specifies the third wajib of Hajj: standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah during a precise time window. The Hanafi school considers this an obligatory element, though other schools view it as recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
The act is waqf at Muzdalifah; the time is from Fajr to sunrise on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
2
Understand the legal classification
It is wajib, not fard, meaning the Hajj is valid without it but a dam is required.
Wajib elements require compensation if omitted; fard elements invalidate the act.
3
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is consider it sunnah, not wajib, so no penalty for omission.
This ikhtilaf affects the practical ruling for followers of each school.
4
Apply the ruling
If a pilgrim misses this waqf entirely, they must sacrifice a dam.
The dam is a specific animal sacrifice or equivalent charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۲۳۹)[۳] دسویں تاریخ کی فجر سے لیکر سورج طلوع ہونے تک میں مزدلفہ کا وقوف کرنا واجب ہے۔ تشريح : دسویں ذی الحجہ کی رات کو مزدلفہ آجائے اور فجر طلوع ہونے سے وقت سے سورج طلوع ہونے کے درمیان وقوف مزدلفہ کرنا واجب ہے۔
Translation: (1239) [3] Stopping at Muzdalifah from the Fajr of the 10th until sunrise is wajib. Explanation: One should come to Muzdalifah on the night of the 10th of Dhil Hijjah, and stopping at Muzdalifah between the time of Fajr and sunrise is wajib.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage presents the third wajib of Hajj: the standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah. It specifies the time: from the Fajr prayer on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah until sunrise. The pilgrim should have arrived at Muzdalifah during the previous night. The author states this as a ruling without citing explicit proof, but it is established from the Prophet's practice described in the previous lesson (departing from Arafat after sunset, staying at Muzdalifah overnight, and praying Fajr there before moving to Mina). In the Hanafi madhhab, this is a wajib; leaving it out requires a dam. This indicates that although the Hajj remains valid without this stop, a sacrifice is necessary as compensation.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place near Mina where pilgrims spend the night of the 10th and perform Fajr prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Anytime during the days of Tashriq

Key Takeaway
Standing at Muzdalifah after Fajr on the 10th until sunrise is a wajib of Hajj; omission requires a dam.

The Wajib Standing at Arafat Until Sunset
Ruling with proof for wajib standing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing at Arafat, identify the prophetic proofs, and explain the consequence of leaving before sunset.

Core Idea
Standing at Arafat until sunset is wajib; departing early requires dam.

Standing at Arafat (wuquf) on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah is a central rite of Hajj. The Hanafi school holds that extending this standing until sunset is a wajib obligation, established by the Prophet's practice and explicit sunnah. In this lesson, we examine the textual proofs and understand the legal consequence of omission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening sentence of the passage. It states: 'Standing at Arafat until Maghrib is wajib.' Note the term 'wajib' in Hanafi fiqh meaning obligatory but not a rukn.
Wajib in Hajj usually requires a dam (sacrifice) if omitted, unlike a rukn which invalidates Hajj.
2
Locate the First Proof (Hadith of Jabir)
The passage cites the famous hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's Hajj: 'He continued standing until the sun set, the yellowness disappeared a little, and the disk vanished.' This fi'l (action) of the Prophet is taken as evidence for wujub.
Remember the Hanafi usul principle: Fi'l al-nabi li al-bayan yufidu al-wujub.
3
Analyze the Second Proof (Hadith of al-Musawwar)
The Prophet distinguished Islamic practice from pre-Islamic custom: 'We will depart after it sets.' This explicit statement (qawl) strengthens the obligation.
This hadith directly contrasts with the polytheist practice of departing while the sun was still high.
4
Determine the Consequence of Omission
Since the ruling is wajib, not rukn, leaving Arafat before sunset without a valid excuse requires a dam (sacrificial animal) as compensation. The Hajj itself remains valid.
According to the Hanafi school, omission of a wajib in Hajj is compensated by dam, not by repeating the Hajj.
5
Compare with Other Schools
Imam al-Shafi'i considers standing at Arafat a rukn of Hajj, so leaving before sunset would invalidate the Hajj unless a valid excuse and return. This difference (thamarah al-khilaf) impacts the validity and compensation.
Understanding inter-madhhab differences is crucial for fatwa and practice in diverse communities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۳۸)[۲] وقوف عرفات کو غروب تک دراز کرنا۔ تشریح : وقوف عرفہ مغرب تک کرنا واجب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے ۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... فلم يزل واقفا حتى غربت الشمس وذهبت الصفرة قليلا حتى غاب القرص واردف اسامة خلفه ودفع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وقد شنق للقصواء الزمام حتى ان رأسها ليصيب مورك رحله ويقول بيده اليمنى ايها الناس السكينة السكينة كلما اتى حبلا من الحبال ارخى لها قليلا حتى تصعد حتى اتى المزدلفة . Translation: (1238)[2] Extending the standing at Arafat until sunset. Explanation: Standing at Arafat until Maghrib is wajib. Proof: (1) In this hadith: 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... He continued standing until the sun set, the yellowness disappeared a little, and the disk vanished. Usama rode behind him, and the Messenger of Allah set out, snuggling the reins of al-Qaswa', such that its head reached the front of his saddle, and he said with his right hand: 'O people, calm, calm.' Whenever he came to a hill, he let the reins loose a little until it ascended, until he reached Muzdalifah.' (Muslim, Book of Hajj; Abu Dawud, Book of Hajj) From this hadith it is understood that he departed from Arafat after Maghrib. (2) There is also this hadith: 'Al-Musawwar ibn Makhramah said: The Messenger of Allah addressed us at Arafat, praised Allah, then said: As for after, the people of shirk and idols used to depart from this place when the sun was on the heads of the mountains like turbans on men's faces, but we will depart after it sets. And they used to depart from al-Mash'ar al-Haram when the sun was spread out.' (Mustadrak al-Hakim) In this hadith it is that we will leave Arafat after Maghrib, therefore staying until Maghrib is wajib.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof (hukm ma'a al-dalil) within Kitab al-Hajj of Thamaratun Najah. The ruling stated is that it is wajib to extend one's standing (wuquf) at Arafat until the sun has fully set (ghurub). The author provides two hadith proofs: (1) The famous hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's farewell pilgrimage, where he remained standing until the sun had completely set before departing to Muzdalifah. This establishes the prophetic practice as the standard. (2) The hadith of al-Musawwar ibn Makhramah, where the Prophet explicitly distinguishes the Islamic practice from pre-Islamic customs: the polytheists would depart from Arafat while the sun was still high, but the Muslims depart after sunset. Both narrations are cited with full chains in reliable hadith collections. The Hanafi position is that this standing (wuquf) from after noon until sunset is wajib, and if one omits it unnecessarily, a dam (sacrificial animal) becomes obligatory. The text follows the standard Hanafi method: it states the ruling (tarjama), then provides a brief explanation (tashrih), then lists proofs (wajh).

Key Terms
وقوف عرفات (wuquf Arafat): Standing at the plain of Arafat on the ninth of Dhul-Hijjah as a compulsory rite of Hajj.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required to compensate for an omitted wajib in Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Standing at Arafat until sunset is a wajib act in Hajj; omission requires a dam compensation according to the Hanafi school.

Standing at Muzdalifah After Fajr: Wajib and Its Proofs
Ruling with proofs for wajib standing at Muzdalifah after Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing at Muzdalifah after Fajr and cite the Quranic and hadith proofs for its wujub.

Core Idea
Standing at Muzdalifah after Fajr is wajib; the Quran's imperative and the Prophet's hadith make it a binding requirement.

This lesson examines the ruling on standing at Muzdalifah (wuquf Muzdalifah), one of the wajibat of Hajj. The passage provides two clear proofs: the Quranic verse at al-Mash'ar al-Haram and the hadith of 'Urwah ibn Mudarris. Understanding these proofs will equip you to defend the Hanafi position and appreciate how the school derives obligations from scriptural texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is standing at Muzdalifah after Fajr on Yawm al-Nahr. The Hanafi ruling: it is wajib (obligatory, not a pillar). Omission requires a dam (penalty).
2
Locate the first dalil – the Quranic verse
The author cites Quran 2:198: 'When you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument (al-Mash’ar al-Haram).' Hanafis identify al-Mash’ar al-Haram as Muzdalifah.
The verse contains the imperative 'fadhkuru' (remember).
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a qarinah to the contrary. Here, no such qarinah exists, so standing at Muzdalifah is wajib.
This is the key derivation step.
4
Locate the second dalil – the hadith
The hadith of 'Urwah ibn Mudarris reports that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever witnesses this prayer of ours (Fajr at Muzdalifah) and stands with us until we depart, and has stood at Arafat before that by night or day, his Hajj is complete and he has fulfilled its obligations.' This makes completion conditional on standing at Muzdalifah.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi’i and Maliki also consider it wajib but with different timings; Hanbali considers it a rukn (pillar). The Hanafi mufta bihi is that it is wajib requiring a dam if omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبل طلوع الشمس (۱۲۴۰) ورمي الجمار (۱۲۴۱ ) وذبح القارن والمتمتع (۱۲۴۲) والحلق وجه : (۱) مزدلفہ کا وقوف واجب ہے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ فاذا افضتم من عرفات فاذكرو الله عند المشعر الحرام (آیت ۱۹۸ سورة البقرة ٢) ( اس آیت میں امر کا صیغہ ہے کہ مشعر حرام کے پاس اللہ کا ذکر کرو اور مشعر حرام مزدلفہ میں ہے اس لئے مزدلفہ کا وقوف واجب ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عروة بن مضرس قال اتيت رسول الله بالمزدلفة . فقال رسول الله من شهد صلوتنا هذه ووقف معنا حتى يدفع وقدوقف بعرفة قبل ذلك ليلا او نهارا فقدتم حجه و قضی تفته ( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء من ادرک الامام مجمع فقد ادرک الحج ص ۷۹ انمبر (۸۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مزدلفہ کا وقوف کرنا ضروری ہے۔
And before sunrise (1240) Stoning the Jamarat (1241) Slaughtering for Qarin and Mutamatti (1242) Shaving. Proof: (1) Standing at Muzdalifah is wajib. Its evidence is this verse: 'When you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:198). In this verse there is a command form: remember Allah near the Sacred Monument, and the Sacred Monument is in Muzdalifah. Therefore standing at Muzdalifah is wajib. (2) There is a hadith: 'Urwah ibn Mudarris said: I came to the Messenger of Allah at Muzdalifah. The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever witnesses this prayer of ours and stands with us until we depart, and has already stood at Arafat before that by night or day, then his hajj is complete and he has fulfilled its obligations.' (Tirmidhi) In this hadith it is that standing at Muzdalifah is necessary.

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and proofs for the wajib of standing at Muzdalifah (wuquf Muzdalifah). The author first gives the time frame: after Fajr on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah) and before sunrise. The proof is twofold: (1) The Quranic verse commanding remembrance at 'al-Mash'ar al-Haram' (the Sacred Monument), which the Hanafis interpret as Muzdalifah, and the imperative form (amr) indicates wujub. (2) The hadith of 'Urwah ibn Mudarris, which explicitly conditions completion of hajj on witnessing the Fajr prayer with the Imam at Muzdalifah and staying until departure. This hadith also establishes that standing at Arafat earlier—whether by night or day—is sufficient, but Muzdalifah standing is required. The Hanafi ruling is that standing at Muzdalifah for any length of time after Fajr until sunrise is wajib; if omitted, a dam is due. This passage follows the standard format: the listing of additional Hajj obligations (ramy, dhabh, halq) serves as a thematic introduction before providing the evidence for Muzdalifah.

Key Terms
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A sacred plain between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night after Arafat and stand after Fajr on the 10th.
مشعر حرام (al-Mash'ar al-Haram): The Sacred Monument, identified by Hanafis as Muzdalifah.

Stoning the Jamarat (Ramy al-Jimar) – Wajib and Its Proofs
Ruling with proof for wajib stoning of the pillars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that ramy al-jimar is wajib in Hanafi fiqh, cite the two proofs (hadith of Jabir and athar of 'Ata), and apply the consequence (dam) when ramy is omitted.

Core Idea
Ramy al-Jimar is wajib; omission incurs dam—proved by the Prophet's action and a companion's ruling.

In this passage, the author establishes the legal status of stoning the Jamarat (ramy al-jimar) during Hajj. While the ruling is not explicitly stated as 'wajib', the two proofs cited—the Prophet's stoning in the hadith of Jabir and the statement of 'Ata ibn Abi Rabah—clearly indicate wujub according to Hanafi usul. Understanding these proofs helps us grasp why a dam is required if stoning is missed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and what hukm the Hanafi school assigns to it. Look for the term 'ramy al-jimar' and note the implication of dam for omission.
The text does not say 'wajib' explicitly but uses proofs that establish wujub.
2
Analyze the first proof – Hadith of Jabir
Read the hadith describing the Prophet's stoning. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action (fi'l) in a teaching context indicates wujub. Identify the key phrase: 'he threw seven pebbles, saying Allahu Akbar with each.'
The hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Analyze the second proof – Athar of 'Ata
Consider the statement of the tabi'i 'Ata: 'Whoever forgets one Jamrah... one dam suffices him.' The ruling that dam is owed for omission is taken as proof that the act is wajib, because dam is only for wajib.
4
Conclude the Hanafi position
Combine the two proofs: the Prophet's action shows the act is required; the companion's statement shows the consequence of omission. Therefore, ramy is wajib and leaving it requires dam.

Translation: (1240) [4] Throwing pebbles at the Jamarat. Proof: (1) In this hadith also: 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... Then he took the middle path that leads to the great Jamrah, until he reached the Jamrah by the tree, and he threw at it with seven pebbles, saying Allahu Akbar with each pebble.' (Muslim, Abu Dawud) From this hadith it is understood that one should throw. (2) In this saying of a companion, that if one leaves the throwing, then a dam (sacrificial animal) will be necessary, which proves obligation: 'Ata ibn Abi Rabah said: Whoever forgets one Jamrah or all the Jamarat until the days of Tashriq have passed, then one dam suffices him.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) From this athar it is understood that if one leaves the throwing, a dam will be necessary.

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on ramy al-jimar (stoning the pillars). The author states the ruling without explicitly saying 'wajib' but the proofs indicate wujub. Two items of evidence: (1) The hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's stoning at the Jamrah near the tree with seven pebbles, glorifying Allah each time. The Prophet's action (fi'l) here, performed in the context of hajj instructions, is taken by Hanafis as indicating wujub (al-fi'l yufid al-wujub when done as a public demonstration). (2) The statement (qawl) of the successor 'Ata ibn Abi Rabah, which is cited as proof that skipping ramy incurs a dam. Although 'Ata is a tabi'i, not a Sahaba, his statement is used as evidence because it reflects the understanding of earlier generation. The ruling: ramy is wajib in Hanafi fiqh; leaving it requires dam.

رمي الجمار (ramy al-jimar): Throwing small pebbles at the three pillars (Jamarat) in Mina during Hajj.
دم (dam): Sacrificial animal offered as compensation for an omitted wajib in Hajj.

Standing at Muzdalifah is Wajib
Establishes obligation of standing at Muzdalifah with Quran and Hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing at Muzdalifah, cite the Quranic and Hadith proofs, and explain why it is wajib not fard.

Core Idea
Standing at Muzdalifah is wajib; omission requires dam but does not invalidate Hajj.

In this lesson, we examine a key wajib of Hajj according to the Hanafi school: standing at Muzdalifah. The author provides two clear proofs—a Quranic verse with an imperative and a prophetic hadith. Understanding the distinction between fard and wajib is essential for correct practice and compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State what act is being ruled upon (standing at Muzdalifah) and its hukm level (wajib).
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the two proofs: Quran 2:198 and the hadith of Urwa ibn Mudarris.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the Quran, the imperative 'fadhkuru' indicates obligation per Hanafi usul. For the hadith, the conditional phrase shows necessity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'is consider this act sunnah, not wajib, because they interpret the command as recommended.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Hanafis rely on the principle 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub' and consider the hadith authentic, thus ruling wajib.

Commentary
This passage type is a ruling with proof. The author establishes the obligation (wujub) of standing at Muzdalifah, which is one of the wajibat of Hajj according to the Hanafi school. The proof is twofold: first, the Quranic verse (2:198) using the imperative form 'fadhkuru' (remember), which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation (wujub) when not otherwise specified. Second, the hadith of Urwa ibn Mudarris, where the Prophet explicitly makes completion of Hajj conditional upon standing at Muzdalifah. Note that the hadith text includes a request for the Prophet to state the ruling. The Hanafi position is clear: this standing is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is from a hadith ahad and the command is open to interpretation for sunnah according to some scholars, but the Hanafi school leans to wujub.

Key Terms
وقوف (wuquf): Standing or staying at a specific place during Hajj rituals, here specifically at Muzdalifah.
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims stay after departing Arafat, also known as al-Mash'ar al-Haram.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act whose omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of standing at Muzdalifah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Standing at Muzdalifah is a wajib act of Hajj in the Hanafi school; omission requires a dam but does not invalidate the pilgrimage.
