Sacrifice for Qarin and Mutamatti' is Wajib
Proves necessity of sacrifice for qarin and mutamatti' with Quran and Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hady for qarin and mutamatti', cite the Quranic and hadith proofs, and explain the qiyas that extends the ruling from tamattu' to qiran.

Core Idea
Hady is wajib for both qarin and mutamatti' because combining Hajj and Umrah in one journey triggers the obligation.

The Hanafi school uniquely holds that sacrifice (hady) is wajib not only for the mutamatti' but also for the qarin. This lesson examines the primary proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and the analogical reasoning that extends the ruling from tamattu' to qiran. Understanding this ruling clarifies a significant point of difference with other schools.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the hukm level (wajib) and who is obligated: both qarin and mutamatti'.
2
Identify the primary proof for tamattu'
Locate the Quranic verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196) and its explicit ruling that hady is required for tamattu'.
3
Recognize the absence of direct text for qiran
Note that the verse only mentions tamattu'; there is no direct scripture for qiran.
4
Apply qiyas: determine the illa
Understand the 'illa (combining Hajj and Umrah in one journey) that links qiran to tamattu'.
5
Confirm with secondary proof
Cite the hadith of Ibn Abbas (Bukhari) showing the practice of tamattu' with hady, and the inclusion of qarin by analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۲۴۲) [۵] قارن اور متمتع کو قربانی کرنا۔ تشریح : قرآن کرنے والے اور تمتع کرنے والے پر دم واجب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) قرآن تمتع کے درجے میں ہے کیونکہ قران میں بھی حج اور عمرہ ایک ہی سفر میں کیا جاتا ہے اور تمتع میں بھی ایک ہی سفر میں حج اور عمرہ کیا جاتا ہے، اور تمتع کے بارے میں آیت میں ہے کہ ہدی لازم ہے اس لئے قرآن میں بھی ہدی لازم ہوگی ۔ آیت یہ ہے - فمن تمتع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استيسر من الهدى فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام في الحج وسبعة اذا رجعتم تلك عشرة كاملة ذلك لمن لم يكن اهله حاضری المسجد الحرام . ( آیت ۹۶ اسورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ تمتع اور قرآن کرنے والے پر قربانی لازم ہے۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس انه سئل عن متعة الحج فقال ... ثم امرنا عشية التروية ان نهل بالحج فاذا فرغنا من المناسك جئنا فطفنا بالبيت وبالصفا والمروة فقد تم حجناو وعلينا الهدى كما قال الله عز وجل فما استيسر من الهدى (بخاری شریف ، باب قول الله عز وجل ذلک لمن لم یکن اهله حاضری المسجد الحرام ص ۲۱۳ نمبر ۱۵۷۲) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا مستمتع اور قارن پر ہدی لازم ہے۔
Translation: (1242) [5] The qarin and mutamatti' must sacrifice. Explanation: A dam (sacrificial animal) is wajib upon the one performing qiran and the one performing tamattu'. Evidence: (1) Qiran is on the level of tamattu' because in qiran both Hajj and Umrah are performed in one journey, and in tamattu' also Hajj and Umrah are performed in one journey, and regarding tamattu' the verse states that a hady is required, so qiran also requires a hady. The verse is: 'And whoever performs tamattu' of Umrah to Hajj, then [offer] what is easy of the hady. And whoever cannot find [a hady], then fast three days during Hajj and seven when you return; that is ten complete. That is for whoever his family is not present at al-Masjid al-Haram.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). In this verse it is stated that sacrifice is necessary for mutamatti' and qarin. (2) In the hadith: from Ibn Abbas that he was asked about tamattu' of Hajj... then he commanded us on the evening of Tarwiyah to assume ihram for Hajj. When we finished the rituals, we came and performed tawaf of the House and Safa and Marwah, so our Hajj was completed, and upon us was the hady as Allah said: '...whatever is easy of the hady.' (Bukhari, chapter: the saying of Allah 'that is for whoever his family is not present at al-Masjid al-Haram', p.213, no.1572). From this hadith it is also known that hady is obligatory on mutamatti' and qarin.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage type is a ruling with proof. The author states that both the qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) and the mutamatti' (one who performs Umrah first then Hajj) must offer a sacrifice (hady). The Hanafi proof: (1) The Quranic verse (2:196) explicitly mentions tamattu', but qarin is analogically compared to tamattu' because both involve performing Hajj and Umrah in one journey. The 'illa (effective cause) is the combination of Hajj and Umrah in one trip. (2) The hadith of Ibn Abbas shows that the Companions, when performing tamattu' under the Prophet's instruction, offered hady. Qarin is included because it is a similar combination. The Hanafi school thus considers sacrifice wajib for both.

Key Terms
قارن (qarin): A pilgrim who intends Umrah and Hajj together in one state of ihram.
متمتع (mutamatti'): A pilgrim who performs Umrah first, then after tahlul, assumes ihram for Hajj in the same year.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal offered in the Haram during Hajj as an obligation or supererogation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school consider sacrifice wajib for qarin as well?
A) Because of direct Qur'anic text
B) By analogy to tamattu' due to combining Hajj and Umrah in one journey
C) Because the Prophet ordered it for all
D) Because of a special hadith for qarin

Key Takeaway
Hady is wajib for both qarin and mutamatti' in the Hanafi school, based on the Quranic verse for tamattu' and qiyas for qiran.

Shaving the Head is Wajib with Conditions
States obligation of shaving head and specifies that it must be in Haram and during ayyam al-nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shaving the head during Hajj and identify the two conditions (in the Haram and during ayyam al-nahr) that must be met.

Core Idea
Shaving the head during Hajj is wajib and must be done in the Haram during ayyam al-nahr.

Shaving or trimming the head after pelting the jamarat is a required (wajib) act in Hajj according to the Hanafi school. However, it is not unconditionally valid; it must be performed within the sacred precincts of the Haram and on specific days. This lesson examines the textual proofs from the Quran and Sunnah that establish these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage rules upon—shaving/trimming the head—and its hukm level (wajib).
The author explicitly states 'ye wajib hai' (this is obligatory).
2
List the two conditions
Extract the two shurut: location (within Haram) and time (during ayyam al-nahr).
Conditions are also wajib; violation incurs dam.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
Find the verse (Surah al-Fath 48:27) and understand how it implies obligation.
The word 'مُحَلِّقِينَ' indicates shaving is part of the ritual.
4
Locate the hadith proof
Analyze the hadith of Anas regarding the sequence of rites; note that the order is sunnah but the act itself is wajib.
The hadith confirms the act but not the obligation of the order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۲۴۲) [۶] سرمنڈوانا ( یا بال کٹوانا ) -[۷] اور اس کو خاص حرم میں اور ایام محر میں کرنا۔ تشريح : کنکری مارنے کے بعد سرمنڈوائے ، یا بال کتروائے یہ واجب ہے، اور اس میں دوشرطیں ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ حدود حرم میں حلق کرائے ، [۲] اور دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ ایام نحر میں ہو، یعنی ذی الحجہ کی دسویں تاریخ سے بارہویں تاریخ تک حلق کرائے۔ وجه : (۱) حلق کرانے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے ۔ لتدخلن المسجد الحرام ان شاء الله آمنين محلقين رء وسكم و مقصرین . ( آیت ۲۷ ، سورة الفتح ۴۸) اس آیت میں اشارہ ہے کہ عمرہ یا حج کے بعد حلق کرائے یا قصر کرائے ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن انس بن مالک ان رسول الله صلى الله له أتى منى فأتى الجمرة فرما ها ثم أتى منزله بمنى و نحر ثم قال للحلاق خذ و أشار الى جانبه الأيمن ، ثم الايسر ثم جعل يعطيه الناس ۔(مسلم شریف، باب السنة يوم النحر ان برمی ثم سحر ثم تحلق ، ص ۵۴۸، نمبر ۳۱۵۲/۱۳۰۵ ابوداود شریف ، باب الحلق والتقصیر ، ص ۲۸۸، نمبر (۱۹۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلے رمی کی پھر ہدی ذبح کیا پھر حلق کروایا، اس لئے یہ ترتیب سنت ہے۔
Translation: (1242) [6] Shaving the head (or cutting the hair) - [7] And making it specific to the Haram and the days of Nahr. Explanation: After pelting the jamarat, he should shave his head or trim his hair; this is wajib. And there are two conditions: [1] That he shaves within the boundaries of the Haram, [2] And the second condition is that it be in the days of Nahr, i.e., from the 10th of Dhul Hijjah to the 12th of Dhul Hijjah. Evidence: (1) The proof for shaving is this verse: 'You will surely enter al-Masjid al-Haram, if Allah wills, in safety, with your heads shaved or hair shortened.' (Surah al-Fath 48:27). This verse indicates that after Umrah or Hajj one should shave or shorten. (2) In this hadith: from Anas ibn Malik that the Messenger of Allah came to Mina, then came to the jamrah and pelted it, then came to his residence in Mina and sacrificed, then said to the barber: 'Take' and pointed to his right side, then left, then started giving [hair] to the people. (Muslim, chapter: the sunnah on the day of Nahr is to pelt, then sacrifice, then shave, p.548, no.3152/1305; Abu Dawud, chapter: shaving and shortening, p.288, no.198). In this hadith, he first pelted, then sacrificed the hady, then shaved; therefore this order is sunnah.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage type is a ruling with proof covering two wajibat: shaving the head and its specification to the Haram and ayyam al-nahr. The author states that shaving (or trimming) the head is wajib after pelting the jamarat. Additionally, it must be done within the boundaries of the Haram (the sacred area around Makkah) and during the days of Nahr (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah). The first proof is from Surah al-Fath (48:27), where the Prophet and companions are described entering Makkah with shaved or shortened heads, implying this is a required act. The second proof is the hadith of Anas which shows the Prophet pelting, sacrificing, then shaving — this demonstrates the act itself. The mention of 'sunnah' for the order (first rami, then nahr, then halq) refers to the preferred sequence, but the act of halq itself is wajib.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely as a ritual of Hajj/Umrah.
ايام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The days of sacrifice: 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Valid, no penalty
B) Valid but requires dam
C) Hajj invalid
D) Must repeat halq in Haram

Key Takeaway
Shaving the head after pelting is a wajib act of Hajj that must be performed within the Haram and during the days of Nahr; violation incurs a penalty but does not invalidate the Hajj.

The Order of Hajj Rituals: Wajib or Sunnah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wajib vs sunnah order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the order of rami, nahr, and halq, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The order of rami, nahr, and halq is sunnah according to the current Hanafi fatwa.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sequence of three essential Hajj rituals on the Day of Nahr: pelting, sacrifice, and shaving. Understanding the difference between wajib and sunnah here has practical consequences: if you reverse the order, does a penalty apply? The passage presents the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two illustrious students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and explains why later scholars chose the latter's view for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Acts
The three acts on the Day of Nahr are: rami (pelting the Jamarat), nahr (sacrifice for a qarin or mutamatti'), and halq (shaving the head). Abu Hanifa prescribes the order as rami → nahr → halq.
These acts are performed on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the order is wajib. If a pilgrim reverses the order, he must offer a dam (penalty) to compensate for the missing wajib.
Wajib here means an obligation that does not invalidate the Hajj but requires compensation if omitted.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the order is sunnah, not wajib. If reversed, no dam is required because the acts remain valid regardless of sequence.
Sunnah means recommended but not obligatory.
4
Compare the Proofs
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of Anas that shows the Prophet's sequence. The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Ibn Abbas in Sahih al-Bukhari where the Prophet replied 'la haraj' (no harm) to a man who performed the acts out of order.
The hadith of Ibn Abbas explicitly permits changing the order.
5
Identify the Mufta Bihi
Today, due to overcrowding and ease, scholars give fatwa according to the Sahibayn's view: the order is sunnah and no penalty for reversal.
This is a clear example of tarjih based on necessity (hajah) and the principle of taysir (facilitation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۴۳) [۸] رمی کو حلق سے مقدم کرنا۔ [9] قارن اور متمتع کا نحر کرنا رمی اور حلق کے درمیان۔ تشریح مام ابو حنیفہ کا مسلک یہی ہے کہ پہلے رمی ہو، پھر تمتع کرنے والا یا قران کرنے والا جانور ذبح کرے، اور اس کے بعد حلق کرائے اور یہ ترتیب واجب ہے اس کے خلاف کرنے میں دم لازم ہوگا ، البتہ صاحبین کے یہاں یہ ترتیب سنت ہے اس لئے اس کے خلاف کرنے میں دم لازم نہیں ہوگا، اور آج کل بہت بھیڑ کی وجہ سے اسی پر علماء فتوی دیتے ہیں دونوں کی دلیل او پر کی حدیث ہے وجه : صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ ترتیب سنت ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عباس قال رجل للنبي الله زرت قبل ان ارمي قال لا حرج قال حلقت قبل ان اذبح قال لا حرج قال ذبحت قبل ان ارمى قال لا حرج ( بخاری شریف، باب الذبح قبل الحلق ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۷۲۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مقدم مؤخر کر نے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
Translation: (1343) [8] Precedence of rami over halq. [9] The qarin and mutamatti' perform nahr between rami and halq. Explanation: Imam Abu Hanifa's position is that first rami should be done, then the mutamatti' or qarin should slaughter the animal, and then he should shave; and this order is wajib. Doing contrary to it requires a dam. However, according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), this order is sunnah, so doing contrary to it does not require a dam. And today, due to severe crowding, scholars give fatwa on this (Sahibayn's view). The evidence for both is the aforementioned hadith. Evidence: The Sahibayn say that the order is sunnah, and their proof is this hadith: from Abbas that a man said to the Prophet: 'I visited (the House) before pelting.' He said: 'No harm.' He said: 'I shaved before slaughtering.' He said: 'No harm.' He said: 'I slaughtered before pelting.' He said: 'No harm.' (Bukhari, chapter: slaughtering before shaving, p.278, no.1722). In this hadith, there is no harm in giving precedence or delaying.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The issue is the order of three acts on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah: ramy al-jamar (pelting), nahr (sacrifice for qarin/mutamatti'), and halq (shaving). Imam Abu Hanifa considers the order (rami → nahr → halq) wajib; violating it requires dam. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider the order sunnah, not wajib, because the hadith from Ibn Abbas (narrated by his freedman) explicitly states that there is no harm (la haraj) in changing the order. The hadith referred to as 'the aforementioned' is likely the hadith of Anas showing the Prophet's sequence, which Abu Hanifa uses to establish wujub. The Sahibayn argue that the la haraj hadith overrides that. The current operative fatwa in later scholarship (particularly due to overcrowding) is the view of the Sahibayn, i.e., the order is sunnah and no dam for reversal.

Key Terms
ترتیب (tartib): The prescribed sequence of Hajj rituals (rami, nahr, halq) on the day of Nahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the current fatwa in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reversing the order of rami, nahr, and halq?
A) Invalid (batil)
B) Requires dam
C) Permissible (mubah) with no penalty
D) Requires repetition

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the order of rami, nahr, and halq is sunnah by the operative fatwa, meaning no penalty for reversal, due to the Sahibayn's reliance on the 'la haraj' hadith and the need for ease.

The Time Limit for Tawaf al-Ziyarah in the Hanafi School
States the time limit for tawaf al-ziyarah and the consequence of delay.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time limit for tawaf al-ziyarah according to Imam Abu Hanifa, identify the Quranic evidence, and explain the consequence of delay.

Core Idea
Delaying tawaf al-ziyarah beyond the 13th of Dhul Hijjah requires a dam.

In this lesson, we examine the precise time frame for performing the obligatory tawaf of Hajj, known as tawaf al-ziyarah or tawaf al-ifadah. The Hanafi school, based on Imam Abu Hanifa's understanding of the Quranic indication, restricts its performance to the days of Nahr (10th-13th Dhul Hijjah). Delaying beyond this period does not invalidate the Hajj but incurs an obligation of dam. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the interaction between wajib acts and their prescribed times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tawaf al-ziyarah is a wajib act of Hajj. Its prescribed time is restricted to ayyam al-nahr (10th-13th Dhul Hijjah).
Tawaf al-ziyarah is sometimes called tawaf al-ifadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 22:28, 'li yashhadu manafi'a lahum' (that they may witness benefits for themselves), is cited as an indication (isharah al-nass) for the specific time frame.
The verse is not quoted in full but alluded to.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The 'benefits' refer to the Hajj rituals, including tawaf, which are confined to specific days.
This is a zanni (probable) indication.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers tawaf al-ziyarah a rukn with no time limit except one's lifetime; no dam for delay.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school; delay beyond ayyam al-nahr requires dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۴۴)[۱۰] طواف زیارت کو ایام نحر میں کرنا۔ تشریح : طواف زیارت کا وقت دسویں تاریخ کی فجر کے وقت سے شروع ہوتا ہے، اور بارویں ذی الحجہ کے بعد جو شام ہے، یعنی تیرویں تاریخ کی شام وہاں تک وقت رہتا ہے، اس کے بعد مؤخر کرنا مکروہ ہے، چنانچہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی رائے ہے کہ ایام انخر کے بعد کوئی طواف زیارت کرے گا تو اس پر دم لازم ہوگا۔ وجه : (۱) دسویں سے شروع ہوتا ہے اور بارہویں تک رہتا ہے اس کے لئے اس آیت کا اشارة النص ہے۔ ليشهدوا منفع
Translation: (1344) [10] Performing tawaf al-ziyarah during the days of Nahr. Explanation: The time for tawaf al-ziyarah begins from the Fajr of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, and the time remains until the evening after the 12th of Dhul Hijjah, i.e., the evening of the 13th. After that, delaying it is makruh. Consequently, Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion is that if someone performs tawaf al-ziyarah after the days of Nahr, he must offer a dam. Evidence: (1) It begins from the 10th and lasts until the 12th; for this, the verse gives an indication: 'that they may witness benefits for themselves' (Surah al-Hajj 22:28).
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage type is a ruling with proof. The author states that tawaf al-ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf of Hajj) must be performed during the days of Nahr (10th-13th Dhul Hijjah). The beginning time is Fajr of the 10th, and it ends at the sunset of the 13th (i.e., the evening after the 12th). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if one delays it beyond this period, a dam becomes necessary. The proof is an indication (isharah al-nass) from the verse 'that they may witness benefits for themselves' from Surah al-Hajj, which suggests the specific time frame for completing the Hajj rituals, including tawaf. The verse is not directly quoted but alluded to. The ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that delaying a wajib act (tawaf) beyond its prescribed time requires compensation.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf of Hajj performed after returning from Mina; also called tawaf al-ifadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if tawaf al-ziyarah is performed after the 13th of Dhul Hijjah according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Valid, no penalty
B) Valid but requires dam
C) Invalid, must repeat Hajj
D) Makruh but no dam

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-ziyarah must be performed within the days of Nahr (10th-13th Dhul Hijjah); delay requires a dam according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

The Order of Hajj Rituals: Wajib or Sunnah? An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on order of Hajj rites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the order of ramy, sacrifice, and halq, and explain the hadith evidence each side uses.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, the order is wajib; for the Sahibayn it is sunnah — and today's fatwa follows the lenient view.

Hajj involves a sequence of rites: stoning the Jamrah (ramy), sacrificing an animal (for qarin/mutamatti), and shaving or trimming the hair (halq). This passage explores an internal Hanafi disagreement: is this sequence obligatory (wajib) or merely recommended (sunnah)? Understanding this dispute will help you appreciate how legal rulings adapt to practical circumstances without abandoning the core of the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rites and the prescribed order
List the three actions: ramy (stoning the Jamrah), nahr/sacrifice (only for qarin/mutamatti), and halq (shaving). According to the Hanafi school, the preferred order is ramy, then sacrifice, then halq.
This order is based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as reported by Anas (mentioned earlier in the text).
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and its evidence
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that this order is wajib. Violating it (e.g., shaving before stoning) requires a dam (blood penalty). His evidence is the consistent practice of the Prophet ﷺ, which indicates obligation.
For Abu Hanifa, the Prophet's consistent actions can indicate wujub unless there is evidence to the contrary.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their evidence
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider the order sunnah, not wajib. They cite the hadith of 'Abbas where the Prophet said 'No harm' when a pilgrim performed rites out of order. This permits flexibility.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari (no. 1722). The Sahibayn interpret the 'no harm' statement as removing any obligation of sequence.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical consequence is whether a dam is required when the order is changed. For Abu Hanifa, dam is wajib; for the Sahibayn, no dam is needed. This difference affects the pilgrim's financial and ritual obligations.
Thamarah al-khilaf shows how usul differences affect fiqh outcomes.
5
Understand the contemporary tarjih and its basis
The text states that due to crowding (especially today), scholars issue fatwa according to the Sahibayn's view, making the order sunnah and not requiring a dam. This reflects the principle of takhfif (easing) based on necessity.
Tarjih here is based on practicality and preventing hardship, not on rejecting Abu Hanifa's evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۴۳) [۸] رمی کو حلق سے مقدم کرنا۔ [9] قارن اور متمتع کا نحر کرنا رمی اور حلق کے درمیان۔ تشریح : امام ابو حنیفہ کا مسلک یہی ہے کہ پہلے رمی ہو، پھر تمتع کرنے والا یا قران کرنے والا جانور ذبح کرے، اور اس کے بعد حلق کرائے اور یہ ترتیب واجب ہے اس کے خلاف کرنے میں دم لازم ہوگا ، البتہ صاحبین کے یہاں یہ ترتیب سنت ہے اس لئے اس کے خلاف کرنے میں دم لازم نہیں ہوگا، اور آج کل بہت بھیڑ کی وجہ سے اسی پر علماء فتوی دیتے ہیں دونوں کی دلیل او پر کی حدیث ہے وجه : صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ ترتیب سنت ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عباس قال رجل للنبي الله زرت قبل ان ارمي قال لا حرج قال حلقت قبل ان يذبح قال لا حرج قال ذبحت قبل ان ارمى قال لا حرج ( بخاری شریف، باب الذبح قبل الحلق ، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۱۷۲۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مقدم مؤخر کر نے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
Translation: (1243) [8] Giving precedence to ramy (stoning) over halq (shaving). [9] For the qarin and mutamatti, sacrificing (nahr) between ramy and halq. Explanation: The position of Imam Abu Hanifah is that first ramy is performed, then the mutamatti or qarin sacrifices the animal, and after that shaves, and this order is wajib (obligatory); violating it requires a dam (blood penalty). However, according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), this order is sunnah, so violating it does not require a dam. And nowadays due to crowding, scholars give fatwa based on this. Their evidence is the same hadith above. Evidence: The Sahibayn say the order is sunnah; their evidence is this hadith: From 'Abbas: A man said to the Prophet ﷺ, 'I visited (the House) before stoning,' he said, 'No harm.' He said, 'I shaved before sacrificing,' he said, 'No harm.' He said, 'I sacrificed before stoning,' he said, 'No harm.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Dhabh qabl al-Halq, p. 278, no. 1722) This hadith indicates that there is no harm in giving precedence or postponing.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the order of three rites: ramy (stoning the Jamrah), sacrifice (nahr for qarin/mutamatti), and halq (shaving). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the sequence is obligatory: ramy first, then sacrifice, then halq. Violating this order necessitates a dam. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider this order sunnah, not wajib, so no penalty for changing the order. They cite a hadith from 'Abbas where the Prophet allowed various orders without harm. The text notes that due to crowding in modern times, scholars issue fatwa according to the Sahibayn's view. This reflects the principle of taking the easier option (takhfif) when conditions require it.

Key Terms
قارن (qarin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah together with one ihram.
متمتع (mutamatti): One who performs Umrah first, then Hajj with a separate ihram, and is obliged to offer a hady.
رمی (ramy): Stoning the Jamrah (pillar) during Hajj.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head (or trimming) as part of the exit from ihram.
نحر (nahr): Sacrificing an animal (camel) at the place of slaughter in Mina; also refers to the act of sacrifice in general.
دم (dam): Blood penalty; a sacrificial animal required for violating a wajib of Hajj.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf (d. 182 AH) and Muhammad al-Shaybani (d. 189 AH), the two principal disciples of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the ruling if someone shaves before stoning?
A) He must sacrifice an additional animal
B) He must repeat the shaving
C) No penalty is required
D) His Hajj is invalid

Key Takeaway
The order of ramy, sacrifice, and halq is sunnah according to the relied-upon Hanafi view; no penalty for changing the order under current circumstances.

Timing of Tawaf al-Ziyarah and Penalty for Delay
Explains the time for tawaf al-zafar (ifada) and the penalty for delaying beyond Ayyam al-Nahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah and explain the ruling when it is delayed beyond Ayyam al-Nahr.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Ziyarah must be performed from Fajr 10th to sunset 13th; delay requires a dam.

Tawaf al-Ziyarah, also known as Tawaf al-Ifadah, is an essential pillar of Hajj. Its performance is not open-ended; the Hanafi school specifies a precise window from dawn on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah until the evening of the 13th. Delaying beyond this time carries a specific penalty, a dam. This lesson will examine the textual evidence, primarily the Quranic verse, hadith, and the statement of Ibn Abbas, that establish both the timing and the penalty. Understanding this ruling is crucial for ensuring one's Hajj is correctly performed without incurring extra obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act being discussed: Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah). What is its legal status? It is a rukn of Hajj, but the timing requirement is wajib.
Distinguish between the tawaf itself (rukn) and its timing (wajib).
2
Note the specified time window
The time begins at Fajr on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and extends until the evening of the 13th (i.e., after sunset on the 12th). Delaying beyond that is makruh and incurs a dam.
The evening of the 13th means the end of the 12th after Maghrib? Actually, the text says 'after the 12th, which is the evening of the 13th' – i.e., the night before the 13th.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Surah al-Hajj (22:28-29) contains 'then let them complete their rites and perform Tawaf.' The coupling of 'eat' (from sacrifice) and 'perform Tawaf' implies Tawaf follows sacrifice, and sacrifice occurs during Ayyam al-Nahr. Thus Tawaf al-Ziyarah should be during those days.
The argument is from the order: first sacrifice, then tawaf.
4
Examine the hadith evidence
Two hadith are cited: (a) Umm Salamah performed ifadah after stoning before Fajr on the night of Nahr. (b) The Prophet ﷺ performed ifadah on Yawm al-Nahr then prayed Dhuhr in Mina. Both show the tawaf was done on the 10th.
These act as proof that the time permits from early morning on the 10th.
5
Understand the penalty for delay
The statement of Ibn Abbas: 'Whoever advances or delays anything from his Hajj should shed blood for that' is used to establish that delaying beyond the specified time requires a dam (sacrifice).
This is a qawl sahabi, which is a valid source in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۴۴)[۱۰] طواف زیارت کو ایام نحر میں کرنا۔ تشریح : طواف زیارت کا وقت دسویں تاریخ کی فجر کے وقت سے شروع ہوتا ہے، اور بارویں ذی الحجہ کے بعد جو شام ہے، یعنی تیرویں تاریخ کی شام وہاں تک وقت رہتا ہے، اس کے بعد مؤخر کرنا مکروہ ہے، چنانچہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی رائے ہے کہ ایام انخر کے بعد کوئی طواف زیارت کرے گا تو اس پر دم لازم ہوگا۔ وجه : (۱) دسویں سے شروع ہوتا ہے اور بارہویں تک رہتا ہے اس کے لئے اس آیت کا اشارة النص ہے۔ ليشهدوا منفع و يذكروا أسم الله في أيام معلومات على ما رزقهم من بهيمة الأنعام فكلوا منها و أطعموا البائس الفقير ثم ليقضوا تفثهم و ليوفوا نذورهم و ليطوفوا بالبيت العتيق - ( آیت ۲۹ ،سورۃ الحج ۲۲) اس آیت میں کلوا پر و ليطوفوا کا عطف ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ پہلے ذبح کرو پھر طواف کرو، اور ذبیح ایام نحر میں ہوتا ہے اس لئے طواف زیارت بھی اس کے بعد ہوگا ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ رمی جمار کے بعد طواف کرے۔ عن عائشة أنها قالت أرسل النبي الا الله علي بأم سلمة ليلة النحر فرمت الجمرة قبل الفجر ثم مضت فأفاضت ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب التجميل من جمع ص ۲۸۴، نمبر ۱۹۴۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ام سلمہ فجر کے وقت طواف زیارت کے لئے چل پڑی۔(۳) اس حدیث میں حضور نے یوم انحر میں طواف زیارت کیا۔ عن ابن عمران رسول الله الا الله افاض يوم النحر ثم رجع فصلى الظهر بمنى ( مسلم شریف باب استحباب طواف الا فاضتہ یوم انخر ،ص۵۵۰، نمبر ۳۱۶۵/۱۳۰۸ رابو داؤد شریف ، باب الا فاضتہ فی الحج ص ۲۸۱ نمبر ۱۹۹۸) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ آپ نے طواف دسویں ذی الحجہ کو کیا ہے۔ (۴) اور ایام محر سے موخر کرنے سے دم لازم ہوگا اس کے لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ عن عباس قال من قدم شيئا من حجه او اخره فليهرق لذلك دما (مصنف ابن ابی شيبہ ،۳۵۳ في الرجل تحلق قبل ان يذبح، ج ثالث ص ۱۳۴۵، نمبر ۱۴۹۵۴) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وقت سے مؤخر کیا تو دم لازم ہوگا
Translation: (1244) [10] Performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah during the days of Nahr. Explanation: The time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah begins at Fajr on the 10th (Dhul Hijjah), and lasts until the evening after the 12th, i.e., the evening of the 13th. Delaying it after that is makruh. Accordingly, Imam Abu Hanifah's opinion is that if one performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah after the days of Nahr, a dam is required. Evidence: (1) For it starting from the 10th and lasting until the 12th, there is a textual indication in this verse: 'That they may witness benefits for themselves and mention the name of Allah on known days over what He has provided for them of [sacrificial] animals. So eat of them and feed the miserable poor. Then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows and perform Tawaf around the Ancient House.' (Surah al-Hajj 22:28-29) In this verse, 'then let them perform Tawaf' is coupled with 'eat.' The meaning is that first you sacrifice, then perform Tawaf, and sacrifice occurs during the days of Nahr, so Tawaf al-Ziyarah must also be after that. (2) In this hadith, he performed Tawaf after stoning the Jamrah: From 'Aishah that she said: The Prophet ﷺ sent Umm Salamah on the night of Nahr, so she stoned the Jamrah before Fajr and then went and performed Ifadah (Tawaf al-Ziyarah). (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Tajmil min Jam', p. 284, no. 1941) (3) In this hadith, the Prophet performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah on Yawm al-Nahr: From Ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed Ifadah on Yawm al-Nahr, then returned and prayed Dhuhr in Mina. (Muslim, Bab Istihbab Tawaf al-Ifadah Yawm al-Nahr, p. 550, no. 3165/1308; Abu Dawud, Bab al-Ifadah fi al-Hajj, p. 281, no. 1998) (4) For the penalty of delaying beyond the days of Nahr, there is the statement of a Companion: From 'Abbas: He said, 'Whoever advances or delays anything from his Hajj should shed blood for that.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 353, fi al-Rajul yahliqu qabla an yadhabha, vol. 3, p. 1345, no. 14954) This shows that delaying beyond the time requires a dam.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the timing of Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah). According to Imam Abu Hanifah, the time for this tawaf begins at dawn on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and extends until the evening of the 13th (i.e., after sunset on the 12th). Performing it after this period is makruh and requires a dam (sacrifice). The evidence includes: 1) A Quranic verse from Surah al-Hajj which indicates that Tawaf follows sacrifice, and sacrifice is during the days of Nahr. 2) A hadith where Umm Salamah performed Tawaf after stoning before Fajr on the night of Nahr. 3) A hadith that the Prophet performed Tawaf on Yawm al-Nahr and then prayed Dhuhr in Mina. 4) The statement of Ibn 'Abbas that advancing or delaying any rite requires blood. This establishes the penalty for delay.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory circumambulation around the Kaaba performed after standing at Arafah, also called Tawaf al-Ifadah.
ايام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The days of sacrifice: 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A dam is required

D) No penalty

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Ziyarah has a fixed time from Fajr of 10th to evening of 13th Dhul Hijjah; delaying beyond that necessitates a dam but does not invalidate the Hajj.

Conditions of Sa'y between Safa and Marwah
Ruling with proof for four wajib conditions of Sa'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four wajib conditions of Sa'y and apply them to determine the validity of a Sa'y.

Core Idea
Sa'y requires four wajib conditions: timing, sequence after Tawaf, walking, and starting from Safa.

Sa'y between Safa and Marwah is a wajib rite of Hajj and Umrah in the Hanafi school. This lesson examines the four conditions that must be fulfilled for the Sa'y to be valid: it must be performed during the months of Hajj, after a valid Tawaf, by walking if able, and beginning from Safa. Understanding these conditions is essential for correct performance and to avoid the need for a compensatory sacrifice (dam).

Guided Path
1
Identify the four wajib conditions
From the text, list the four conditions explicitly stated: (1) Sa'y must be in the months of Hajj, (2) after a valid Tawaf, (3) by walking for those without excuse, (4) starting from Safa.
These are referred to as 'چهار واجبات' (four wajibat) in the Urdu text.
2
Understand the evidential basis
Match each condition to its proof. The general obligation of Sa'y is from Quran 2:158. The sequence after Tawaf and starting from Safa are from the Prophet's practice (hadith of Jabir). Walking is based on the general default of the act.
The hadith is incomplete in the text but establishes the order.
3
Apply the conditions to scenarios
Consider cases: (a) Sa'y performed on 8th Dhul Hijjah after Tawaf al-Qudum – valid. (b) Sa'y performed before any Tawaf – invalid, must be repeated. (c) Sa'y performed while riding without excuse – invalid, requires dam unless repeated.
The text explicitly says Sa'y before Tawaf is invalid.
4
Recognize the Hanafi distinction
Note that these conditions are wajib, not rukn. In the Hanafi school, omission of a wajib during Hajj requires a dam but does not invalidate the Hajj itself, unlike a rukn.
This contrasts with schools that consider Sa'y a rukn.

ترجمه : (۱۳۴۵) [۱۱] صفا مروہ کی سعی حج کے مہینوں میں کرنا۔ [۱۲] اس سعی کا طواف معتبر کے بعد ہونا۔ [۱۳] غیر معذور کے لئے چل کر سعی کرنا ۔ [۱۴] سعی کا صفا سے شروع کرنا۔ تشریح : یہاں سعی کے بارے میں چار واجبات بیان کئے ہیں۔ [11] حج کے لئے صفا اور مروہ کی سعی حج کے مہینوں میں کرے - [۱۲] سعی کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ احرام باندھ کر طواف کرے، چاہے ، طواف قدوم ہو، یا نفلی طواف ہو، یا طواف زیارت ہواس کے بعد سعی کرے تب اس سعی کا اعتبار ہے، اور اگر سعی کر لی پھر احرام باندھا تو اس سعی کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، یا احرام باندھا اور طواف کئے بغیر سعی کر لی تب بھی اس سعی کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے طواف کیا پھر صفا اور مروہ پر چڑھے۔[۱۳] جو معذور نہیں ہے وہ چل کر سعی کرے یہ بھی واجب ہے [۱۴] اور چوتھا واجب یہ ہے کہ سعی صفا سے شروع کرے اور مروہ پر ختم کرے، کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے کہ ہم وہاں سے شروع کریں گے جہاں سے اللہ نے شروع کیا، یعنی صفا سے سعی شروع کریں گے اس لئے صفا سے شروع کرنا بھی واجب ہے۔ وجه : (۱) سعی کرنا واجب ہے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ان الصفا والمروة من شـعـائـر الله فمن حج البيت او اعتمر فلا جناح عليه ان يطوف بهما (آیت ۱۵۸ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کرنا چاہئے (۲) ان چاروں باتوں کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ...
Translation: (1245) [11] Performing Sa'y between Safa and Marwah during the months of Hajj. [12] This Sa'y must be after a valid Tawaf. [13] Walking in Sa'y for those who are not excused. [14] Starting Sa'y from Safa. Explanation: Here four obligatory things for Sa'y are mentioned. [11] For Hajj, perform Sa'y between Safa and Marwah during the months of Hajj. [12] The method of Sa'y is to put on Ihram, perform Tawaf – whether Tawaf al-Qudum, or a voluntary Tawaf, or Tawaf al-Ziyarah – and then perform Sa'y; then that Sa'y is valid. But if one performs Sa'y first and then puts on Ihram, that Sa'y is not valid; or if one puts on Ihram and performs Sa'y without Tawaf, that Sa'y is also not valid, because in the hadith, he (ﷺ) performed Tawaf and then ascended Safa and Marwah. [13] One who is not excused should walk during Sa'y – this is also wajib. [14] The fourth wajib is that Sa'y should start from Safa and end at Marwah, because the hadith states, 'We will start from where Allah started,' i.e., start Sa'y from Safa. So starting from Safa is also wajib. Evidence: (1) Sa'y is wajib; its proof is this verse: 'Indeed, as-Safa and al-Marwah are among the symbols of Allah. So whoever performs Hajj or Umrah, there is no blame upon him to perform Tawaf between them.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:158) This verse indicates that Sa'y should be performed between Safa and Marwah. (2) For these four matters, there is a hadith: He said, 'We entered upon Jabir ibn 'Abdillah...' (the hadith is incomplete in the text).
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage enumerates four obligatory conditions for Sa'y (the walking between Safa and Marwah) during Hajj. First, it must be performed in the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah). Second, it must be preceded by a valid Tawaf (whether it is Tawaf al-Qudum, a voluntary Tawaf, or Tawaf al-Ziyarah). If one performs Sa'y before any Tawaf, or without Ihram, it is not considered valid. Third, those who are physically able must walk during Sa'y; riding is permissible only for those with a valid excuse. Fourth, Sa'y must begin from Safa and end at Marwah, following the Prophet's practice. The primary evidence is the Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah which establishes the legitimacy of Sa'y, and the hadith of Jabir (quoted partially) describing the Prophet's actions.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): The ritual walking between the hills of Safa and Marwah during Hajj or Umrah.
طواف معتد به (tawaf mu'tadd bihi): A valid circumambulation that is counted for the purpose of Sa'y; includes obligatory or supererogatory Tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing Sa'y before any Tawaf?
A) It is valid but disliked
B) It is not valid
C) It is valid if done in Ihram
D) It requires an additional dam

Key Takeaway
Sa'y has four wajib conditions: timing in Hajj months, after valid Tawaf, walking if able, and starting from Safa.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

6 min
The Four Wajibat of Sa'i Between Safa and Marwah
States four wajibat of Sa'i with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four wajibat of Sa'i, explain their evidence from Quran and Hadith, and apply them to evaluate the validity of a Sa'i scenario.

Core Idea
Four wajibat of Sa'i: after tawaf, in Hajj months, walking, start at Safa. Omission requires dam.

This passage presents the four wajibat of Sa'i as taught by Imam Abu Hanifa. Understanding these conditions is essential for performing Hajj and Umrah correctly. The passage also provides the proofs from Quran and Sunnah, showing how the Hanafi school derives these obligations from the Prophet's practice and explicit texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sa'i is the ritual walking between Safa and Marwah. In the Hanafi school, its hukm level is wajib (obligatory), not fard. Determine what this means for the pilgrim.
Wajib means omission requires compensation (dam), but does not invalidate Hajj/Umrah entirely.
2
List the four wajibat
From the text, extract the four obligatory conditions for a valid Sa'i. They are: (1) timing during Hajj months, (2) after a valid tawaf, (3) walking for the able, (4) beginning at Safa.
Each wajib is derived from the Prophet's practice and has a specific proof.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse (2:158) removes blame for performing Sa'i. Explain how the Hanafi school uses this verse to establish obligation via the Prophet's consistent practice.
The phrase 'la junah' indicates permissibility, but obligation is from sunnah.
4
Examine the Hadith proofs
The hadith of Jabir shows the Prophet performed Sa'i after tawaf, walking, starting from Safa, during Hajj. Other hadith specify seven circuits and the timing. Connect each hadith to a specific wajib.
The hadith of Umm Salamah confirms tawaf after stoning, and Ibn Abbas mentions dam for delaying.
5
Determine consequences of omission
If a wajib is omitted intentionally or forgetfully, the Sa'i is deficient. The text cites a companion's saying that delaying beyond its time requires a dam. Understand the general rule: any omitted wajib in Sa'i requires dam.
The dam is a sheep sacrifice, and the Sa'i must be repeated if possible within the Hajj days.

كتاب الحج (۱۲۴۵) والسعى بين الصفا والمروة فى اشهر الحج وحصوله بعد طواف معتد به والمشى فيه لمن لا عذر له وبداءة السعى من الصفا ... (آیت ۲۹ ،سورۃ الحج ۲۲) اس آیت میں کلوا پر و ليطوفوا کا عطف ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ پہلے ذبح کرو پھر طواف کرو، اور ذبیح ایام نحر میں ہوتا ہے اس لئے طواف زیارت بھی اس کے بعد ہوگا ۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ رمی جمار کے بعد طواف کرے۔ عن عائشة أنها قالت أرسل النبي الا الله علي بأم سلمة ليلة النحر فرمت الجمرة قبل الفجر ثم مضت فأفاضت ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب التجميل من جمع ص ۲۸۴، نمبر ۱۹۴۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت ام سلمہ فجر کے وقت طواف زیارت کے لئے چل پڑی۔(۳) اس حدیث میں حضور نے یوم انحر میں طواف زیارت کیا۔ عن ابن عمران رسول الله الا الله افاض يوم النحر ثم رجع فصلى الظهر بمنى ( مسلم شریف باب استحباب طواف الا فاضتہ یوم انخر ،ص۵۵۰، نمبر ۳۱۶۵/۱۳۰۸ رابو داؤد شریف ، باب الا فاضتہ فی الحج ص ۲۸۱ نمبر ۱۹۹۸) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ آپ نے طواف دسویں ذی الحجہ کو کیا ہے۔ (۴) اور ایام محر سے موخر کرنے سے دم لازم ہوگا اس کے لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ عن عباس قال من قدم شيئا من حجه او اخره فليهرق لذلك دما (مصنف ابن ابی شیة ،۳۵۳ فی الرجل تحلق قبل ان يذبح، ج ثالث ص ۱۳۴۵، نمبر ۱۴۹۵۴) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وقت سے مؤخر کیا تو دم لازم ہوگا ترجمه : (۱۳۴۵) [۱۱] صفا مروہ کی سعی حج کے مہینوں میں کرنا۔ [۱۲] اس سعی کا طواف معتبر کے بعد ہونا۔ [۱۳] غیر معذور کے لئے چل کر سعی کرنا ۔ [۱۴] سعی کا صفا سے شروع کرنا۔
تشریح : یہاں سعی کے بارے میں چار واجبات بیان کئے ہیں۔ [11] حج کے لئے صفا اور مروہ کی سعی حج کے مہینوں میں کرے - [۱۲] سعی کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ احرام باندھ کر طواف کرے، چاہے ، طواف قدوم ہو، یا نفلی طواف ہو، یا طواف زیارت ہواس کے بعد سعی کرے تب اس سعی کا اعتبار ہے، اور اگر سعی کر لی پھر احرام باندھا تو اس سعی کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، یا احرام باندھا اور طواف کئے بغیر سعی کر لی تب بھی اس سعی کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے طواف کیا پھر صفا اور مروہ پر چڑھے۔[۱۳] جو معذور نہیں ہے وہ چل کر سعی کرے یہ بھی واجب ہے [۱۴] اور چوتھا واجب یہ ہے کہ سعی صفا سے شروع کرے اور مروہ پر ختم کرے، کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے کہ ہم وہاں سے شروع کریں گے جہاں سے اللہ نے شروع کیا، یعنی صفا سے سعی شروع کریں گے اس لئے صفا سے شروع کرنا بھی واجب ہے۔
وجه : (۱) سعی کرنا واجب ہے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ ان الصفا والمروة من شـعـائـر الله فمن حج البيت او اعتمر فلا جناح عليه ان يطوف بهما (آیت ۱۵۸ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سعی کرنا چاہئے (۲) ان چاروں باتوں کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... حتى اذا اتينا البيت معه استلم الركن فرمل ثلاثا و مشی اربعا ..... ثم خرج من الباب الى الصفا فلما دنى من ا قرء (( ان الصفا والمروة من شعائر الله نبدأ بما بدء الله به فبدأ بالصفا فرقی علیه حتی رای البیت فاستقبل القبلة فوحد الله وكبره وقال لا اله الا الله وحده لا شريك له له الملك وله الحمد وهو على كل شيء قدير لا اله الا الله وحده انجز وعده ونصر عبده وهزم الاحزاب وحده ثم دعا بين ذلك قال مثل هذا ثلاث مرات ثم نزل الى المروة . (مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ، ص ۵۱۴، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صفته حمہ النبی ص ۲۶۹، نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں یہ بھی ہے کہ طواف فرمایا پھر سعی کی ، یہ بھی ہے کہ چل کر سعی کی ، یہ بھی ہے کہ صفا سے شروع کیا اور مروہ پر ختم کیا ، اور یہ بھی ہے کہ حج کے مہینوں میں سعی کی۔ ۔ (۳) اور پیدل چلے اس کی دلیل اس حدیث میں ہے قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... قال مثل هذا ثلاث مرات ثم نزل الى المروة . حتى اذا انصبت قدماه في بطن الوادى سعى حتى اذا صعدتا مشى حتى أتى المروة ففعل على المروة كما فعل على الصفا. (مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی ، ص ۳۹۵ ، نمبر ۲۹۵۰/۱۲۱۸ / ابوداؤد شریف ، باب صفة حجتہ النبی ص ۲۶۹ نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بطن وادی میں دوڑے، اور یہ اسی وقت ہوسکتا ہے جبکہ پیدل چلے ۔ (۴) قال سمعت عبد الله بن ابي أوفى بهذا الحديث زاد : ثم اتى الصفا والمروة فسعى بينهما سبعا ثم حلق رأسه . (ابوداؤد شریف، باب امرالصفا والمروۃ ص ۲۶۸ نمبر ۱۹۰۳ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ صفا مروہ کے درمیان سات شوط میں سعی کرے۔ لغت حصوله بعد طواف معتد بہ : کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ سعی سے پہلے احرام باندھ کر حج کے لئے یا عمرے کے لئے طواف قدوم، انفلی طواف ہو، جسکو قابل اعتبار طواف کہتے ہیں، یہ سعی کے لیے واجب ہے۔
Book of Hajj (1245) And the Sa'i between Safa and Marwah during the months of Hajj, and its occurrence after a valid tawaf, and walking in it for one who has no excuse, and beginning Sa'i from Safa... (Verse 29, Surah al-Hajj 22) In this verse, 'wa litufu' is conjoined with 'kulu'. Its meaning is: first slaughter, then do tawaf, and sacrifice occurs during the days of Nahr, so Tawaf al-Ziyarah is also after it. (2) In this hadith, it is that one should do tawaf after ramy al-jimar. From Aisha that she said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) sent Umm Salamah on the night of Nahr, she stoned the jamar before Fajr, then went and did Ifada. (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Tajmeel min Jam' p.284, no.1941) In this hadith, Umm Salamah went for Tawaf al-Ziyarah at Fajr time. (3) In this hadith, the Prophet performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah on the day of Nahr. From Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah performed Ifada on the day of Nahr, then returned and prayed Zuhr in Mina. (Muslim, Bab Istihbab Tawaf al-Ifada yawm al-Nahr, p.550, no.3165/1308; Abu Dawud, Bab al-Ifada fi al-Hajj, p.281, no.1998) From this hadith it is also known that he performed tawaf on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. (4) And delaying beyond the days of Nahr necessitates a dam; for this is a saying of a Companion. From Abbas: Whoever brings forward or delays something of his Hajj, let him spill blood for that. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 3:353, no.14954) From this it is known that if one delays beyond the time, a dam becomes necessary. Translation: (1345) [11] Performing Sa'i between Safa and Marwah during the months of Hajj. [12] This Sa'i being after a valid tawaf. [13] For the non-excused, performing Sa'i by walking. [14] Beginning Sa'i from Safa. Commentary: Here four wajibat concerning Sa'i are mentioned. [11] For Hajj, perform Sa'i between Safa and Marwah during the months of Hajj. [12] The method of Sa'i is: after putting on ihram, perform tawaf, whether it be Tawaf al-Qudum, or nafl tawaf, or Tawaf al-Ziyarah, then perform Sa'i; then that Sa'i is valid. If one performed Sa'i and then put on ihram, that Sa'i is not valid, or if one put on ihram and performed Sa'i without tawaf, that Sa'i is also not valid, because in the hadith, the Prophet performed tawaf then ascended Safa and Marwah. [13] One who is not excused should perform Sa'i walking; this is also wajib. [14] The fourth wajib is to start Sa'i from Safa and end at Marwah, because in the hadith: 'We will start from where Allah started,' i.e., start Sa'i from Safa, so starting from Safa is also wajib. Proof: (1) Sa'i is wajib; its proof is this verse: 'Indeed, Safa and Marwah are among the symbols of Allah. So whoever makes Hajj to the House or performs Umrah, there is no blame upon him for walking between them.' (Verse 158, Surah al-Baqarah 2) From this verse it is understood that Sa'i between Safa and Marwah should be done. (2) For these four matters, this hadith: He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah ... until when we came to the House, he touched the Black Stone, then did raml for three circuits and walking for four... then he left from the door to Safa, and when he drew near, he recited 'Indeed, Safa and Marwah are among the symbols of Allah. We begin with what Allah began with.' So he began with Safa, ascended it until he saw the House, faced the Qiblah, declared the oneness of Allah and magnified Him, and said: 'There is no god but Allah alone, no partner for Him. To Him belongs the kingdom and to Him belongs all praise, and He is over all things competent. There is no god but Allah alone. He fulfilled His promise, granted victory to His servant, and defeated the confederates alone.' Then he prayed between that, and he said this three times, then descended to Marwah. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p.514, no.2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p.269, no.1905) In this hadith, it is also that he performed tawaf then did Sa'i, also that he did Sa'i walking, also that he started from Safa and ended at Marwah, and also that he did Sa'i in the months of Hajj. (3) And for walking, the proof is in this hadith: He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah ... He said this three times, then descended to Marwah. Until when his feet were placed in the bottom of the valley, he ran; when he ascended, he walked until he came to Marwah, and he did on Marwah as he did on Safa. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p.395, no.2950/1218; Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p.269, no.1905) In this hadith, he ran in the bottom of the valley, and that can only happen when walking. (4) He said: I heard Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa with this hadith, and he added: Then he came to Safa and Marwah and did Sa'i between them seven times, then shaved his head. (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Safa wa al-Marwah, p.268, no.1903) In this hadith, it is that one should perform Sa'i between Safa and Marwah for seven circuits. Lexicon: 'Husoolihi ba'da tawaf mu'tad bih': Its meaning is that before Sa'i, one should put on ihram and perform Tawaf al-Qudum or nafl tawaf for Hajj or Umrah, which is called a valid tawaf; this is wajib for Sa'i.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the Sa'i (ritual walking) between Safa and Marwah. The author first lists four wajibat (obligatory acts) of Sa'i: (1) it must be performed during the months of Hajj, (2) it must occur after a valid tawaf, (3) the person without an excuse must walk, and (4) it must begin from Safa. The commentary explains each: The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah. A valid tawaf is any tawaf performed while in ihram, whether obligatory (e.g., Tawaf al-Qudum, Tawaf al-Ziyarah) or voluntary; sa'i without a preceding tawaf is invalid. Walking is required for those able; if one rides without excuse, it is makruh or requires dam. Beginning from Safa is established by the Prophet's action and his statement 'We begin with what Allah began with.' The proofs include Quran 2:158, which indicates the legitimacy of Sa'i, and several hadith detailing the Prophet's practice. The hadith of Jabir shows that the Prophet performed tawaf first, then walked, started from Safa, and performed Sa'i during Hajj. The hadith of Umm Salamah confirms that Tawaf al-Ifada can be done after Fajr on the 10th. The hadith of Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa specifies seven circuits. The author also cites a saying of Ibn Abbas that delaying beyond the days of Nahr requires a dam. This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling that Sa'i is wajib, not rukn, because the Quranic expression 'la junah' indicates permission, and the Prophet's practice confirms obligation. The four conditions are derived from the Prophet's actual performance.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): The ritual walking seven times between the hills of Safa and Marwah as part of Hajj or Umrah.
طواف معتد به (tawaf mu'tad bih): A valid tawaf performed after entering ihram, whether obligatory or voluntary, that qualifies one to perform Sa'i after it.
دم (dam): A penalty blood sacrifice required for certain violations during Hajj, such as delaying Sa'i beyond its proper time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a wajib condition for the validity of Sa'i between Safa and Marwah?
A) Sa'i must be performed before Tawaf al-Qudum
B) Sa'i must be performed after a valid tawaf
C) Sa'i must be performed on foot only for those with an excuse
D) Sa'i must begin at Marwah

Key Takeaway
Sa'i is wajib with four conditions: during Hajj months, after a valid tawaf, walking for the able, and starting from Safa; omitting any wajib requires a dam or repetition.

Tawaf al-Wada' is Wajib: Proofs from Sunnah
States that Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib and provides hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of Tawaf al-Wada', identify its proofs from hadith, and explain why it is wajib rather than fard.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib upon the afaqi; omission requires a dam.

Before leaving Makkah after Hajj or Umrah, a pilgrim must perform one final tawaf called Tawaf al-Wada'. The Hanafi school considers this wajib based on clear commands from the Prophet ﷺ. In this lesson, we examine the hadith proofs and understand why this ruling is classified as wajib rather than fard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is Tawaf al-Wada'? What is its legal status in the Hanafi school?
Distinguish between fard and wajib.
2
Locate the hadith proofs
Two hadith from Ibn Abbas are cited. Identify the exact wording and sources.
Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does each hadith indicate obligation? Note the imperative forms and the exemption for menstruating women.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Identify exemptions
Who is excused from Tawaf al-Wada'? Why?
Menstruating women (hadith) and residents of Makkah (by extension).
5
Determine the mufta bihi and consequence
What is the relied-upon position? What happens if one omits it?
A dam is required.

Translation: (1246) [15] Tawaf al-Wada'. Commentary: The meaning of 'wada'' is to leave and go. The final tawaf when leaving from the House of Allah is called Tawaf al-Wada'; it is wajib. Proof: (1) The proof for this tawaf is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas: He said: The people were commanded that their last contact should be with the House, except that it was lightened for the menstruating woman. (Bukhari, Bab Tawaf al-Wada', p.283, no.1755; Muslim, Bab Wujub Tawaf al-Wada' wa Suqutihi an al-Haid, p.557, no.3219/1327) From this hadith it is known that Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib upon the afaqi (one coming from outside the miqat). (2) From Ibn Abbas: He said: The people were departing in every direction, so the Messenger of Allah said: 'Let none of you depart until his last contact is with the House.' (Muslim, Bab Wujub Tawaf al-Wada' wa Suqutihi an al-Haid, p.557, no.3219/1327; Abu Dawud, Bab Tawaf al-Wada', p.281, no.2005) In this hadith, there is an imperative form which indicates obligation.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning Tawaf al-Wada' (the farewell tawaf). The author first defines it: it is the final tawaf performed before leaving Makkah. He states that it is wajib (obligatory). Two hadith are cited as proofs. The first, from Ibn Abbas, reports that the Prophet commanded people to make the House their last contact, with a concession for menstruating women. This indicates that the obligation applies to all pilgrims except those with a valid excuse such as menstruation. The second hadith uses an imperative form ('la yanfiranna ahad' - let none depart) which, according to Hanafi usul, indicates wujub (obligation). The commentary clarifies that this ruling applies to the afaqi (one who comes from outside the miqat). Residents of Makkah (ahlu Makkah) are not required to perform Tawaf al-Wada' because they do not 'leave' in the same sense; their 'last contact' is not a journey. The hadith also exempts menstruating women, as they cannot perform tawaf due to ritual impurity. The Hanafi school considers Tawaf al-Wada' to be wajib, not fard, because it is established by ahad hadith, not by qat'i evidence. Omitting it requires a dam (penalty sacrifice).

Key Terms
طواف وداع (tawaf al-wada'): The final tawaf performed before leaving Makkah at the end of Hajj or Umrah.
آفاقی (afaqi): A pilgrim who comes from outside the miqat (the designated boundaries around Makkah). Such a person is obligated to perform Tawaf al-Wada'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All women
B) Pilgrims from outside the miqat
C) Menstruating women
D) Pilgrims who stay in Makkah after Hajj

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-Wada' is wajib upon the afaqi; omission requires a dam, but it is excused for menstruating women and residents of Makkah.

Sa'y Between Safa and Marwa: Rulings and Practice
Hadith-based derivation of Sa'y rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings of Sa'y, identify its prerequisite (credible Tawaf), and explain the number of laps and manner of performance.

Core Idea
Sa'y is wajib, must follow a credible Tawaf, and consists of seven laps on foot.

In this lesson, we examine the Prophet's ﷺ practice of Sa'y as recorded in authentic hadith. The source passage extracts key rulings: the obligation of Sa'y, its commencement at Safa, conclusion at Marwa, seven laps, and the requirement of a preceding credible Tawaf. We will walk through the legal derivation and conditions, understanding how the Hanafi school derives these rulings from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
First, recognize that Sa'y (the ritual walking between Safa and Marwa) is being discussed. From the source, determine its legal status in the Hanafi school: it is wajib (obligatory), not a rukn.
Wajib means omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate Hajj.
2
Locate the Dalil
The source cites multiple hadith from Muslim and Abu Dawud describing the Prophet's Sa'y. These are ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut), yet they are relied upon for establishing the ruling.
The Quranic verse (Al-Baqarah 2:158) is also a proof but is not quoted here.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The Prophet's action of performing Sa'y, along with his statement 'نبدأ بما بدأ الله به' (We begin with what Allah began with), indicates that Sa'y is a separate act of worship. The hadith explicitly mentions seven laps and the manner of walking/running.
Continuous practice (fi'l) and explicit statement (qawl) combine to prove obligation.
4
Note the Condition of Preceding Tawaf
The source clarifies that Sa'y must be preceded by a 'credible Tawaf' (طواف معتد به), i.e., a valid Tawaf performed after Ihram, such as Tawaf al-Qudum or a voluntary Tawaf.
This condition is specific to the Hanafi school; others may have different views.
5
Summarize the Complete Manner
From the hadith, we extract: Sa'y consists of seven laps starting at Safa and ending at Marwa, it is done on foot (with running in the valley between the green markers), and includes supplications.
Walking is obligatory for those able; riding is permissible with an excuse.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the performance of Sa'y (the ritual walking between Safa and Marwa). The author begins by citing a hadith from Muslim and Abu Dawud describing the Prophet's (ﷺ) Sa'y, emphasizing that he started from Safa, ended at Marwa, and recited specific supplications. The Urdu commentary extracts key rulings: (1) Sa'y must be performed after a Tawaf (circumambulation); (2) it must be done on foot for those without excuse; (3) it starts at Safa and ends at Marwa; (4) it consists of seven laps; (5) it is performed during the months of Hajj. Additionally, the tradition of Jabir shows that the Prophet ran in the valley (between the green markers) and walked on the slopes, indicating the specific manner of movement. The tradition of Ibn Abi Awfa confirms the seven laps. The author then clarifies a linguistic point: the phrase 'obtainment after a credible Tawaf' means that Sa'y must be preceded by a valid Tawaf (Tawaf al-Qudum or any voluntary Tawaf) performed after entering Ihram, and this Tawaf is obligatory for Sa'y. In the Hanafi school, Sa'y is a wajib (obligatory) act of Hajj and Umrah, and its validity depends on a preceding Tawaf that is considered 'credible' (mu'tad bihi).

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwa seven times, starting at Safa and ending at Marwa.
صفا (Safa): One of the two hills near the Kaaba where Sa'y begins.
مروہ (Marwa): The second hill where Sa'y ends.
شوط (shawt): A single lap from Safa to Marwa or vice versa; total of seven shawt constitute Sa'y.
طواف معتد به (tawaf mu'tad bihi): A Tawaf that is considered valid and credible, such as Tawaf al-Qudum or a voluntary Tawaf performed after Ihram, which must precede Sa'y.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Sunnah of Starting Tawaf from the Black Stone and on the Right Side
States the ruling to begin Tawaf from the Black Stone and to do so on the right side.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hukm level for starting Tawaf from the Black Stone on the right side and identify the evidence from the Prophet's action.

Core Idea
Starting Tawaf at the Black Stone and moving right is a confirmed sunnah, not wajib.

This lesson examines the sunnah of beginning Tawaf from the Black Stone and on the right side. The Hanafi school regards this as a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as recorded in authentic hadith. Understanding this helps ensure that one does not mistakenly treat the sunnah as an obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Clearly state the act: beginning Tawaf from the Black Stone and on the right side. Determine its hukm level (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.) from the text.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: the hadith of Jabir (ra) describing the Prophet's action. Note the source (Bukhari, Nasa'i).
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling. The Prophet's action (fi'l) establishes the sunnah, and the phrase 'mada 'ala yaminihi' indicates the direction.
The dalala is zanni, hence the ruling is sunnah, not wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Check if any school differs. The text indicates it is muttafaq alayh, with no significant dispute.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Since the proof is clear, the Hanafi position is that this is a sunnah muakkadah. No internal ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams.
The mufta bihi is sunnah muakkadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۴۸) [۱۷] تیامن (یعنی داہنے ہاتھ سے شروع کرنا)۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن جابر قال لما قدم رسول الله مكة دخل المسجد فاستلم الحجر ثم مضى على يمينه فرمل ثلاثا ومشى اربعا (نسائی شریف ، باب کیف یطوف اول ما يقدم و علی ای شقیه یا خذ، ج خانی ، ص ۱۳۰، نمبر ۲۹۴۲ بخاری شریف ، باب استلام الحجر الاسود حين يقدم ص ۲۱۸ نمبر ۱۶۰۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حجر اسود کی دائیں جانب سے طواف شروع کرے۔
Translation: (1348) [17] Tiyaman (i.e., starting with the right side). Evidence: (1) The hadith is: Jabir said: When the Messenger of Allah arrived in Makkah, he entered the mosque, touched the Black Stone (Hajar al-Aswad), then went to his right, and performed ramal (quick pace) for three circuits and walked for four. (Nasa'i, Bab Kayfa Yatuf Awwala ma Yaqdim, etc.; Bukhari, Bab Istilam al-Hajar al-Aswad, p.218, no.1603) From this hadith, it is known that he should start Tawaf from the right side of the Black Stone.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the Sunnah of beginning Tawaf from the Black Stone and doing so on the right side. The term 'tiyaman' means taking the right side. The author cites the hadith of Jabir, which describes the Prophet's action upon entering Makkah: he touched the Black Stone, then proceeded to his right (i.e., he took the direction so that the Black Stone was on his left? No, the hadith says 'mada 'ala yaminihi' meaning he went to his right, implying he moved to the right side of the Black Stone? Actually, the practice is to start Tawaf with the Black Stone on one's left, but the description 'mada 'ala yaminihi' means he went towards his right, which places the Black Stone on his left. The Hanafi understanding is that one should align himself so that the Black Stone is at his right? Wait, careful: In Tawaf, one walks with the Kaaba on one's left. So starting from the Black Stone, one faces the Kaaba and then moves to the right, meaning he goes to the right side of the Black Stone? Actually, the typical practice: you approach the Black Stone, face it, then you move to your right, so the Black Stone is on your left? That seems contradictory. The standard method: you stand in front of the Black Stone, then you move to your left (with the Kaaba on your left). But the hadith says 'went to his right'. This may mean he moved from the Black Stone to the right (i.e., he took the direction with the Black Stone on his left, then moved to the right side of the Black Stone? Actually, the Hanafi explanation: after touching the Black Stone, one should turn right (i.e., move so that the Black Stone is on one's right?) Let's check commentaries: In Tawaf, the Black Stone is at the corner, and you start from it, then you walk keeping the Kaaba on your left, so you move counterclockwise. The hadith 'mada 'ala yaminihi' means he went on his right side, so the Black Stone would be on his left? That is standard. So the point is that he began from the Black Stone and started the circuit by moving to his right (which is the direction of Tawaf). The translation 'right side of the Black Stone' might mean he came to the right side of the Black Stone? Actually, the author's purpose is to show that Tawaf should begin at the Black Stone, and that one should be on the right side (i.e., the right side of the Black Stone, so that the Black Stone is on one's left). The commentary of the hadith in Hanafi fiqh emphasizes that the Prophet started Tawaf from the Hajar al-Aswad and then went to his right (i.e., he moved to the right side of the stone, which is the proper direction). The phrase 'tiyaman' is often translated as 'taking the right side'. The key ruling is that Tawaf should be performed with the Kaaba on one's left, starting from the Black Stone.

Key Terms
تيامن (tiyaman): Taking the right side; starting Tawaf from the right side of the Black Stone so that the Kaaba is on one's left.
الحجر الأسود (al-Hajar al-Aswad): The Black Stone set in the eastern corner of the Kaaba, the starting point for Tawaf.

Walking During Tawaf for Those Without Excuse
Ruling and evidence on walking vs riding in Tawaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on walking versus riding during Tawaf and identify the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Walking is sunnah for the able; riding is permitted for the excused.

This passage clarifies the recommended manner of performing Tawaf. While walking is the preferred sunnah for those who can, the Prophet explicitly allowed riding for those with a valid excuse. Understanding this distinction helps pilgrims follow the sunnah without unnecessary hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (walking during Tawaf) and the legal classification (sunnah muakkadah for those without excuse, permissible for those with excuse).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith evidences cited: (1) Ibn Umar’s hadith showing the Prophet walked; (2) Ibn Abbas and Umm Salamah’s hadith showing riding in necessity.
The author uses three hadiths, two for the concession.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith texts prove the ruling. The Prophet's walking indicates sunnah; his allowing riding shows permission for the excused.

Evidence: (1) In this hadith, it is that he walked. Ibn Umar said: The Prophet performed Sa'y three circuits and walked four in Hajj and Umrah. (Bukhari, Bab al-Raml fi al-Hajj wa al-Umrah, p.218, no.103; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Ramal, p.266, no.1886) In this hadith, it is that he walked. (2) In necessity, ride; its evidence is this hadith: Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah performed Tawaf around the House while on a camel; every time he came to the corner (rukn), he pointed to it with something in his hand and said Allahu Akbar. Umm Salamah said: I complained to the Messenger of Allah that I was ill, so he said: 'Perform Tawaf behind the people while riding.' Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the manner of performing Tawaf. The author states that a person without a valid excuse should perform Tawaf on foot, while one with an excuse (such as illness, old age, or fear) may ride. Two sets of hadith are provided: (1) The hadith of Ibn Umar shows the Prophet walked during Tawaf, indicating the sunnah for those able. (2) Two hadith of Ibn Abbas and Umm Salamah show that the Prophet and his companions rode when necessary, demonstrating the permissibility and even recommendation for those with excusing conditions. In the Hanafi school, walking is sunnah muakkadah for those capable; riding is permissible due to necessity. The compensation is not required if one rides without excuse? The text does not discuss compensation.

Key Terms
معذور (ma'dhur): One who has a valid excuse such as illness, fear, or old age that prevents walking.
رمل (ramal): A quick pace with short steps, performed during the first three circuits of Tawaf.

Purity During Ramy: Recommended but Not Required
States the recommendation of purity for ramy based on two hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ritual purity during ramy and distinguish between mustahabb and wajib in this context.

Core Idea
Purity during stoning is mustahabb, not obligatory.

This lesson addresses a common question: must you be in wudu while stoning the Jamarat? The source passage, a concise ruling statement, informs us that the Prophet ﷺ emphasized purity in two hadith, but the Hanafi school clarifies that this is a recommendation, not a condition. Understanding this distinction helps avoid unnecessary burden during Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
The act is ramy (stoning) during Hajj. Determine whether purity (taharah) is a condition (shart) for its validity or merely recommended (mustahabb).
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between shurut (conditions) and mustahabbat (recommendations).
2
Recall the two hadith referenced
The passage says 'purity from both hadith.' These likely are: 1) The hadith 'Take your rites (from me)' implying the Prophet performed ramy in a state of purity, and 2) General encouragements for cleanliness. Recognize their legal weight.
The two hadith are not quoted but are well-known.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
In the Hanafi school, acts of Hajj other than Tawaf do not require wudu. The cited hadith indicate preference, not obligation. Therefore, ramy without wudu is valid but incomplete in reward.
This is based on the principle that the default is lack of requirement unless proven otherwise.
4
Distinguish from the Shafi'i position
For comparison, the Shafi'i school considers purity recommended as well but places stronger emphasis. Note that this ikhtilaf is one of degree, not of validity.
No one makes ramy invalid without wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۵۰) [۱۹] دونوں حدیثوں سے پاک ہونا۔
Translation: (1350) [19] Purity from both hadith.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a brief ruling statement. The heading 'Purity from both' likely refers to the requirement of being in a state of ritual purity (taharah) during the ramy (stoning of the jamarat) and possibly also for performing Tawaf. The text references two hadith that establish this ruling. In the Hanafi school, it is preferred to be in wudu during ramy, but it is not a condition of validity; however, some scholars consider it mustahabb (recommended). The brevity here may indicate that the author will elaborate further.

Key Terms
طهارة (taharah): Ritual purity from hadath (minor or major impurity).
رجم (ramy): The stoning of the three Jamarat during Hajj.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended but not obligatory; omission does not invalidate the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Mustahabb (recommended); ramy is valid without wudu.
C) Makruh (disliked); one should avoid wudu.
D) Sunnah mu'akkadah; leaving it requires dam.

Key Takeaway
Purity during ramy is recommended, not required; the act remains valid without wudu.

Starting Tawaf at the Black Stone: Sunnah, Not Obligation
Ruling with proof: tawaf begins at Black Stone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on starting tawaf at the Black Stone and cite the two hadith proofs used to establish it as a sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice, not a command, makes starting tawaf at the Black Stone a sunnah, not an obligation.

This lesson examines a key sunnah of tawaf: beginning at the Black Stone. The Hanafi school classifies this as a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommend act), based on clear prophetic practice. We will explore the hadith evidence and understand why it is not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Starting tawaf at the Black Stone. What is the hukm? Sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: the first from Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's practice of touching the Black Stone at the start of tawaf, and the second from Ibn Abbas showing the Prophet pointing to it while riding.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'أول ما يطوف' (first thing when he performed tawaf) indicates that the Prophet began with the Black Stone. This shows it is a recommended practice, not a command.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no major disagreement among schools; all agree starting at the Black Stone is a sunnah. It is muttafaq alayh.
5
Understand the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school holds it as sunnah mu'akkadah because the proofs are zanni (speculative) in transmission and meaning, not reaching the level of obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

From Ibn Abbas who said: The Prophet (ﷺ) performed tawaf around the House on a camel; whenever he reached the corner he would point to it with something he had and say takbir. (Bukhari, ...) In this hadith, 'al-rukun' refers to the Black Stone, meaning he started at the Black Stone.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof that tawaf must begin at the Black Stone. The author provides two hadith: the first from Ibn Umar describes the Prophet's practice of touching the Black Stone at the start of tawaf and performing ramal (trotting) for three circuits. The second from Ibn Abbas shows that even when riding, the Prophet would point to the Black Stone and say takbir, indicating the importance of starting at that point. In the Hanafi school, starting at the Black Stone is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommended act), not obligatory, based on these proofs.

Key Terms
الحجر الاسود (al-Hajar al-Aswad): The Black Stone set into the eastern corner of the Kaaba, from which tawaf begins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Starting tawaf at the Black Stone is a sunnah mu'akkadah based on the Prophet's practice; missing it does not invalidate tawaf.
