Tayammun in Tawaf: The Sunnah of Starting on the Right
Ruling with proof that tawaf starts from the right side

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammun in tawaf and explain its evidence from the hadith of Jabir.

Core Idea
Tawaf begins on the right of the Black Stone — a confirmed sunnah, not a fard.

Tawaf around the Kaaba is a central rite of Hajj and Umrah. The Prophet's ﷺ manner of performing tawaf set a precise precedent that the Hanafi school follows as a sunnah. One key element is starting on the right side of the Black Stone (tayammun). This lesson examines the evidence from the hadith and clarifies why this is recommended, not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'tayammun', i.e., starting tawaf on the right side. Determine the Hanafi ruling: is it fard, wajib, or sunnah?
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Jabir (رضي الله عنه) reported in Nasai and Bukhari.
The hadith describes the Prophet's actions after entering Masjid al-Haram.
3
Extract the wajh al-dalalah
Identify the specific phrase that proves the ruling: 'ثم مضى على يمينه' (then went to his right). This shows the direction.
The Prophet explicitly moved to his right, indicating the starting side.
4
Note the hukm level
The Hanafi school classifies this as sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) because the Prophet did it consistently but did not command it as binding.
Contrast with fard/wajib: omission does not invalidate tawaf but loses reward.
5
Check cross-madhhab agreement
Other schools also consider tayammun mustahabb or sunnah. This is a mutually agreed-upon practice (muttafaq alayh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۴۸) [۱۷] تیامن (یعنی داہنے ہاتھ سے شروع کرنا)۔ وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن جابر قال لما قدم رسول الله مكة دخل المسجد فاستلم الحجر ثم مضى على يمينه فرمل ثلاثا ومشى اربعا (نسائی شریف ، باب کیف یطوف اول ما يقدم و علی ای شقیه یا خذ، ج خانی ، ص ۱۳۰، نمبر ۲۹۴۲ بخاری شریف ، باب استلام الحجر الاسود حين يقدم ص ۲۱۸ نمبر ۱۶۰۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حجر اسود کی دائیں جانب سے طواف شروع کرے۔
Translation: (1348) [17] Tayammun (i.e., starting with the right hand). Evidence: (1) The hadith: From Jabir who said: When the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) arrived in Mecca, he entered the mosque, touched the Stone, then went to his right, trotted three circuits and walked four. (Nasai, ...) This hadith shows that tawaf should begin from the right side of the Black Stone.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This ruling with proof establishes that tawaf should be performed starting on the right side of the Black Stone, meaning the tawaf direction is counterclockwise (starting from the east corner going to the right). The hadith of Jabir shows the Prophet touched the Black Stone and then proceeded on his right side, performing ramal (trotting) for three circuits. In the Hanafi school, this is a sunnah act, as the Prophet's practice indicates the proper way to perform tawaf.

Key Terms
تيامن (tayammun): Starting on the right side; in tawaf, it means beginning from the right side of the Black Stone, i.e., moving to the right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tayammun (starting tawaf on the right of the Black Stone) is a confirmed sunnah based on the Prophet's practice, not a mandatory obligation.

Purity from Both Hadaths in Tawaf
Ruling with proof that tawaf requires purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that purification from both minor and major impurities is a condition for tawaf and identify the three proofs from the sunnah.

Core Idea
Tawaf requires purification like prayer; without it, tawaf is invalid.

This passage establishes the necessity of being free from both minor (hadath asghar) and major (janabah) impurities during tawaf. The author cites three hadiths to prove this ruling. Understanding this condition is essential for the validity of tawaf in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that purity from both minor and major impurities is a condition (shart) for tawaf. Note that this is not just recommended; it is required.
2
Locate the first proof
The hadith of Aisha (ra) shows that the Prophet (saw) performed wudu before tawaf. This action implies that wudu is a prerequisite.
Bukhari 1641
3
Locate the second proof
The hadith of Ibn Abbas (ra) explicitly states that tawaf is like prayer, except that speech is allowed. Since prayer requires purification, so does tawaf.
Tirmidhi 960
4
Locate the third proof
The hadith about menstruation (Aisha, ra) shows that major impurity prevents tawaf until purification, confirming the necessity of purity from hadath akbar.
Bukhari 1650
5
Conclude the ruling
Tawaf performed without wudu or while in a state of janabah is invalid and must be repeated. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
All three proofs together establish the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۵۰) [۱۹] دونوں حدیثوں سے پاک ہونا۔ تشریح : طواف کے وقت جنابت سے بھی پاک ہونا ضروری ہے، اور حدث اصغر سے بھی پاک ہونا ضروری ہے۔ وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں طواف کے لئے وضو کا ذکر ہے۔ اخبرتني عائشة ان اول شيء بدأ به حين قدم أنه ہے۔اخبـر توضأ ثم طاف بالبيت ثم لم تكن عمرة - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الطاف علی وضوء ،ص ۲۶۵ نمبر ۱۶۴۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وضو کر کے طواف کیا ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف کے لئے وضو ضروری ہے ۔ (۲) عن ابن عباس ان النبي الله قال الطواف حول البيت مثل الصلوة الا انكم تتكلمون فيه فمن تكلم فيه فلا يتكلم الا بخير (ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فى الكلام في الطواف ، ص ۱۹۰، نمبر ۹۶۰ رنسائی شریف، باب اباحۃ الکلام فی الطواف ج ثانی ص ۲۸ نمبر ۲۹۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف نماز کی طرح ہے اس لئے طواف میں بھی وضو شرط ہے (۳) جنابت سے پاک ہو اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عائشة انها قالت قدمت مكة وانا حائض ولم اطف بالبيت ولا بين الصفا والمروة قالت فشكوت ذلك الى رسول الله فقال افعلى كما يفعل الحاج غير ان لا تطوفى بالبيت حتى تطهری (بخاری شریف، باب تقضی الحائض المناسک کلھا الا الطواف بالبیت، ص ۲۶۷، نمبر ۱۶۵۰) اس حدیث سے بھی پتہ چلا کہ طہارت کے بغیر طواف نہ کرے۔
Translation: (1350) [19] Purity from both hadaths. Explanation: During tawaf, it is necessary to be pure from major impurity (janabah) and minor impurity (hadath asghar). Evidence: (1) The hadith mentions wudu for tawaf: Aisha informed me that the first thing he (the Prophet) did when he arrived was that he performed wudu, then performed tawaf, and then there was no Umrah. (Bukhari, ...) This hadith shows that tawaf requires wudu. (2) From Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (ﷺ) said: Tawaf around the House is like prayer, except that you may speak in it. So whoever speaks, let him speak only good. (Tirmidhi, ...) This hadith shows that tawaf is like prayer, so wudu is a condition. (3) Purity from janabah: Aisha said: I arrived in Mecca while I was menstruating and did not perform tawaf or sa'y. I complained to the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ), and he said: Do as the pilgrims do, but do not perform tawaf until you are pure. (Bukhari, ...) This hadith also shows that one should not perform tawaf without purification.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This ruling establishes that purification from both major and minor impurities is necessary (shart) for tawaf. The author provides three proofs: (1) Aisha's hadith that the Prophet performed wudu before tawaf, indicating that a state of wudu is required. (2) The hadith equating tawaf to prayer, implying that purity is a condition similarly. (3) The hadith about menstruation shows that a woman in a state of major impurity (such as menstrual blood) must wait until she becomes pure before performing tawaf. In the Hanafi school, purification from both hadaths is a condition (shart) for the validity of tawaf. If one performs tawaf without wudu or in a state of janabah, the tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.

Key Terms
الحدثين (al-hadathayn): Both types of impurity: minor impurity (hadath asghar, requiring wudu) and major impurity (hadath akbar, requiring ghusl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because menstruation is a major impurity requiring purification.
B) Because she was tired.
C) Because she had no wudu.
D) Because the Kaaba was under construction.

Key Takeaway
Purification from both minor and major impurities is a necessary condition for the validity of tawaf, as established by multiple hadiths.

Covering the Awrah in Tawaf
Ruling with proof that covering the awrah is required in tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on covering the awrah in tawaf, cite the two proofs (Quran and hadith), and explain why covering the awrah is a condition for validity.

Core Idea
Covering the awrah is a condition for tawaf, just as for prayer – an uncovered tawaf is invalid.

This passage establishes a crucial analogy between tawaf and prayer. The Hanafi school teaches that just as prayer requires covering the awrah, so does tawaf. Two proofs are cited: a verse commanding adornment at every mosque, and a hadith prohibiting naked tawaf. Understanding this ruling is essential for anyone performing Hajj or Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and what legal classification is given. Here, the act is tawaf, and covering the awrah is identified as a condition (shart) for its validity.
Condition (shart) means if missing, the act is invalid.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the two proofs: the Quranic verse (7:31) and the hadith from Bukhari about the announcement of Abu Bakr.
Both are textual proofs (dalil naqli).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof indicates the requirement. The verse commands 'take your adornment' which includes proper dress; the hadith explicitly forbids naked tawaf.
The verse is general, the hadith is specific to tawaf.
4
Note the analogy to prayer
The author states tawaf is 'of the same level as prayer' (fi darajah al-salat), so the same rules apply, including covering awrah.
This analogy is a form of qiyas.
5
State the practical consequence
If the awrah is uncovered during tawaf, the tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.
This follows from the condition being breached.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۲۵۱ [الف) [۲۰] ستر چھپانا۔ تشریح طواف نماز کے درجے میں ہے اس لئے جس طرح وہاں ستر عورت ضروری ہے اسی طرح یہاں بھی ستر عورت ضروری ہے وجه : (۱) اس آیت سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے ۔ یا بنی آدم خذوا زينتكم عند كل مسجد ۔ ( آیت ۳۱ سورة الاعراف ۷) کہ ہر نماز کے وقت زینت اختیار کرو۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ جاہلیت کی طرح ننگا نہ رہے۔ عن ابي هريرة ان ابا بكر الصديق بعثه في الحجة التي امره عليها النبي الالالا لاله قبل حجة الوداع يوم النحر في رهط يوذن في الناس ان لا يحج بعد العام مشرك و لا يطوف بالبيت عریان ( بخاری شریف، باب حج ابی بکر بالناس في سه يتسع ، ص ۳۹ ۷، نمبر ۴۳۶۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ننگا طواف نہ کرے۔
Translation: (1251 [a]) [20] Covering the private parts (satr). Explanation: Tawaf is of the same level as prayer, so just as covering the awrah is necessary there, it is also necessary here. Evidence: (1) The verse can be used as evidence: 'O Children of Adam, take your adornment at every mosque.' (Surah al-A'raf 7:31) Meaning at the time of every prayer, adopt adornment (i.e., wear proper clothing). (2) The hadith states that one should not be naked as in the time of ignorance. From Abu Huraira that Abu Bakr al-Siddiq sent him during the Hajj that he (the Prophet) appointed him before the Farewell Pilgrimage on the day of sacrifice with a group to announce among the people that after this year no polytheist should perform Hajj and no one should perform tawaf around the House naked. (Bukhari, ...) This hadith states that one should not perform tawaf naked.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This ruling establishes that covering the awrah is a condition (shart) for the validity of tawaf, just as it is for prayer. The author provides two proofs: first, the Quranic verse (7:31) which is interpreted as commanding proper dress at every mosque, especially during prayer and worship; second, the hadith of Abu Bakr announcing that no one should perform tawaf naked, which was a practice of pre-Islamic days. In the Hanafi school, the awrah for men is from the navel to the knees, and for women the entire body except the face, hands, and feet. Performing tawaf with the awrah uncovered invalidates the tawaf.

Key Terms
ستر العورة (satr al-'awrah): The obligation to cover the private parts during tawaf, which is a condition for its validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) That no polytheist should perform Hajj and no one should perform tawaf naked.
B) That tawaf should be done on foot.
C) That the Black Stone is the starting point.
D) That women must cover their faces.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires covering the awrah during tawaf, using the Quranic verse and the hadith, making it a condition for validity.

Ruling on Completing Tawaf al-Ziyarah in the Days of Nahr
Ruling with proof about timing of tawaf al-ziyarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of tawaf al-ziyarah, distinguish between fard and wajib circuits, and identify the penalty for delay.

Core Idea
Four circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah are fard; the remaining three are wajib; delay beyond the Days of Nahr requires dam.

Tawaf al-ziyarah is the central tawaf of Hajj. This lesson clarifies that while four circuits are fard (pillar), the remaining three are wajib and must also be completed within the Days of Nahr. Delaying any circuit beyond these days incurs a compensatory dam (sacrifice). The proof comes from the saying of Ibn Abbas that any delay in Hajj rites requires blood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is tawaf al-ziyarah, specifically its timing. The ruling: all seven circuits must be performed in the Days of Nahr.
The ruling distinguishes between fard (four) and wajib (three).
2
Understand the fard vs wajib distinction
In Hanafi fiqh, four circuits are fard (omission invalidates Hajj), and three are wajib (omission requires dam but Hajj is valid).
This distinction affects the penalty for delay.
3
Identify the consequence of delay
If any circuit is delayed beyond the Days of Nahr, a dam (sacrifice) becomes necessary. This is because the wajib was not performed on time.
The dam is in addition to completing the circuits later.
4
Analyze the evidence
The proof is a qawl sahabi (saying of a Companion): Ibn Abbas said, 'Whoever brings forward or delays something of his Hajj, let him cause a blood (sacrifice) for that.' This general statement applies to tawaf al-ziyarah.
This evidence is considered authoritative in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۲۵۱ [ ب]) [۲۱] طواف زیارت کے زیادہ شوطوں کو ایام نحر میں ادا کرنے کے بعد تین شوط کو بھی ایام نحر میں ادا کرنا ہے۔ تشریح : طواف زیارت کے چارشو ط کو ایام نحر میں کرنا فرض ہے، اور باقی تین شوط کو ایام نحر میں ادا کرنا واجب ہے، تو گویا کہ سب طوافوں کو ایام نحر میں ادا کرنا واجب ہوا ۔ وجه : (۱) اور ایام نحر سے موخر کرنے سے دم لازم ہوگا اس کے لئے یہ قول صحابی ہے۔ عن عباس قال من قدم شيئا من حجه او اخره فليهرق لذلك دما (مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۳۵۳ فی الرجل يحلق قبل ان یذ بح ، ج ثالث ص ۱۳۴۵، نمبر ۱۴۹۵۴)
Translation: (1251 [b]) [21] After performing the majority of circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah in the Days of Nahr, it is also obligatory to perform the three remaining circuits in the Days of Nahr. Explanation: Four circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah are obligatory (fard) to perform in the Days of Nahr, and the remaining three circuits are wajib (obligatory) in the Days of Nahr. So it becomes that all circuits are wajib to be performed in the Days of Nahr. Evidence: (1) And if delayed beyond the Days of Nahr, a dam becomes necessary. For this, there is the saying of a Companion: From Abbas who said: Whoever brings forward or delays something of his Hajj, let him cause a blood (sacrifice) for that. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, ...)
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This ruling explains that tawaf al-ziyarah must be performed within the Days of Nahr (10th to 13th of Dhul-Hijjah). Four circuits are fard (obligatory) and must be done in these days; if one performs four, the remaining three are wajib to also be done in these days. Delaying any part beyond the Days of Nahr incurs a dam (a penalty sacrifice). The proof is the statement of Ibn Abbas that any delay or advancement of Hajj rites requires a blood sacrifice. In the Hanafi school, performing all seven circuits in the Days of Nahr is considered wajib; missing the time requires dam.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The essential tawaf performed during Hajj, also called tawaf al-ifadah, performed in the Days of Nahr.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (e.g., a sheep) that must be slaughtered in Mecca as a penalty for missing or delaying a wajib act of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No penalty, it is simply invalid.
B) A dam (sacrificial animal).
C) Fasting three days.
D) Repeating the entire Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Performing all seven circuits of tawaf al-ziyarah within the Days of Nahr is wajib; delay incurs a dam.

Prohibited Acts During Ihram (Muhazrat)
Ruling and enumeration of prohibited acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibited acts (muhazrat) during ihram and explain why avoiding them is wajib.

Core Idea
A muhrim must avoid sewn clothes, head/face covering (men), obscene speech, and hunting — or incur sin and penalty.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah enumerates the prohibitions of ihram and emphasizes that avoiding them is wajib (obligatory). It provides four categories of prohibited acts and clarifies key terms. We will work through each category and understand the legal implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The text states that avoiding the muhazrat (prohibited acts) is wajib. This means a muhrim must abstain from these actions; committing them incurs sin and often requires compensation (dam).
The ruling is a direct statement from the text: 'ترك المحظورات ... واجب'.
2
List the main prohibitions
The passage lists: (1) Men wearing sewn garments (makhit). (2) Men covering the head or face; women covering the face (but covering head is allowed). (3) Obscene speech (rafath), transgression (fusuq), and argumentation (jidal). (4) Hunting or assisting in hunting (killing, pointing, directing).
Each category is distinct and must be avoided.
3
Distinguish gender-specific rules
Men cannot cover the head or face; women cannot cover the face (to avoid contact with the veil) but may cover the head. This is a key Hanafi position.
Women covering the face would mean touching the face, which is prohibited.
4
Appreciate the scope of hunting prohibition
Hunting is prohibited not only in action but also through indirect means like pointing to game or directing others. This shows the principle that aiding in a prohibited act is also prohibited.
This extends to verbal or gestural assistance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ج وترك المحظورات كلبس الرجل المخيط وستر رأسه ووجهه وستر المرأة وجهها والرفث والفسوق والجدال وقتل الصيد والاشارة اليه والدلالة عليه. 
ترجمه : (۱۲۵۱ [ج]) [۲۲] ممنوعات کا ترک کرنا۔ جیسے مرد کا سلے ہوئے کپڑے پہننا،اور اپنا سر اور چہرہ ڈھانپنا ، اور عورت کا صرف چہرہ ڈھانپنا، اور رفٹ (پخش کلام) فسق ، جھگڑا، شکار کو مارنا، اور اس کی طرف اشارہ کرنا ، یا اس کی طرف رہنمائی کرنا۔ 
تشریح : حج میں جو باتیں کرنا ممنوع ہیں ان سے بچنا بھی واجب ہے، پھر اسکی چار مثالیں دی ہیں [1] مرد کے لئے سلا ہوا کپڑا پہنا ممنوع ہے اس لئے اس سے بھی بچے [۲] مرد کے لئے سر ڈھانپنا اور چہرہ ڈھانپنا ممنوع ہے اس لئے اس سے بھی بچے ، اور عورت کے لے سر ڈھانپنا تو جائز ہے، لیکن چہرہ ڈھانپنا ممنوع ہے [۳] احرام کی حالت میں جماع وغیرہ ، اور فسق و فجور کی باتیں کرنا بھی ممنوع ہے اور جھگڑا کرنا بھی ممنوع ہے اس لئے اس سے بھی بچے [۴] ، شکار کو مارنا، اور اس کی طرف اشارہ کرنا، بیا اس کی طرف رہنمائی کرنا یہ بھی ممنوع ہیں اس لئے ان سے بھی بچے ۔۔ انکی دلیل بعد میں آئے گی۔ 
لغت المتطورات بظر سے مشتق ہے، احرام کی حالت میں ممنوع با تیں۔ المحیط : خاط ، مخیط سے مشتق ہے،سلا ہوا کپڑا۔ الرفث : جماع کی باتیں کرنا۔ الفسوق فسق کی باتیں۔ الجدال : جھگڑا کرنا۔ الاشارۃ الیہ : شکار کی طرف اشارہ کرنا۔
And the prohibition of prohibited acts, such as a man wearing sewn garments, covering his head and face, and a woman covering her face, and obscene speech, transgression, argumentation, killing game, pointing to it, and directing towards it. 
Translation: (1251 [c]) [22] Leaving the prohibited acts. Like a man wearing sewn clothes, and covering his head and face, and a woman covering only her face, and obscene speech, transgression, argumentation, killing game, pointing to it, or directing towards it. 
Explanation: Avoiding those things that are prohibited in Hajj is also wajib. Then he gives four examples: [1] For a man, wearing sewn clothes is prohibited, so avoid it. [2] For a man, covering the head and face is prohibited, so avoid it. For a woman, covering the head is permissible, but covering the face is prohibited. [3] In the state of ihram, sexual intercourse and the like, and acts of transgression and immorality, are prohibited, and argumentation is also prohibited, so avoid that. [4] Killing game, pointing to it, or directing towards it are also prohibited, so avoid them. Their evidence will come later. 
Lexicon: محظورات (muhazrat) is derived from hazr (prohibition), meaning things prohibited in the state of ihram. المخيط (al-makhit) is derived from khayt (thread), meaning sewn garment. الرفث (al-rafath) means talking about sexual intercourse. الفسوق (al-fusuq) means acts of transgression. الجدال (al-jidal) means argumentation. الاشارة اليه (al-isharah ilayhi) means pointing to game.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage enumerates the prohibitions (muhazrat) of ihram and states that avoiding them is wajib (obligatory). The commentator lists four categories: (1) Men wearing sewn garments is prohibited. (2) Men covering the head or face is prohibited, while women covering the head is allowed but covering the face is not (to avoid contact with the veil). (3) Obscene speech (rafath), transgression (fusuq), and argumentation (jidal) are prohibited. (4) Hunting or aiding in hunting by pointing or directing is prohibited. The lexical notes clarify the meanings of key terms: muhazrat (prohibited acts), makhit (sewn garment), rafath (sexual talk), fusuq (sin), jidal (quarrel), and isharah (pointing). The proofs for these prohibitions are promised to come later in the text.

Key Terms
المحظورات (al-muhazrat): Things prohibited during the state of ihram.
المخيط (al-makhit): Sewn garments that are tailored to the body, prohibited for men in ihram.
الرفث (al-rafath): Obscene or sexual speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Avoiding all muhazrat is wajib in ihram, covering four categories: clothing, head/face (gender-specific), verbal sins, and hunting.

Sunnahs of Hajj Before Ihram: Ghusl, Garments, and Perfume
Lists and proves the Sunnahs of Hajj with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Sunnahs of Hajj before ihram, explain their dalil, and distinguish them from wajib acts.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice establishes ghusl, white garments, and perfume as Sunnahs—not wajib—yet their omission reduces reward.

The Hajj begins with entering ihram, and the Prophet taught us specific Sunnahs to perform before that moment. This lesson examines three of those Sunnahs, their proofs, and clarifies why they are recommended rather than obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What are the Sunnahs listed? They are: (1) ghusl or wudu for ihram, (2) wearing izaar and rida', (3) applying perfume. They are classified as Sunnah mu'akkadah in the Hanafi school.
Sunnah mu'akkadah means omission reduces reward but no expiation (dam) is required.
2
Locate the dalil
For ghusl: the hadith of Ibn Abbas describing the Prophet's own ghusl before ihram and the hadith of Asma bint Umays ordering ghusl for a postpartum woman. For garments and perfume: the hadith of Ibn Abbas about the Prophet's dress and the hadith of Aisha about white shrouds.
These are all ahad hadiths with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's own action of performing ghusl, wearing izaar and rida', and applying perfume indicates desirability. The Hanafi principle: consistent practice of the Prophet indicates Sunnah mu'akkadah.
The command to Asma was for cleanliness, not ritual purity.
4
Note the scope
These Sunnahs apply to men and women, even menstruating and postpartum women. Ghusl is for cleanliness, so it is recommended for them as well.
Women may apply perfume before ihram but should avoid scented products after entering ihram.
5
Distinguish from wajib
Unlike wajib acts, omitting these Sunnahs does not require a dam (sacrifice). The omission only reduces reward. This is based on the absence of a command that indicates obligation.
Compare with the wajib acts of Hajj like staying at Arafah.

صل الله
And the Sunnahs of Hajj: (1252) Among them is ghusl even for a menstruating woman or woman in postpartum bleeding, or wudu when one intends ihram. (1253) And wearing an izaar and a rida'. [Urdu: Translation: (1252) Among the Sunnahs of Hajj is ghusl, even for a menstruating or postpartum woman; or wudu at the time of ihram. Explanation: The meaning of Sunnah is that the hadith has mentioned it as good; leaving it will decrease reward but no dam is required. The first Sunnah is to perform ghusl when entering ihram, and if unable, then wudu. This is also Sunnah for menstruating and postpartum women because the purpose is purity and cleanliness, so even though they are not ritually pure, cleanliness is achieved. Proof: (1) Hadith: Ibn Abbas said the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed ghusl, then wore his clothes, and when he reached Dhul-Hulayfah, he prayed two rakahs, then sat on his camel, and when he arrived at al-Bayda', he entered ihram for Hajj. (Darqutni, etc.) From this it is known that performing ghusl for ihram is better. (2) Another hadith: Aishah said Asma bint Umays experienced postpartum bleeding at Shajarah, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed Abu Bakr to tell her to perform ghusl and enter ihram. (Muslim) This shows that the postpartum woman should perform ghusl and enter ihram, indicating that this is for cleanliness. Translation: (1253) And wearing an izaar and a rida', both new and white. And applying perfume. Explanation: Wear a loincloth and a sheet, both preferably white, and applying perfume is also Sunnah. Proof: (1) Hadith: Abdullah ibn Abbas said the Prophet left Madinah after combing his hair, applying oil (perfume), and wearing his izaar and rida'—he and his companions—and he did not forbid any of the sheets or loincloths. (Bukhari) From this it is known to wear izaar and rida'. And 'adhan' means applying perfume. (2) Hadith: Aishah said the Prophet was shrouded in three white Yemeni cotton garments. (Bukhari) [Text cuts off]
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the Sunnahs (mustahabbat) of Hajj before ihram. It begins by listing the Sunnahs: (1) performing ghusl (full bath) when intending ihram, and if unable, then wudu (ablution) is sufficient. This is also recommended for menstruating and postpartum women, as the primary purpose is cleanliness rather than ritual purity. (2) Wearing an izaar (lower garment) and rida' (upper garment), preferably new and white, and applying perfume. The Urdu commentary explains that these acts are Sunnah—omission causes loss of reward but no penalty (dam). The proofs are provided from authentic hadith. For ghusl, the text cites Ibn Abbas's narration of the Prophet's own practice, and the hadith of Asma bint Umays where the Prophet ordered her to perform ghusl despite being in nifas. For wearing izaar and rida', the hadith of Ibn Abbas mentions the Prophet's dress, and Bukhari's narration about white shrouds supports the preference for white. The commentary also notes that oil or perfume is applied before ihram. According to the Hanafi school, these acts are Sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized Sunnah) for both men and women, and a person who omits them does not need to offer a dam.

Key Terms
السنن (al-sunan): Recommended acts that the Prophet regularly performed; omission reduces reward but does not require expiation.
الازار (al-izaar): A lower garment wrapped around the waist, covering from navel to knees, worn during ihram.
الرداء (al-rida'): An upper garment draped over the shoulders, covering the upper body, worn during ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a menstruating woman performing ghusl before ihram?
A) It is haram because she is in a state of impurity
B) It is wajib for her to perform ghusl
C) It is Sunnah for her to perform ghusl for cleanliness
D) It is makruh because it is futile

Key Takeaway
The three Sunnahs before ihram—ghusl (or wudu), wearing izaar and rida', and perfume—are emphasized but not obligatory; their omission reduces reward but does not require a dam.

Two Rak'ahs After Ihram: A Confirmed Sunnah
States the ruling and proof for two rak'ahs after assuming ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying two rak'ahs after wearing ihram and cite the hadith evidence to support the classification as sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
Praying two rak'ahs before ihram is a confirmed sunnah, not wajib — established by the Prophet's action.

This lesson examines a specific sunnah act related to Hajj: performing a two-rak'ah prayer after putting on the ihram garments but before reciting the talbiyah. The Hanafi school classifies this as a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation, based on the evidence from the Prophet's practice. Understanding this ruling helps pilgrims distinguish between necessary and recommended acts during the sacred journey.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying two rak'ahs after wearing the ihram garments, with the intention of entering the state of ihram. The ruling in the Hanafi school is 'sunnah mu'akkadah' (confirmed sunnah), as explicitly stated in the text.
The ruling is explicitly labeled as sunnah in the source.
2
Recognize the hukm level
In Hanafi fiqh, sunnah mu'akkadah is a recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed. It is not wajib because the evidence is a prophetic action (fi'l), not a command. The absence of an explicit command places it in the category of recommendation.
Compare with fard (obligatory) and wajib (necessary) which require stronger evidence.
3
Examine the evidence
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Abbas states that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs at the mosque of Dhu al-Hulayfah before making ihram for Hajj. This is a direct observation of the Prophet's practice, used as the primary evidence.
The hadith is narrated in Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Bukhari, indicating its authenticity.
4
Understand the legal reasoning
The Hanafi usul principle is that a prophetic action (fi'l) indicates recommendation (sunnah) unless there is evidence to raise it to obligation. Since no command accompanies this action, it remains sunnah.
This is a key distinction in Hanafi usul: amr (command) indicates wujub, fi'l indicates sunnah.
5
Apply in practice
A pilgrim at the miqat should, after wearing the two white cloths, pray two rak'ahs with the intention of sunnah for ihram, then recite the talbiyah. Missing it does not harm the validity of the ihram, but doing it earns reward.
The prayer is performed before the talbiyah, as the Prophet did.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۲۵۴) دورکعت پڑھنا۔
تشریح : احرام پہنے کے بعد احرام باندھنے کے لئے دورکعت پڑھنا سنت ہے۔
وجه : قلت لعبد الله ابن عباس .... خرج رسول الله الله حاجا فلما صلى في مسجد ه بذي الحليفة ركعتيه أوجب في مجلسه فأهل بالحج حين فرغ من ركعتيه ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی وقت الاحرام ص ۲۵۳ نمبر ۷۷۰ ارترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء متی احرم النبی می ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۸۱۹ / بخاری شریف ، باب الاهلال مستقبل القبلة ، ص ۲۵۲، نمبر ۱۵۵۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے احرام باندھنے کے لئے دورکعت نماز پڑھی۔
Translation: (1254) To pray two rak'ahs. Explanation: After wearing the ihram, to pray two rak'ahs for tying the ihram is sunnah. Proof: I said to Abdullah ibn Abbas... The Messenger of Allah, ﷺ, went for Hajj, and when he prayed two rak'ahs in the mosque of Dhu al-Hulayfah, he made the ihram in his place and recited the talbiyah for Hajj when he finished his two rak'ahs. (Abu Dawud, etc.) In this hadith, the Prophet ﷺ prayed two rak'ahs for tying the ihram.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This is a ruling with its proof. The author states that after one has worn the ihram garments, it is a sunnah to pray two rak'ahs with the intention of entering the state of ihram. This is established by the hadith of Ibn Abbas describing the Prophet's practice at Dhu al-Hulayfah. The Prophet prayed two rak'ahs before reciting the talbiyah for Hajj. This is the Hanafi position, and it is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah).

Key Terms
احرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, entering which certain actions become prohibited (haram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs after wearing ihram are a confirmed sunnah based on the Prophet's action, not an obligation.

Sunnan of Talbiyah After Ihram
Explains the sunnan related to reciting the talbiyah after ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six sunnan occasions for talbiyah after ihram and identify the hadith proof for each.

Core Idea
The Prophet’s practice makes these six acts sunnah mu'akkadah—meritorious but not obligatory.

After entering ihram, the pilgrim recites the talbiyah frequently. The text explains six specific occasions when it is sunnah to do so: raising the voice, after prayer, when ascending or descending a height, when meeting a rider, at dawn, and repeating often. Each occasion is supported by a hadith, confirming the practice as a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
List the six occasions
Read the passage and identify the six specific times or circumstances for reciting the talbiyah. Write them down.
The occasions: (1) raising the voice, (2) after praying, (3) when ascending, (4) when descending, (5) when meeting a rider, (6) at dawn, and also repeating often.
2
Match each occasion with its hadith
The passage cites a hadith for each occasion. Locate the hadith reference and note the key ruling phrase.
For example, the hadith of Anas ibn Malik for raising the voice, the hadith of Ibn Abbas for talbiyah after prayer, etc.
3
Determine the hukm level
The text explicitly states each act is 'sunnah'. In Hanafi fiqh, identify the precise level: sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah).
Sunnah mu'akkadah means the Prophet consistently did it and omission is disliked but not sinful.
4
Analyze the dalalah (indication) of each hadith
For each hadith, note how it indicates recommendation (not obligation). For example, the command 'raise your voices' indicates recommended, not obligatory.
Hanafi usul: a command may indicate obligation, but here the context and the Prophet's practice show it is sunnah.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
Other schools may classify some of these acts as mustahabb (preferable) or even wajib. The Hanafi position is sunnah mu'akkadah.
The Shafi'i school generally agrees; the Maliki school may consider some as mustahabb.

Translation: (1255) To increase the talbiyah after ihram. To raise the voice in talbiyah when he prays, or when he ascends a height, or descends into a valley, or meets a rider, and at dawn. And whenever he recites the talbiyah, he should repeat it often. Explanation: After tying the ihram, reciting the talbiyah abundantly is sunnah. Then he should raise his voice, recite when climbing a hill, descending, meeting a rider, and repeat it often. All these are sunnan. (1) Hadith for raising voice and reciting after prayer: Anas ibn Malik said: The Prophet prayed Zuhr and Asr in Medina and at Dhu al-Hulayfah two rak'ahs, and I heard them reciting loudly with both. (Bukhari) This hadith indicates raising the voice. (2) Another hadith: From Khallad ibn al-Sa'ib... that Jibril came and ordered me to command my companions to raise their voices with talbiyah. (Abu Dawud) (3) Hadith for talbiyah after prayer: ...the Prophet recited talbiyah after finishing his two rak'ahs. (4) Hadith for meeting riders: From Abdullah ibn Umar: when the Prophet's camel stood up at the mosque of Dhu al-Hulayfah, he recited talbiyah. (Muslim, Bukhari) (5) Hadith for repetition: From Ibn Abbas: Usama was riding behind the Prophet from Arafah to Muzdalifah, then al-Fadl from Muzdalifah to Mina, and both said he continued reciting talbiyah until he stoned the Jamrat al-Aqabah. (Bukhari) (6) Hadith for descending into valley: Ibn Abbas said: Moses recites talbiyah when descending into the valley. (Bukhari) Glossary: al-tayyib = applying perfume. 'ala sharafa = ascending a height. habata = descending. takrir = repetition.

Commentary
This passage details the sunnan (recommended acts) related to reciting the talbiyah after entering ihram. The author lists six specific occasions: raising the voice, reciting after prayer, when ascending or descending, when meeting riders, at dawn, and repeating frequently. Each is supported by a hadith. The Hanafi madhhab considers these acts as sunnah, meaning they are meritorious but not obligatory. The glossary at the end clarifies key terms from the preceding discussion.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The recitation of 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' which is a declaration of response to Allah's call for Hajj.
سنن (sunan): Plural of sunnah, meaning recommended acts that the Prophet consistently performed but did not obligate.

Sending Salawat and Supplications After Ihram
States the ruling and proof for reciting salawat, asking for Jannah, and seeking refuge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three recommended supplications after talbiyah and identify the textual evidence for each from the reported hadiths.

Core Idea
Three sunnan follow talbiyah: salawat, asking Jannah, seeking refuge—all proven by the Prophet's practice and command.

After entering ihram and reciting the talbiyah, the pilgrim is encouraged to engage in specific supplications that the Prophet ﷺ himself practiced. These include sending blessings upon him, asking for Paradise and righteous company, and seeking refuge from the Fire. In this lesson, we examine the textual evidence for these recommended acts and understand their place in the Hajj rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three recommended acts
From the lesson title and first line, list: (1) sending salawat upon the Prophet ﷺ, (2) asking for Jannah and the company of the righteous, (3) seeking refuge from the Fire.
2
Locate the first dalil (salawat)
Find the hadith of Ibn Abbas: when opposite the Black Stone, say takbir, supplicate, and send salawat. This is generalized to after talbiyah because salawat is recommended before any du'a.
Reference: Sunan al-Bayhaqi (9266)
3
Trace the second dalil (salawat before du'a)
The hadith of Fadala ibn Ubayd: the Prophet instructed a man to begin du'a with praise of Allah and then send salawat before supplicating. This establishes the principle of preceding du'a with salawat.
Reference: Tirmidhi (7347)
4
Examine the third dalil (asking Jannah and seeking refuge)
The hadith of Khuzayma ibn Thabit describes the Prophet's practice after talbiyah: he would ask for Allah's pleasure and forgiveness and seek refuge from the Fire. This directly shows the specific du'as.
Reference: Sunan al-Bayhaqi (9038)
5
Synthesize the ruling
Combine the proofs: salawat is proven by specific command and general principle; the du'as are proven by the Prophet's practice. All are sunnah mu'akkadah, not obligatory. Missing them does not invalidate Hajj but loses reward.
Hanafi ruling: sunnah mu'akkadah

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۵۶) اور بنی پاک صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود پڑھنا۔ اور جنت ، ونیکوں کی صحبت کا سوال کرنا۔ اور جہنم سے پناہ مانگنا۔ وجه : (۱) درود شریف پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال اذا حاذیت به فکبر و ادع و صل على محمد النبي علیه السلام (سنن بیہقی ، باب الاستلام في الزحام، ج خامس ،ص ۱۳۱، نمبر ۹۲۶۶) (۲) چونکہ یہاں دعا کرنی ہے اس لئے اس سے پہلے درود شریف پڑھے، اس کے لئے حدیث یہ ہے۔ سمع فضالة ابن عبيد يقول سمع النبي الله رجلا يدعو في صلاته فلم يصل على النبي الله فقال النبي اللهم عجل هذا ، ثم دعاه فقال له او لغيره ، اذا صلی احدكم فليبدأ بتحميدالله و الثناء عليه ثم ليصل على النبي عل الله ثم ليدع بعد ما شاء ( ترندی شریف، باب فی ایجاب الدعاء بتقديم الحمد والثناء والصلاۃ علی النبی عه قبلہ، ص ۷۹۴، نمبر ۷ ۳۴۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ دعا سے پہلے درود شریف پڑھے۔ (۳) دعا کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن خزيمة بن ثابت ان النبي الله كان اذا فرغ من تلبيته سأل الله رضوانه و مغفرته و استعاذ برحمته من النار ( سنن بیہقی ، باب ما يستحب من القول في اثر التلبية ، ج خامس ،ص ۷۲ ، نمبر ۹۰۳۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جنت کا سوال کرے اور جہنم سے پناہ مانگے ۔
Translation: (1256) And to send salawat upon the Prophet, ﷺ. And to ask for Jannah and the companionship of the righteous. And to seek refuge from the Fire. Proof: (1) Hadith for sending salawat: From Ibn Abbas: When you come opposite it [the Black Stone?], say takbir and supplicate, and send salawat upon Muhammad, the Prophet. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) (2) Since one should make du'a here, before it he should send salawat. Hadith: Fadala ibn Ubayd heard the Prophet ﷺ say when a man prayed without sending salawat: 'This man is hasty.' Then he called him and said: 'When one of you prays, let him begin with praise of Allah and then send salawat upon the Prophet, then supplicate as he wishes.' (Tirmidhi) This hadith indicates to send salawat before du'a. (3) Du'a: Hadith of Khuzayma ibn Thabit: The Prophet ﷺ, after finishing his talbiyah, would ask Allah for His pleasure and forgiveness and seek refuge by His mercy from the Fire. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) This hadith indicates to ask for Jannah and seek refuge from Jahannam.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This lesson covers three sunnan after entering ihram: sending salawat (blessings) upon the Prophet ﷺ, asking for Paradise and righteous company, and seeking refuge from Hell. The author provides proof for each: the first from a hadith of Ibn Abbas (though contextually about the Black Stone, it is generalized), the second from the well-known principle that du'a should be preceded by praise and salawat, and the third from a specific hadith about the Prophet's practice after talbiyah. These are all considered sunnah; they are not obligatory but highly recommended.

Key Terms
درود (salawat / durood): Sending blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ, typically 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad' or similar phrases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the talbiyah
B) Salawat, then ask for Jannah and seek refuge
C) Takbir and tahmid
D) Recite Quran

Key Takeaway
The Prophet ﷺ would ask for Jannah and seek refuge after talbiyah, and it is sunnah to preface this with salawat.

Sunan of Talbiyah and Salawat in Hajj
Lists recommended acts with prophetic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific sunan associated with talbiyah and the post-talbiyah supplications, and identify the prophetic evidence (dalil) for each.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice establishes six sunan for talbiyah and three after it; omitting them does not invalidate Hajj but loses reward.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah outlines the sunan (recommended acts) associated with the talbiyah during Hajj. The author lists specific moments to recite the talbiyah and then additional supplications after it, each supported by authentic ahadith. Understanding these sunan helps the pilgrim follow the Prophet's way and gain maximum reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
List the six situations for reciting talbiyah and the three recommended acts after talbiyah as mentioned in the passage.
The six situations: raising voice, ascending a high place, descending a valley, meeting a rider, at dawn, and repeating it. After talbiyah: sending salawat, asking for Paradise, and seeking refuge from Hell.
2
Match each sunnah to its hadith evidence
For each sunnah, locate the specific hadith cited by the author. Note that the hadith are from Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi, and Bayhaqi.
Example: The sunnah of reciting talbiyah when mounting is proven by the hadith of Ibn Umar.
3
Analyze the legal implication (wajh al-dalalah)
Explain how the Prophet's action (e.g., reciting talbiyah at a certain time) indicates sunnah (recommendation) rather than obligation in the Hanafi school.
The Hanafi principle: The Prophet's consistent practice (without a command of obligation) indicates sunnah muakkadah.
4
Distinguish sunnah from wajib
Understand that these acts are sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib. Omitting them does not invalidate Hajj, but following them brings reward.
In Hanafi, talbiyah itself is wajib, but these are sunan. Missing a sunnah does not require compensation (sajdah sahw or dam).

The Hajj Sunan. His voice when he prays or when he ascends a high place or descends a valley or meets a rider, and at dawn, and its repetition whenever he starts it. (4) At the time of meeting a rider he should recite a hadith. For this there is this hadith: From Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) when his mount stood up straight at the mosque of Dhu'l-Hulayfah, he said the talbiyah and said 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...' (Muslim, etc.) In this hadith, the Prophet recited talbiyah after mounting the ride. (5) He should repeat it. For this there is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas that Usama was riding behind the Messenger of Allah (SAW) from Arafat to Muzdalifah, then Fadl rode behind from Muzdalifah to Mina. He said: both of them said that the Prophet (SAW) kept reciting talbiyah until he stoned the Jamrat al-Aqabah. (Bukhari, etc.) In this hadith, he should repeat talbiyah repeatedly. (6) When descending or ascending a valley he should recite talbiyah. For this there is this hadith: Ibn Abbas said, I did not hear him but he said: Moses – it is as if I see him – when he descended in the valley he said talbiyah. (Bukhari, etc.) In this hadith, he should recite talbiyah when descending a valley. Vocabulary: 'al-tayyab' means applying perfume. 'Ula sharafa': sharaf means high, 'ula sharafa' means ascending a high place. 'Habat' means descended. 'Takrir' means repeating again and again. (1256) And sending prayers upon the Prophet (SAW) and asking for Paradise and the company of the righteous and seeking refuge from the Fire. Translation: (1256) And reciting salawat upon the Prophet (SAW). And asking for Paradise and the company of the righteous. And seeking refuge from Hell. Evidence: (1) He should recite salawat. For this there is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas: When you come opposite it, say takbir and supplicate and send prayers upon Muhammad the Prophet (SAW) (Sunan Bayhaqi). (2) Since supplication is to be made here, one should recite salawat before it. For this there is this hadith: Fadala ibn Ubayd heard the Prophet (SAW) say to a man who prayed without salawat: 'This one hurried.' Then he called him and said to him or to another: 'When one of you prays, let him begin with praise of Allah and then send prayers upon the Prophet (SAW) and then supplicate as he wishes.' (Tirmidhi) In this hadith, he should recite salawat before du'a. (3) He should supplicate. For this there is this hadith: From Khuzayma ibn Thabit that the Prophet (SAW) when he finished his talbiyah, asked Allah for His pleasure and forgiveness and sought refuge by His mercy from the Fire. (Sunan Bayhaqi) In this hadith, he should ask for Paradise and seek refuge from Hell.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage enumerates the sunan (recommended acts) associated with the talbiyah during Hajj. The first part lists six situations for reciting the talbiyah: raising the voice, when ascending a high place, descending a valley, meeting a rider, at dawn, and repeating it whenever one begins. The author then provides supporting ahadith from Bukhari, Muslim, and others for each. The second part (number 1256) adds that after the talbiyah, one should send salawat upon the Prophet (SAW), ask for Paradise and the company of the righteous, and seek refuge from Hell. Ahadith from Bayhaqi and Tirmidhi support these acts, emphasizing the etiquette of beginning du'a with praise and salawat. In the Hanafi school, these are all mustahabb; the talbiyah itself is wajib.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...' recited by the pilgrim during Hajj.
سنن (sunan): Recommended acts based on the Prophet's practice, not obligatory.
درود (salawat): Sending blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad (SAW).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Send salawat and supplicate for Paradise and refuge from Hell
C) Recite the talbiyah again
D) Make a sacrifice

Key Takeaway
The sunan of talbiyah and post-talbiyah are recommended acts rooted in the Prophet's practice; following them enhances the Hajj without affecting its validity.

Sunnah Acts for Entering Makkah: Ghusl, Entry from Upper Gate, and Daytime Entry
States the sunnah of ghusl before entering Makkah and entering from the upper gate by day.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state three sunnah acts for entering Makkah and identify the evidence for each from the ahadith cited.

Core Idea
Ghusl before entering Makkah is sunnah; wudu suffices if ghusl is not possible; entry from the upper gate by day follows prophetic practice.

This lesson covers the recommended acts when entering Makkah for Hajj or Umrah. The source text presents several ahadith from Ibn Umar and Aisha showing that the Prophet (SAW) performed ghusl, entered from the upper pass, and entered during the day. Understanding these sunnah acts helps the pilgrim prepare respectfully for the sacred city.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
The passage states that ghusl before entering Makkah is a sunnah. What is the specific hukm level? (sunnah muakkadah). Note the minimum alternative if ghusl is not possible.
The text says 'and the minimum is to perform wudu'.
2
Locate the proofs for ghusl
List the ahadith that support performing ghusl: the hadith of Ibn Umar about the Prophet (SAW) at Dhi Tuwa and the hadith at Fakh. Identify the narrators and sources (Bukhari, Tirmidhi).
These are ahadith (single) but considered reliable.
3
Identify the minimum requirement
If ghusl is not possible, the sunnah is to perform wudu. Which hadith supports this? (Aisha's hadith about the Prophet (SAW) performing wudu before tawaf). Why is this applicable to entering Makkah?
The hadith indicates wudu is the minimum purification before entering the House.
4
Determine the sunnah for entry point and time
Find the evidence for entering Makkah from the upper pass (Bab al-Mu'alla) and during the day. Which hadith is cited? (Ibn Umar: the Prophet entered from the upper pass and exited from the lower pass; he spent the night at Dhi Tuwa until dawn then entered).
These are separate sunnah acts, each with explicit prophetic practice.
5
Evaluate the practical application
How should a pilgrim apply these today? The mufta bihi is that ghusl is recommended but if not possible, wudu suffices. Entering from the upper gate and by day are sunnah, though not obligatory.
The Hanafi position is based on these ahadith; missing these does not invalidate the Hajj or Umrah.

(1257) And ghusl for entering Makkah, and entering it from the Bab al-Mu'alla during the day. Translation: (1257) Performing ghusl for entering Makkah. (Bukhari, Muslim) In this hadith, he should perform wudu. (4) There are two routes to the House of Allah: one from above and the other from below. So one should come from above, that is sunnah, because the Prophet (SAW) came that way. From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah used to enter Makkah from the upper pass and exit from the lower pass. (Bukhari, Nasa'i) (5) And he entered during the day. The hadith for this is: From Ibn Umar: The Prophet (SAW) spent the night at Dhi Tuwa until morning, then entered Makkah, and Ibn Umar used to do that. (Bukhari)

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah of ghusl (full ablution) before entering Makkah for Hajj or Umrah. The author provides ahadith showing that the Prophet (SAW) and the Companions performed ghusl at Dhi Tuwa or Fakh. If ghusl is not possible, performing wudu is the minimum requirement. Additionally, the sunnah is to enter Makkah from the upper pass (Bab al-Mu'alla) and during the daytime, following the Prophet's example. These acts are mustahabb, emphasizing the preparation and respect for the sacred city.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Full ritual washing of the body with water.
باب المعلاة (Bab al-Mu'alla): One of the gates of the Masjid al-Haram, associated with the upper path to Makkah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Wudu
C) No alternative
D) Reciting takbir

Key Takeaway
Performing ghusl before entering Makkah is a confirmed sunnah; if not possible, wudu suffices, and it is sunnah to enter from the upper gate during the day.

Takbir and Du'a Upon Seeing the Kaaba
Ruling on recommended acts upon sighting the Kaaba with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts upon seeing the Kaaba and identify the supporting proofs.

Core Idea
Upon seeing the Kaaba, sunnah is to say takbir, tahleel, and du'a; du'a at this moment is answered.

When a pilgrim first catches sight of the Kaaba, the heart stirs with awe. The Hanafi tradition teaches specific remembrances and supplications at that blessed moment. In this lesson, we will learn what the Prophet ﷺ did upon seeing the House, and why this moment is so special for du'a.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
List the three actions taught in the passage: saying takbir (Allahu Akbar), tahleel (La ilaha illallah), and making du'a.
2
Review the proof from hadith
Examine the ahadith cited: the mursal narration of Makhul, the instruction to Umar, and the du'a of the Prophet.
These ahadith establish the practice as sunnah.
3
Understand the virtue of du'a at this moment
Note that the text states du'a upon seeing the Kaaba is answered, so one should ask for good, especially for the Hereafter.
4
Apply the ruling
Describe what a pilgrim should do when first seeing the Kaaba: raise hands, say takbir and tahleel, then make du'a.

(۱۲۵۸) والتكبير والتهليل عند رؤية البيت، والدعاء بما شاء لأن الدعاء عند رؤية البيت مستجاب.
ترجمه : (۱۲۵۸) بیت اللہ نظر آئے تو تکبیر، ولا الہ الا اللہ پڑھنا۔ بیت اللہ کو دیکھتے ہی محبوب چیز کی دعا مانگنا کہ اس وقت دعا قبول ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح : بیت اللہ نظر آئے تو اللہ اکبر کہے, لا اله الا الله ، پڑھے، اور جو چیز اس کو پسند آئے اس کی دعا کرے، بہتر یہ ہے کہ آخرت کے لئے دعا کرے، کیونکہ اس وقت دعا قبول ہوتی ہے۔
وجه : (1) تکبیر کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن مكحول قال كان النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا دخل مكة فرأى البيت رفع يديه و كبر ـ ( سنن للبیھقی ، باب القول عند رویتہ البیت ج خامس ص ۱۱۸ نمبر ۹۲۱۳) اس حدیث مرسل میں ہے کہ بیت اللہ دیکھتے وقت تکبیر کہے (۲) ـ عـن عـمـر بـن الـخـطـاب ان النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم قال له : يا عمر انک رجل قوی ، لاتزاحم علی الـحـجـر فتؤذي الضعيف ، ان وجدت خلوة فاستلمه و الا فاستقبله فهلل و كبر . (مسند احمد، باب مسند عمر بن الخطاب، ج اول ص ۴۸، نمبر (۱۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حجر اسود کے چومتے وقت چومنے کا موقع نہ ملے تو تکبیر و تہلیل کہیں۔(۳) اس حدیث میں بھی دعاء کا ذکر ہے۔ عن ابن جریح ان النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم كان اذا راى البيت رفع يديه وقال اللهم زد هذا البيت تشريفا و تعظيما الخ ( سن لیتی ، باب القول عند رویۃ البیت ، ج خامس ص ۱۸، نمبر ۹۲۱۳ ترمندی شریف ، باب
(1258) And takbir and tahleel upon seeing the House, and supplication for whatever one wishes, because supplication at the sight of the House is answered. Translation: (1258) When the House of Allah is sighted, say takbir, 'La ilaha illallah'. Upon seeing the House of Allah, make du'a for a beloved thing, for at that time du'a is accepted. Explanation: When the House of Allah is seen, one should say 'Allahu Akbar', 'La ilaha illallah', and make du'a for whatever he likes. It is better to make du'a for the Hereafter, because at that time du'a is accepted. Evidence: (1) For takbir, this hadith: From Makhul: When the Prophet (SAW) entered Makkah and saw the House, he raised his hands and said takbir. (Sunan Bayhaqi) This mursal hadith states to say takbir when seeing the House. (2) From Umar ibn al-Khattab: The Prophet (SAW) said to him: 'O Umar, you are a strong man, do not crowd at the Black Stone and harm the weak. If you find a free space, touch it, otherwise face it and say tahleel and takbir.' (Musnad Ahmad) This hadith indicates to say takbir and tahleel when unable to kiss the Black Stone. (3) Also, du'a is mentioned: From Ibn Jurayj: When the Prophet (SAW) saw the House, he raised his hands and said, 'O Allah, increase this House in honor and veneration...' (Sunan Bayhaqi, Tirmidhi)
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage teaches the recommended acts upon first seeing the Kaaba: saying takbir (Allahu Akbar), tahleel (La ilaha illallah), and making du'a. The author notes that du'a at this moment is especially accepted, so one should ask for good in this world and the Hereafter, preferably for the Hereafter. Ahadith support raising hands for takbir and making specific supplications. In the Hanafi school, these are mustahabb acts that enhance the spiritual experience of Hajj.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' (Allah is the Greatest).
تهلیل (tahleel): Saying 'La ilaha illallah' (There is no god but Allah).
دعاء (du'a): Supplication or invocation to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the preferred type of du'a to make upon seeing the Kaaba?
A) Du'a for worldly wealth
B) Du'a for the Hereafter
C) Du'a for health
D) No preference

Key Takeaway
Upon seeing the Kaaba, the sunnah is to recite takbir and tahleel and then make du'a, especially for the Hereafter.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Takbir and Dua Upon Seeing the Kaaba: A Sunnah Moment of Acceptance
Ruling and proofs for takbir and dua upon seeing the Kaaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts upon seeing the Kaaba, identify the relevant hadith proofs, and explain why this moment is particularly virtuous for supplication.

Core Idea
Seeing the Kaaba is a moment of acceptance; recite takbir, tahlil, and make dua.

When the pilgrim first beholds the Kaaba, the heart is overwhelmed. The Hanafi school teaches that this is not only a moment of awe but a prescribed opportunity for worship. Based on the Prophet's practice, one should recite takbir (Allahu Akbar) and tahlil (La ilaha illallah), then raise the hands in supplication. This lesson examines the textual proofs and explains why the Hanafis consider these acts a sunnah mu'akkadah – a highly recommended practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
The passage states three acts: recite takbir, recite tahlil, and make supplication. The ruling for each is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah).
The author also notes it is better to supplicate for the Hereafter because the moment is one when dua is answered.
2
Locate the proof for takbir
The first hadith cited is a mursal hadith from Makhul: the Prophet raised his hands and said takbir upon seeing the Kaaba. A mursal hadith is acceptable as a proof for recommended acts in the Hanafi school.
The hadith text: 'عن مكحول قال كان النبى الله اذا دخل مكة فرأى البيت رفع يديه و كبر'
3
Locate the proof for tahlil
The second hadith, from Umar ibn al-Khattab, instructs to face the Black Stone and say tahlil and takbir when unable to kiss it. This is extended to the general moment of seeing the Kaaba.
Hadith from Musnad Ahmad: 'فاستقبله فهلل و كبر'
4
Examine the supplication evidence
Two hadiths show the Prophet raising hands and making dua upon seeing the Kaaba – one from Ibn Jurayj (with wording: 'اللهم زد هذا البيت تشريفا') and another from Abd al-Rahman ibn Tariq (facing qibla and supplicating).
The hadith about the 'dislike of raising hands' is mentioned but the stronger evidence supports raising hands as sunnah.
5
Understand the virtue and the Hanafi position
The author emphasizes that at this moment dua is accepted. The Hanafi school holds these acts as mu'akkadah sunnah based on multiple authentic reports. The mufta bihi is to perform all three.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the position is consistent across the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۲۵۸) بیت اللہ نظر آئے تو تکبیر، ولا الہ الا اللہ پڑھنا۔ بیت اللہ کو دیکھتے ہی محبوب چیز کی دعا مانگنا کہ اس وقت دعا قبول ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح : بیت اللہ نظر آئے تو اللہ اکبر کہے, لا اله الا الله ، پڑھے، اور جو چیز اس کو پسند آئے اس کی دعا کرے، بہتر یہ ہے کہ آخرت کے لئے دعا کرے، کیونکہ اس وقت دعا قبول ہوتی ہے۔ وجه : (۱) تکبیر کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن مكحول قال كان النبى الله اذا دخل مكة فرأى البيت رفع يديه و كبر ـ ( سنن للبیھقی ، باب القول عند رویتہ البیت ج خامس ص ۱۱۸ نمبر ۹۲۱۳) اس حدیث مرسل میں ہے کہ بیت اللہ دیکھتے وقت تکبیر کہے (۲) ـ عـن عـمـر بـن الـخـطـاب ان النبى الله قال له : يا عمر انک رجل قوی ، لاتزاحم علی الـحـجـر فتؤذي الضعيف ، ان وجدت خلوة فاستلمه و الا فاستقبله فهلل و کبر . (مسند احمد، باب مسند عمر بن الخطاب، ج اول ص ۴۸، نمبر (۱۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حجر اسود کے چومتے وقت چومنے کا موقع نہ ملے تو تکبیر و تہلیل کہیں۔(۳) اس حدیث میں بھی دعاء کا ذکر ہے۔ عن ابن جریح ان النبى الله الله كان اذا راى البيت رفع يديه وقال اللهم زد هذا البيت تشريفا و تعظيما الخ ( سن لیتی ، باب القول عند رویۃ البیت ، ج خامس ص ۱۸، نمبر ۹۲۱۳ ترمندی شریف ، باب ما جاء کراہیتہ رفع الید عند رویۃ البیت ص ۷۴ انمبر ۸۵۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیت اللہ دیکھتے وقت ہاتھ اٹھانا چاہئے ، اور دعا پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ان عبد الرحمن بن طارق ابن علقمة اخبره عن امه ان النبى الله كان اذ جاء مكانا في دار يعلى استقبل القبلة ودعا ۔ (نسائی شریف ، باب الدعا عند رویۃ البیت ،ص ۱۳۹۹، نمبر (۲۸۹۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بیت اللہ دیکھتے وقت دعا کرے۔
Translation: (1258) When the House of Allah is sighted, recite takbir and la ilaha illallah. At the sight of the House of Allah, supplicate for a beloved matter, for at that time supplication is accepted. Explanation: When one sights the House of Allah, he should say Allahu Akbar, recite La ilaha illallah, and supplicate for whatever he likes. It is better to supplicate for the Hereafter, because at that time supplication is accepted. Evidence: (1) For takbir, this hadith: From Makhul, he said: The Prophet, peace be upon him, when he entered Mecca and saw the House, he raised his hands and said takbir. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Qawl 'Inda Ru'yat al-Bayt, vol. 5, p. 118, no. 9213) This mursal hadith indicates that when seeing the House of Allah, one should say takbir. (2) From Umar ibn al-Khattab that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to him: O Umar, you are a strong man. Do not crowd at the Black Stone and thus harm the weak. If you find an open space, then touch it; otherwise, face it and say tahlil and takbir. (Musnad Ahmad, Bab Musnad Umar ibn al-Khattab, vol. 1, p. 48, no. 19) This hadith indicates that when kissing the Black Stone, if one does not get the chance to kiss it, he should say takbir and tahlil. (3) This hadith also mentions supplication: From Ibn Jurayj that the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he saw the House, raised his hands and said: O Allah, increase this House in honor and veneration, etc. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Qawl 'Inda Ru'yat al-Bayt, vol. 5, p. 118, no. 9213; Tirmidhi, Bab Ma Ja'a fi Karahiyat Raf' al-Yad 'Inda Ru'yat al-Bayt, p. 74, no. 855) From this hadith it is learned that when seeing the House of Allah, one should raise his hands and supplicate. And from Abd al-Rahman ibn Tariq ibn Alqamah, who was informed by his mother, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he came to a place in the house of Ya'la, he faced the qibla and supplicated. (Nasa'i, Bab al-Du'a 'Inda Ru'yat al-Bayt, p. 1399, no. 2899) This hadith indicates that one should supplicate when seeing the House of Allah.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It covers the sunnah acts when first seeing the Kaaba: reciting takbir (Allahu Akbar) and tahlil (La ilaha illallah), and making supplication. The author explains that the time of seeing the Kaaba is a moment when dua is answered, so one should ask for what he desires, preferably for the Hereafter. The evidence includes several hadith: a mursal hadith from Makhul about raising hands and saying takbir; a hadith from Umar about tahlil and takbir at the Black Stone; and a hadith from Ibn Jurayj about raising hands and supplicating. The author also cites a hadith from Nasa'i about facing the qibla and making dua. Note: The text mentions a hadith about the dislike (karahiyya) of raising hands, but the author clarifies that from the hadith it is learned that raising hands is recommended. All the proofs support the sunnah nature of these actions.

Key Terms
تكبير (takbīr): Saying 'Allāhu Akbar' (Allah is the Greatest).
تهليل (tahlīl): Saying 'Lā ilāha illallāh' (There is no god but Allah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Upon seeing the Kaaba, what two actions are sunnah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Raml and Idtiba'
B) Takbir and dua
C) Tawaf and sa'y
D) Kissing the Black Stone and making dua

Key Takeaway
Upon first seeing the Kaaba, it is sunnah to recite takbir and tahlil, raise your hands, and make dua, for this is a moment when supplication is accepted.
